000604r 3                               ; Copy the characters from the input buffer to the
000604r 3                               ; history buffer.
000604r 3               
000604r 3               @save_history_loop:
000604r 3  C4 rr                        cpy status+1
000606r 3  F0 07                        beq @save_history_done
000608r 3               
000608r 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp1),y
00060Ar 3  91 rr                        sta (tmp3),y
00060Cr 3  C8                           iny
00060Dr 3  80 F5                        bra @save_history_loop
00060Fr 3               
00060Fr 3               @save_history_done:
00060Fr 3               z_accept:
00060Fr 3  60                           rts
000610r 3               
000610r 3               total_recall:
000610r 3                       ; """Internal subroutine for ACCEPT that recalls history entry"""
000610r 3               
000610r 3                               ; Generate the address of the buffer in tmp3. Start with the
000610r 3                               ; base address.
000610r 3  A9 rr                        lda #<hist_buff
000612r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp3
000614r 3  A9 rr                        lda #>hist_buff
000616r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp3+1
000618r 3               
000618r 3                               ; This is a bit annoying as some bits go into each byte.
000618r 3                               ; .....xxx gets put into address like ......xx x.......
000618r 3  A5 rr                        lda status
00061Ar 3  6A                           ror
00061Br 3  29 03                        and #3
00061Dr 3  18                           clc
00061Er 3  65 rr                        adc tmp3+1
000620r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp3+1
000622r 3               
000622r 3  A5 rr                        lda status
000624r 3  6A                           ror             ; Rotate through carry into msb.
000625r 3  6A                           ror
000626r 3  29 80                        and #$80
000628r 3  18                           clc
000629r 3  65 rr                        adc tmp3
00062Br 3  85 rr                        sta tmp3
00062Dr 3  90 02                        bcc @1           ; Increment the upper byte on carry.
00062Fr 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp3+1
000631r 3               @1:
000631r 3                               ; Save the current length of the input buffer in
000631r 3                               ; histinfo+1 temporarily.  Reduce to 127 if larger.
000631r 3  98                           tya
000632r 3  C9 80                        cmp #$80
000634r 3  90 02                        bcc @2
000636r 3  A9 7F                        lda #$7F
000638r 3               @2:
000638r 3  60                           rts
000639r 3               
000639r 3               
000639r 3               
000639r 3               
000639r 3               
000639r 3               ; ## ACTION_OF ( "name" -- xt ) "Get named deferred word's xt"
000639r 3               ; ## "action-of"  auto  ANS core ext
000639r 3                       ; """http://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ACTION-OF"""
000639r 3               
000639r 3               xt_action_of:
000639r 3                               ; This is a state aware word with differet behavior
000639r 3                               ; when used while compiling vs interpreting.
000639r 3                               ; Check STATE
000639r 3  A5 rr                        lda state
00063Br 3  05 rr                        ora state+1
00063Dr 3  F0 0C                        beq @interpreting
00063Fr 3               
00063Fr 3               @compiling:
00063Fr 3                               ; Run ['] to compile the xt of the next word
00063Fr 3                               ; as a literal.
00063Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_bracket_tick
000642r 3               
000642r 3                               ; Postpone DEFER@ by compiling a JSR to it.
000642r 3  A0 rr                        ldy #>xt_defer_fetch
000644r 3  A9 rr                        lda #<xt_defer_fetch
000646r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr cmpl_subroutine
000649r 3  80 06                        bra @done
00064Br 3               
00064Br 3               @interpreting:
00064Br 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_tick
00064Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_defer_fetch
000651r 3               
000651r 3               @done:
000651r 3  60           z_action_of:           rts
000652r 3               
000652r 3               
000652r 3               
000652r 3               ; ## AGAIN ( addr -- ) "Code backwards branch to address left by BEGIN"
000652r 3               ; ## "again"  tested  ANS core ext
000652r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/AGAIN"""
000652r 3               
000652r 3               xt_again:
000652r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
000655r 3               
000655r 3                               ; Add the opcode for a JMP. We use JMP instead of BRA
000655r 3                               ; so we have the range and don't have to calculate the
000655r 3                               ; offset.
000655r 3  A0 00                        ldy #0
000657r 3  A9 4C                        lda #$4C        ; JMP
000659r 3  91 rr                        sta (cp),y
00065Br 3  C8                           iny
00065Cr 3               
00065Cr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x         ; LSB of address
00065Er 3  91 rr                        sta (cp),y
000660r 3  C8                           iny
000661r 3               
000661r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x         ; MSB of address
000663r 3  91 rr                        sta (cp),y
000665r 3  C8                           iny
000666r 3               
000666r 3                               ; Allot the space we just used
000666r 3  98                           tya
000667r 3  18                           clc
000668r 3  65 rr                        adc cp
00066Ar 3  85 rr                        sta cp
00066Cr 3  90 02                        bcc @done
00066Er 3  E6 rr                        inc cp+1
000670r 3               @done:
000670r 3  E8                           inx
000671r 3  E8                           inx
000672r 3               
000672r 3  60           z_again:        rts
000673r 3               
000673r 3               
000673r 3               
000673r 3               ; ## ALIGN ( -- ) "Make sure CP is aligned on word size"
000673r 3               ; ## "align"  auto  ANS core
000673r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ALIGN
000673r 3                       ; On a 8-bit machine, this does nothing. ALIGNED uses this
000673r 3                       ; routine as well, and also does nothing
000673r 3                       ; """
000673r 3               
000673r 3               ; ## ALIGNED ( addr -- addr ) "Return the first aligned address"
000673r 3               ; ## "aligned"  auto  ANS core
000673r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ALIGNED"""
000673r 3               
000673r 3               xt_align:
000673r 3               xt_aligned:
000673r 3               z_align:
000673r 3  60           z_aligned:      rts             ; stripped out during native compile
000674r 3               
000674r 3               
000674r 3               
000674r 3               ; ## ALLOT ( n -- ) "Reserve or release memory"
000674r 3               ; ## "allot"  auto  ANS core
000674r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ALLOT
000674r 3                       ; Reserve a certain number of bytes (not cells) or release them.
000674r 3                       ; If n = 0, do nothing. If n is negative, release n bytes, but only
000674r 3                       ; to the beginning of the Dictionary. If n is positive (the most
000674r 3                       ; common case), reserve n bytes, but not past the end of the
000674r 3                       ; Dictionary. See http://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ALLOT
000674r 3                       ; """
000674r 3               
000674r 3               xt_allot:
000674r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
000677r 3               
000677r 3                               ; Releasing memory is going to be a very rare operation,
000677r 3                               ; so we check for it at the beginning and try to make
000677r 3                               ; the most common case as fast as possible
000677r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
000679r 3  30 22                        bmi @release
00067Br 3               
00067Br 3                               ; Common case: We are reserving memory, not releasing it
00067Br 3  18                           clc
00067Cr 3  A5 rr                        lda cp
00067Er 3  75 00                        adc 0,x
000680r 3  85 rr                        sta cp
000682r 3               
000682r 3  A5 rr                        lda cp+1
000684r 3  75 01                        adc 1,x
000686r 3  85 rr                        sta cp+1
000688r 3               
000688r 3                               ; Wait, did we just grant more space than we have? This is
000688r 3                               ; a check we only do here, not for other situations like cmpl_a
000688r 3                               ; where smaller amounts are reserved.
000688r 3  A0 FF                        ldy #<cp_end
00068Ar 3  C4 rr                        cpy cp
00068Cr 3  A9 7F                        lda #>cp_end
00068Er 3  E5 rr                        sbc cp+1
000690r 3  B0 48                        bcs @done               ; we're fine.
000692r 3               
000692r 3                               ; Oops, that was too much, we're beyond the end of
000692r 3                               ; legal Dictionary RAM. Reduce to max memory and report
000692r 3                               ; an error
000692r 3  84 rr                        sty cp                  ; still #<cp_end
000694r 3  A9 7F                        lda #>cp_end
000696r 3  85 rr                        sta cp+1
000698r 3               
000698r 3  A9 00                        lda #err_allot
00069Ar 3  4C rr rr                     jmp error
00069Dr 3               
00069Dr 3               @release:
00069Dr 3                  		; The ANS standard doesn't really say what to do if too much
00069Dr 3                               ; memory is freed ("negatively alloted"). In fact, there isn't
00069Dr 3                               ; even an official test. Gforth is little help either. The good
00069Dr 3                               ; news is, this is going to be a rare case. We want to use as
00069Dr 3                               ; few bytes as possible.
00069Dr 3               
00069Dr 3                               ; What we do is let the user free anything up to the beginning
00069Dr 3                               ; of the RAM area assigned to the Dicionary (CP0), but at
00069Dr 3                               ; their own risk. This means that the Dictionary pointer DP
00069Dr 3                               ; might end up pointing to garbage. However, an attempt to
00069Dr 3                               ; free more than RAM than CP0 will lead to CP being set to CP0,
00069Dr 3                               ; the DP pointing to the last word in RAM (should be DROP) and
00069Dr 3                               ; an error message.
00069Dr 3               
00069Dr 3                               ; We arrive here with ( n ) which is negative. First step,
00069Dr 3                               ; subtract the number TOS from the CP for a new CP
00069Dr 3  CA                           dex
00069Er 3  CA                           dex
00069Fr 3  A5 rr                        lda cp
0006A1r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0006A3r 3  A5 rr                        lda cp+1
0006A5r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
0006A7r 3               
0006A7r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_plus                     ; new CP is now TOS
0006AAr 3               
0006AAr 3                               ; Second step, see if we've gone too far. We compare the new
0006AAr 3                               ; CP on TOS (which, if we've really screwed up, might be
0006AAr 3                               ; negative) with CP0. This is a signed comparison
0006AAr 3  CA                           dex
0006ABr 3  CA                           dex                             ; new CP now NOS
0006ACr 3  A9 rr                        lda #<cp0
0006AEr 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0006B0r 3  A9 rr                        lda #>cp0
0006B2r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x                         ; CP0 is TOS
0006B4r 3               
0006B4r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr compare_16bit               ; still ( CP CP0 )
0006B7r 3               
0006B7r 3                               ; If CP (NOS) is smaller than CP0 (TOS), we're in trouble.
0006B7r 3                               ; This means we want Z=1 or N=1
0006B7r 3  F0 17                        beq @nega_done
0006B9r 3  30 15                        bmi @nega_done
0006BBr 3               
0006BBr 3                               ; Yep, we're in trouble. Set CP to CP0, set DP to the first
0006BBr 3                               ; word in ROM (should be DROP), and abort with an error
0006BBr 3  A9 rr                        lda #<cp0
0006BDr 3  85 rr                        sta cp
0006BFr 3  A9 rr                        lda #>cp0
0006C1r 3  85 rr                        sta cp+1
0006C3r 3               
0006C3r 3  A9 rr                        lda #<dictionary_start
0006C5r 3  85 rr                        sta dp
0006C7r 3  A9 rr                        lda #>dictionary_start
0006C9r 3  85 rr                        sta dp+1
0006CBr 3               
0006CBr 3  A9 0A                        lda #err_negallot
0006CDr 3  4C rr rr                     jmp error
0006D0r 3               
0006D0r 3               @nega_done:
0006D0r 3                               ; Save new CP, which is NOS
0006D0r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
0006D2r 3  85 rr                        sta cp
0006D4r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
0006D6r 3  85 rr                        sta cp+1
0006D8r 3               
0006D8r 3  E8                           inx
0006D9r 3  E8                           inx                     ; drop through to @done
0006DAr 3               @done:
0006DAr 3  E8                           inx
0006DBr 3  E8                           inx
0006DCr 3               z_allot:
0006DCr 3  60                           rts
0006DDr 3               
0006DDr 3               
0006DDr 3               
0006DDr 3               ; ## ALLOW_NATIVE ( -- ) "Flag last word to allow native compiling"
0006DDr 3               ; ## "allow-native"  auto  Tali Forth
0006DDr 3               xt_allow_native:
0006DDr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr current_to_dp
0006E0r 3  A0 01                        ldy #1          ; offset for status byte
0006E2r 3  B1 rr                        lda (dp),y
0006E4r 3  29 F5                        and #$ff-NN-AN  ; AN and NN flag is clear.
0006E6r 3  91 rr                        sta (dp),y
0006E8r 3               z_allow_native:
0006E8r 3  60                           rts
0006E9r 3               
0006E9r 3               
0006E9r 3               ; ## ALSO ( -- ) "Make room in the search order for another wordlist"
0006E9r 3               ; ## "also"  auto  ANS search ext
0006E9r 3                       ; """http://forth-standard.org/standard/search/ALSO"""
0006E9r 3               xt_also:
0006E9r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_get_order
0006ECr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_over
0006EFr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_swap
0006F2r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_one_plus
0006F5r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_set_order
0006F8r 3               
0006F8r 3  60           z_also:         rts
0006F9r 3               
0006F9r 3               
0006F9r 3               ; ## ALWAYS_NATIVE ( -- ) "Flag last word as always natively compiled"
0006F9r 3               ; ## "always-native"  auto  Tali Forth
0006F9r 3               xt_always_native:
0006F9r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr current_to_dp
0006FCr 3  A0 01                        ldy #1          ; offset for status byte
0006FEr 3  B1 rr                        lda (dp),y
000700r 3  09 02                        ora #AN         ; Make sure AN flag is set
000702r 3  29 F7                        and #$ff-NN     ; and NN flag is clear.
000704r 3  91 rr                        sta (dp),y
000706r 3               z_always_native:
000706r 3  60                           rts
000707r 3               
000707r 3               
000707r 3               ; ## AND ( n n -- n ) "Logically AND TOS and NOS"
000707r 3               ; ## "and"  auto  ANS core
000707r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/AND"""
000707r 3               xt_and:
000707r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
00070Ar 3               
00070Ar 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
00070Cr 3  35 02                        and 2,x
00070Er 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
000710r 3               
000710r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
000712r 3  35 03                        and 3,x
000714r 3  95 03                        sta 3,x
000716r 3               
000716r 3  E8                           inx
000717r 3  E8                           inx
000718r 3               
000718r 3  60           z_and:          rts
000719r 3               
000719r 3               
000719r 3               ; ## ASSEMBLER_WORDLIST ( -- u ) "WID for the Assembler wordlist"
000719r 3               ; ## "assembler-wordlist"  tested  Tali Assembler
000719r 3                       ; """ Commonly used like `assembler-wordlist >order` to add the
000719r 3                       ; assembler words to the search order so they can be used.
000719r 3                       ; See the tutorial on Wordlists and the Search Order for
000719r 3                       ; more information.
000719r 3                       ;
000719r 3                       ; This is a dummy entry, the code is shared with TWO
000719r 3                       ; """
000719r 3               
000719r 3               
000719r 3               ; ## AT_XY ( n m -- ) "Move cursor to position given"
000719r 3               ; ## "at-xy"  tested  ANS facility
000719r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/facility/AT-XY
000719r 3                       ; On an ANSI compatible terminal, place cursor at row n colum m.
000719r 3                       ; ANSI code is ESC[<n>;<m>H
000719r 3                       ;
000719r 3                       ; Do not use U. to print the numbers because the
000719r 3                       ; trailing space will not work with xterm
000719r 3                       ; """
000719r 3               xt_at_xy:
000719r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
00071Cr 3               
00071Cr 3  A9 1B                        lda #AscESC
00071Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr emit_a
000721r 3  A9 5B                        lda #$5B        ; ASCII for "["
000723r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr emit_a
000726r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr print_u
000729r 3  A9 3B                        lda #$3B        ; ASCII for ";"
00072Br 3  20 rr rr                     jsr emit_a
00072Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr print_u
000731r 3  A9 48                        lda #'H'
000733r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr emit_a
000736r 3               
000736r 3  60           z_at_xy:        rts
000737r 3               
000737r 3               
000737r 3               ; ## BACKSLASH ( -- ) "Ignore rest of line"
000737r 3               ; ## "\"  auto  ANS core ext
000737r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/bs"""
000737r 3               xt_backslash:
000737r 3  A5 rr                        lda ciblen
000739r 3  85 rr                        sta toin
00073Br 3  A5 rr                        lda ciblen+1
00073Dr 3  85 rr                        sta toin+1
00073Fr 3               
00073Fr 3  60           z_backslash:    rts
000740r 3               
000740r 3               
000740r 3               ; ## BASE ( -- addr ) "Push address of radix base to stack"
000740r 3               ; ## "base"  auto  ANS core
000740r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/BASE
000740r 3                       ; The ANS Forth standard sees the base up to 36, so we can cheat and
000740r 3                       ; ingore the MSB
000740r 3                       ; """
000740r 3               xt_base:
000740r 3  CA                           dex
000741r 3  CA                           dex
000742r 3  A9 rr                        lda #<base
000744r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x         ; LSB
000746r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x         ; MSB is always 0
000748r 3               
000748r 3  60           z_base:         rts
000749r 3               
000749r 3               
000749r 3               ; ## BEGIN ( -- addr ) "Mark entry point for loop"
000749r 3               ; ## "begin"  auto  ANS core
000749r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/BEGIN
000749r 3                       ;
000749r 3                       ; This is just an immediate version of here which could just
000749r 3                       ; as well be coded in Forth as
000749r 3                       ;       : BEGIN HERE ; IMMEDIATE COMPILE-ONLY
000749r 3                       ; Since this is a compiling word, we don't care that much about
000749r 3                       ; about speed
000749r 3                       ; """
000749r 3               
000749r 3               xt_begin:
000749r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_here
00074Cr 3  60           z_begin:        rts
00074Dr 3               
00074Dr 3               
00074Dr 3               
00074Dr 3               ; ## BELL ( -- ) "Emit ASCII BELL"
00074Dr 3               ; ## "bell"  tested  Tali Forth
00074Dr 3               xt_bell:
00074Dr 3  A9 07                        lda #7          ; ASCII value for BELl
00074Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr emit_a
000752r 3               
000752r 3  60           z_bell:         rts
000753r 3               
000753r 3               
000753r 3               ; ## BL ( -- c ) "Push ASCII value of SPACE to stack"
000753r 3               ; ## "bl"  auto  ANS core
000753r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/BL"""
000753r 3               
000753r 3               xt_bl:
000753r 3  CA                           dex
000754r 3  CA                           dex
000755r 3  A9 20                        lda #AscSP
000757r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
000759r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x
00075Br 3               
00075Br 3  60           z_bl:           rts
00075Cr 3               
00075Cr 3               
00075Cr 3               ; ## BLK ( -- addr ) "Push address of block being interpreted"
00075Cr 3               ; ## "block"  auto  ANS block
00075Cr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/block/BLK"""
00075Cr 3               xt_blk:
00075Cr 3                               ; BLK is at UP + blk_offset
00075Cr 3  CA                           dex
00075Dr 3  CA                           dex
00075Er 3  18                           clc
00075Fr 3  A5 rr                        lda up
000761r 3  69 00                        adc #blk_offset ; Add offset
000763r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
000765r 3  A5 rr                        lda up+1
000767r 3  69 00                        adc #0          ; Adding carry
000769r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
00076Br 3               
00076Br 3  60           z_blk:          rts
00076Cr 3               
00076Cr 3               
00076Cr 3               ; ## BLKBUFFER ( -- addr ) "Push address of block buffer"
00076Cr 3               ; ## "blkbuffer"  auto  Tali block
00076Cr 3               xt_blkbuffer:
00076Cr 3                               ; blkbuffer address is at UP + blkbuffer_offset.
00076Cr 3                               ; Unlike some of the other user variables, we actually
00076Cr 3                               ; want to push the address stored here, which will
00076Cr 3                               ; point to somewhere outside of the user variables.
00076Cr 3  CA                           dex
00076Dr 3  CA                           dex
00076Er 3                               ; Put the address on the stack.
00076Er 3  A0 28                        ldy #blkbuffer_offset
000770r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
000772r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
000774r 3  C8                           iny             ; Move along to the next byte
000775r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
000777r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
000779r 3               
000779r 3  60           z_blkbuffer:    rts
00077Ar 3               
00077Ar 3               
00077Ar 3               ; ## BLOCK ( u -- a-addr ) "Fetch a block into a buffer"
00077Ar 3               ; ## "block"  auto  ANS block
00077Ar 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/block/BLOCK"""
00077Ar 3               
00077Ar 3               xt_block:
00077Ar 3               
00077Ar 3                               ; See if the block requested is the same as the one we
00077Ar 3                               ; currently have in the buffer. Check the LSB.
00077Ar 3  A0 2A                        ldy #buffblocknum_offset
00077Cr 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
00077Er 3  D5 00                        cmp 0,x
000780r 3  D0 0F                        bne @not_in_buffer
000782r 3               
000782r 3                               ; Check the MSB.
000782r 3  C8                           iny
000783r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
000785r 3  D5 01                        cmp 1,x
000787r 3  D0 08                        bne @not_in_buffer
000789r 3               
000789r 3                               ; The block is in the buffer. See if the buffer is in use.
000789r 3  A0 2C                        ldy #buffstatus_offset
00078Br 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
00078Dr 3  29 01                        and #1          ; Check the in-use flag (bit 0)
00078Fr 3  D0 30                        bne @done       ; It's already in the buffer and in use.
000791r 3                                               ; @done will replace the block# with the
000791r 3                                               ; buffer address.
000791r 3               @not_in_buffer:
000791r 3                               ; Check the buffer status
000791r 3  A0 2C                        ldy #buffstatus_offset
000793r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y      ; Only bits 0 and 1 are used, so only
000795r 3  C9 03                        cmp #3          ; LSB is needed.
000797r 3  D0 0C                        bne @buffer_available ; Unused or not dirty = available
000799r 3               
000799r 3                               ; We need to save the block.
000799r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_blkbuffer
00079Cr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_buffblocknum
00079Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_fetch
0007A2r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_block_write
0007A5r 3               
0007A5r 3               @buffer_available:
0007A5r 3                               ; Save the block number.
0007A5r 3  A0 2A                        ldy #buffblocknum_offset
0007A7r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0007A9r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
0007ABr 3  C8                           iny
0007ACr 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
0007AEr 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
0007B0r 3               
0007B0r 3                               ; Get the requested block.
0007B0r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_blkbuffer
0007B3r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_swap
0007B6r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_block_read
0007B9r 3               
0007B9r 3                               ; Mark the buffer as clean and in-use.
0007B9r 3  A9 01                        lda #1
0007BBr 3  A0 2C                        ldy #buffstatus_offset
0007BDr 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
0007BFr 3               
0007BFr 3                               ; Make room on the stack for the return address.
0007BFr 3  CA                           dex
0007C0r 3  CA                           dex
0007C1r 3               
0007C1r 3               @done:
0007C1r 3                               ; It's in the buffer. Return the buffer address.
0007C1r 3  A0 28                        ldy #blkbuffer_offset
0007C3r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0007C5r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0007C7r 3  C8                           iny
0007C8r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0007CAr 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
0007CCr 3               
0007CCr 3  60           z_block:        rts
0007CDr 3               
0007CDr 3               
0007CDr 3               
0007CDr 3               ; ## BLOCK_RAMDRIVE_INIT ( u -- ) "Create a ramdrive for blocks"
0007CDr 3               ; ## "block-ramdrive-init"  auto  Tali block
0007CDr 3                       ; """Create a RAM drive, with the given number of
0007CDr 3                       ; blocks, in the dictionary along with setting up the block words to
0007CDr 3                       ; use it.  The read/write routines do not provide bounds checking.
0007CDr 3                       ; Expected use: `4 block-ramdrive-init` ( to create blocks 0-3 )
0007CDr 3                       ; """
0007CDr 3               
0007CDr 3               xt_block_ramdrive_init:
0007CDr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
0007D0r 3               
0007D0r 3                               ; Store the string to run here as a string literal.
0007D0r 3                               ; See SLITERAL for the format information. This way, we
0007D0r 3                               ; don't have the words defined below in the Dictionary until
0007D0r 3                               ; we really use them.
0007D0r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @after_ramdrive_code
0007D3r 3               
0007D3r 3               @ramdrive_code:
0007D3r 3  62 61 73 65          .byte "base @ swap decimal"
0007D7r 3  20 40 20 73  
0007DBr 3  77 61 70 20  
0007E6r 3  20 31 30 32          .byte " 1024 *" ; ( Calculate how many bytes are needed for numblocks blocks )
0007EAr 3  34 20 2A     
0007EDr 3  20 64 75 70          .byte " dup"    ; ( Save a copy for formatting it at the end )
0007F1r 3  20 62 75 66          .byte " buffer: ramdrive" ; ( Create ramdrive )
0007F5r 3  66 65 72 3A  
0007F9r 3  20 72 61 6D  
000802r 3                       ; ( These routines just copy between the buffer and the ramdrive blocks )
000802r 3  20 3A 20 62          .byte " : block-read-ramdrive"  ; ( addr u -- )
000806r 3  6C 6F 63 6B  
00080Ar 3  2D 72 65 61  
000818r 3  20 72 61 6D          .byte " ramdrive swap 1024 * + swap 1024 move ;"
00081Cr 3  64 72 69 76  
000820r 3  65 20 73 77  
000840r 3  20 3A 20 62          .byte " : block-write-ramdrive" ; ( addr u -- )
000844r 3  6C 6F 63 6B  
000848r 3  2D 77 72 69  
000857r 3  20 72 61 6D          .byte " ramdrive swap 1024 * + 1024 move ;"
00085Br 3  64 72 69 76  
00085Fr 3  65 20 73 77  
00087Ar 3  20 27 20 62          .byte " ' block-read-ramdrive block-read-vector !" ; ( Replace I/O vectors )
00087Er 3  6C 6F 63 6B  
000882r 3  2D 72 65 61  
0008A4r 3  20 27 20 62          .byte " ' block-write-ramdrive block-write-vector !"
0008A8r 3  6C 6F 63 6B  
0008ACr 3  2D 77 72 69  
0008D0r 3  20 72 61 6D          .byte " ramdrive swap blank base !"
0008D4r 3  64 72 69 76  
0008D8r 3  65 20 73 77  
0008EBr 3               
0008EBr 3               @after_ramdrive_code:
0008EBr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr sliteral_runtime
0008EEr 3               
0008EEr 3  rr rr 18 01  .word @ramdrive_code, @after_ramdrive_code-@ramdrive_code
0008F2r 3               
0008F2r 3                               ; The address and length of the ramdrive code is now on the
0008F2r 3                               ; stack. Call EVALUATE to run it.
0008F2r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_evaluate
0008F5r 3               
0008F5r 3               z_block_ramdrive_init:
0008F5r 3  60                           rts
0008F6r 3               
0008F6r 3               
0008F6r 3               
0008F6r 3               ; ## BLOCK_READ ( addr u -- ) "Read a block from storage (deferred word)"
0008F6r 3               ; ## "block-read"  auto  Tali block
0008F6r 3                       ; """BLOCK-READ is a vectored word that the user needs to override
0008F6r 3                       ; with their own version to read a block from storage.
0008F6r 3                       ; The stack parameters are ( buffer_address block# -- ).
0008F6r 3                       ; """
0008F6r 3               xt_block_read:
0008F6r 3                               ; Execute the BLOCK-READ-VECTOR
0008F6r 3  A0 2E                        ldy #blockread_offset
0008F8r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0008FAr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
0008FCr 3  C8                           iny
0008FDr 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0008FFr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
000901r 3               
000901r 3  6C rr rr                     jmp (tmp1)
000904r 3               
000904r 3               z_block_read:   ; No RTS needed
000904r 3               
000904r 3               
000904r 3               ; ## BLOCK_READ_VECTOR ( -- addr ) "Address of the block-read vector"
000904r 3               ; ## "block-read-vector"  auto  Tali block
000904r 3                       ; """BLOCK-READ is a vectored word that the user needs to override
000904r 3                       ; with their own version to read a block from storage.
000904r 3                       ; This word gives the address of the vector so it can be replaced.
000904r 3                       ; """
000904r 3               xt_block_read_vector:
000904r 3                               ; Get the BLOCK-READ-VECTOR address
000904r 3  CA                           dex
000905r 3  CA                           dex
000906r 3  18                           clc
000907r 3  A5 rr                        lda up
000909r 3  69 2E                        adc #blockread_offset
00090Br 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
00090Dr 3  A5 rr                        lda up+1
00090Fr 3  69 00                        adc #0          ; Add carry
000911r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
000913r 3               
000913r 3               z_block_read_vector:
000913r 3  60                           rts
000914r 3               
000914r 3               
000914r 3               ; This is the default error message the vectored words BLOCK-READ and
000914r 3               ; BLOCK-WRITE start with. This word is not included in the dictionary.
000914r 3               xt_block_word_error:
000914r 3  A9 0C                        lda #err_blockwords
000916r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp error       ; no RTS needed
000919r 3               z_block_word_error:
000919r 3               
000919r 3               ; ## BLOCK_WRITE ( addr u -- ) "Write a block to storage (deferred word)"
000919r 3               ; ## "block-write"  auto  Tali block
000919r 3                       ; """BLOCK-WRITE is a vectored word that the user needs to override
000919r 3                       ; with their own version to write a block to storage.
000919r 3                       ; The stack parameters are ( buffer_address block# -- ).
000919r 3                       ; """
000919r 3               xt_block_write:
000919r 3                               ; Execute the BLOCK-READ-VECTOR
000919r 3  A0 30                        ldy #blockwrite_offset
00091Br 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
00091Dr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
00091Fr 3  C8                           iny
000920r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
000922r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
000924r 3  6C rr rr                     jmp (tmp1)
000927r 3               
000927r 3               z_block_write:  ; No RTS needed
000927r 3               
000927r 3               
000927r 3               ; ## BLOCK_WRITE_VECTOR ( -- addr ) "Address of the block-write vector"
000927r 3               ; ## "block-write-vector"  auto  Tali block
000927r 3                       ; """BLOCK-WRITE is a vectored word that the user needs to override
000927r 3                       ; with their own version to write a block to storage.
000927r 3                       ; This word gives the address of the vector so it can be replaced.
000927r 3                       ; """
000927r 3               xt_block_write_vector:
000927r 3                               ; Get the BLOCK-WRITE-VECTOR address
000927r 3  CA                           dex
000928r 3  CA                           dex
000929r 3  18                           clc
00092Ar 3  A5 rr                        lda up
00092Cr 3  69 30                        adc #blockwrite_offset
00092Er 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
000930r 3  A5 rr                        lda up+1
000932r 3  69 00                        adc #0          ; Add carry
000934r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
000936r 3               
000936r 3               z_block_write_vector:
000936r 3  60                           rts
000937r 3               
000937r 3               
000937r 3               ; ## BOUNDS ( addr u -- addr+u addr ) "Prepare address for looping"
000937r 3               ; ## "bounds"  auto  Gforth
000937r 3                       ; """http://www.complang.tuwien.ac.at/forth/gforth/Docs-html/Memory-Blocks.html
000937r 3                       ; Given a string, return the correct Data Stack parameters for
000937r 3                       ; a DO/LOOP loop over its characters. This is realized as
000937r 3                       ; OVER + SWAP in Forth, but we do it a lot faster in assembler
000937r 3                       ; """
000937r 3               xt_bounds:
000937r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
00093Ar 3               
00093Ar 3  18                           clc
00093Br 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x                 ; LSB u
00093Dr 3  B4 02                        ldy 2,x                 ; LSB addr
00093Fr 3  75 02                        adc 2,x
000941r 3  95 02                        sta 2,x                 ; LSB addr+u
000943r 3  94 00                        sty 0,x
000945r 3               
000945r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x                 ; MSB u
000947r 3  B4 03                        ldy 3,x                 ; MSB addr
000949r 3  75 03                        adc 3,x
00094Br 3  95 03                        sta 3,x                 ; MSB addr+u
00094Dr 3  94 01                        sty 1,x
00094Fr 3               
00094Fr 3  60           z_bounds:       rts
000950r 3               
000950r 3               
000950r 3               ; ## BRACKET_CHAR ( "c" -- ) "Compile character"
000950r 3               ; ## "[char]"  auto  ANS core
000950r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/BracketCHAR
000950r 3                       ; Compile the ASCII value of a character as a literal. This is an
000950r 3                       ; immediate, compile-only word.
000950r 3                       ;
000950r 3                       ; A definition given in
000950r 3                       ; http://forth-standard.org/standard/implement is
000950r 3                       ; : [CHAR]  CHAR POSTPONE LITERAL ; IMMEDIATE
000950r 3                       ; """
000950r 3               xt_bracket_char:
000950r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_char
000953r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_literal
000956r 3  60           z_bracket_char: rts
000957r 3

00095Er 3               ; ## BUFFBLOCKNUM ( -- addr ) "Push address of variable holding block in buffer"
00095Er 3               ; ## "buffblocknum"  auto  Tali block
00095Er 3               xt_buffblocknum:
00095Er 3                               ; BUFFBLOCKNUM is at UP + buffblocknum_offset
00095Er 3  CA                           dex
00095Fr 3  CA                           dex
000960r 3  18                           clc
000961r 3  A5 rr                        lda up
000963r 3  69 2A                        adc #buffblocknum_offset        ; Add offset

00096Er 3               
00096Er 3               ; ## BUFFER ( u -- a-addr ) "Get a buffer for a block"
00096Er 3               ; ## "buffer"  auto  ANS block
00096Er 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/block/BUFFER"""
00096Er 3               
00096Er 3               xt_buffer:
00096Er 3                               ; Check the buffer status
00096Er 3  A0 2C                        ldy #buffstatus_offset
000970r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y      ; Only bits 0 and 1 are used, so only
000972r 3  C9 03                        cmp #3          ; LSB is needed.
000974r 3  D0 0C                        bne @buffer_available ; Unused or not dirty = available
000976r 3               
000976r 3                               ; We need to save the block.
000976r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_blkbuffer
000979r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_buffblocknum
00097Cr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_fetch
00097Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_block_write
000982r 3               
000982r 3               @buffer_available:
000982r 3                               ; Save the block number.
000982r 3  A0 2A                        ldy #buffblocknum_offset
000984r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
000986r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
000988r 3  C8                           iny
000989r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
00098Br 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
00098Dr 3               
00098Dr 3                               ; Mark the buffer as clean and in-use.
00098Dr 3  A9 01                        lda #1
00098Fr 3  A0 2C                        ldy #buffstatus_offset
000991r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
000993r 3               
000993r 3               @done:
000993r 3                               ; Return the buffer address.
000993r 3  A0 28                        ldy #blkbuffer_offset
000995r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
000997r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
000999r 3  C8                           iny
00099Ar 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
00099Cr 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
00099Er 3               
00099Er 3  60           z_buffer:       rts
00099Fr 3               
00099Fr 3               
00099Fr 3               
00099Fr 3               ; ## BUFFER_COLON ( u "<name>" -- ; -- addr ) "Create an uninitialized buffer"
00099Fr 3               ; ## "buffer:"  auto  ANS core ext
00099Fr 3                               ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/BUFFERColon
00099Fr 3                               ; Create a buffer of size u that puts its address on the stack
00099Fr 3                               ; when its name is used.
00099Fr 3                               ; """
00099Fr 3               xt_buffer_colon:
00099Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_create
0009A2r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_allot
0009A5r 3  60           z_buffer_colon: rts

0009A6r 3               ; ## BUFFSTATUS ( -- addr ) "Push address of variable holding buffer status"
0009A6r 3               ; ## "buffstatus"  auto  Tali block
0009A6r 3               xt_buffstatus:
0009A6r 3                               ; BUFFSTATUS is at UP + buffstatus_offset
0009A6r 3  CA                           dex
0009A7r 3  CA                           dex
0009A8r 3  18                           clc
0009A9r 3  A5 rr                        lda up
0009ABr 3  69 2C                        adc #buffstatus_offset  ; Add offset
0009ADr 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0009AFr 3  A5 rr                        lda up+1
0009B1r 3  69 00                        adc #0                  ; Adding carry
0009B3r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
0009B5r 3               
0009B5r 3  60           z_buffstatus:   rts
0009B6r 3               
0009B6r 3               
0009B6r 3               ; ## BYE ( -- ) "Break"
0009B6r 3               ; ## "bye"  tested  ANS tools ext
0009B6r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/tools/BYE"""
0009B6r 3               
0009B6r 3               xt_bye:
0009B6r 3                               ;brk
0009B6r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp platform_bye
0009B9r 3               z_bye:          ;rts             ; never reached
0009B9r 3               
0009B9r 3               
0009B9r 3               
0009B9r 3               ; ## C_COMMA ( c -- ) "Store one byte/char in the Dictionary"
0009B9r 3               ; ## "c,"  auto  ANS core
0009B9r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CComma"""
0009B9r 3               
0009B9r 3               xt_c_comma:
0009B9r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
0009BCr 3               
0009BCr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0009BEr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr cmpl_a
0009C1r 3               
0009C1r 3  E8                           inx
0009C2r 3  E8                           inx
0009C3r 3               
0009C3r 3  60           z_c_comma:      rts
0009C4r 3               
0009C4r 3               
0009C4r 3               
0009C4r 3               ; ## C_FETCH ( addr -- c ) "Get a character/byte from given address"
0009C4r 3               ; ## "c@"  auto  ANS core
0009C4r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CFetch"""
0009C4r 3               xt_c_fetch:
0009C4r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
0009C7r 3               
0009C7r 3  A1 00                        lda (0,x)
0009C9r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0009CBr 3  74 01                        stz 1,x         ; Ignore LSB
0009CDr 3               
0009CDr 3  60           z_c_fetch:      rts
0009CEr 3               
0009CEr 3               
0009CEr 3               ; ## C_STORE ( c addr -- ) "Store character at address given"
0009CEr 3               ; ## "c!"  auto  ANS core
0009CEr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CStore"""
0009CEr 3               xt_c_store:
0009CEr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
0009D1r 3               
0009D1r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
0009D3r 3  81 00                        sta (0,x)
0009D5r 3               
0009D5r 3  E8                           inx
0009D6r 3  E8                           inx
0009D7r 3  E8                           inx
0009D8r 3  E8                           inx
0009D9r 3               
0009D9r 3  60           z_c_store:      rts
0009DAr 3               
0009DAr 3               
0009DAr 3               ; ## CASE (C: -- 0) ( -- ) "Conditional flow control"
0009DAr 3               ; ## "case"  auto  ANS core ext
0009DAr 3                       ; """http://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CASE
0009DAr 3                       ;
0009DAr 3                       ; This is a dummy header, CASE shares the actual code with ZERO.
0009DAr 3                       ; """
0009DAr 3               
0009DAr 3               
0009DAr 3               ; ## CELL_PLUS ( u -- u ) "Add cell size in bytes"
0009DAr 3               ; ## "cell+"  auto  ANS core
0009DAr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CELLPlus
0009DAr 3                       ; Add the number of bytes ("address units") that one cell needs.
0009DAr 3                       ; Since this is an 8 bit machine with 16 bit cells, we add two bytes.
0009DAr 3                       ; """
0009DAr 3               
0009DAr 3               xt_cell_plus:
0009DAr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
0009DDr 3               
0009DDr 3  F6 00                        inc 0,x
0009DFr 3  D0 02                        bne @1
0009E1r 3  F6 01                        inc 1,x
0009E3r 3               @1:
0009E3r 3  F6 00                        inc 0,x
0009E5r 3  D0 02                        bne @done
0009E7r 3  F6 01                        inc 1,x
0009E9r 3               @done:
0009E9r 3  60           z_cell_plus:    rts
0009EAr 3               
0009EAr 3               
0009EAr 3               
0009EAr 3               ; ## CELLS ( u -- u ) "Convert cells to size in bytes"
0009EAr 3               ; ## "cells"  auto  ANS core
0009EAr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CELLS
0009EAr 3                       ;

0009EAr 3                       ; 2*, which is where the header directs us to
0009EAr 3                       ; """

0009EAr 3               
0009EAr 3               ; ## CHAR ( "c" -- u ) "Convert character to ASCII value"
0009EAr 3               ; ## "char"  auto  ANS core
0009EAr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CHAR"""
0009EAr 3               
0009EAr 3               xt_char:
0009EAr 3                               ; get character from string, returns ( addr u )
0009EAr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_parse_name
0009EDr 3               
0009EDr 3                               ; if we got back a zero, we have a problem
0009EDr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0009EFr 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
0009F1r 3  D0 05                        bne @not_empty
0009F3r 3               
0009F3r 3  A9 05                        lda #err_noname
0009F5r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp error
0009F8r 3               
0009F8r 3               @not_empty:
0009F8r 3  E8                           inx             ; drop number of characters, leave addr
0009F9r 3  E8                           inx
0009FAr 3  A1 00                        lda (0,x)       ; get character (equivalent to C@)
0009FCr 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0009FEr 3  74 01                        stz 1,x         ; MSB is always zero
000A00r 3               
000A00r 3  60           z_char:         rts
000A01r 3               
000A01r 3               
000A01r 3               
000A01r 3               ; ## CHAR_PLUS ( addr -- addr+1 ) "Add the size of a character unit to address"
000A01r 3               ; ## "char+"  auto  ANS core
000A01r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CHARPlus
000A01r 3                       ;
000A01r 3                       ; This is a dummy entry, the code is shared with ONE_PLUS
000A01r 3                       ; """
000A01r 3               
000A01r 3               
000A01r 3               ; ## CHARS ( n -- n ) "Number of bytes that n chars need"
000A01r 3               ; ## "chars"  auto  ANS core
000A01r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/CHARS
000A01r 3                       ; Return how many address units n chars are. Since this is an 8 bit
000A01r 3                       ; machine, this does absolutely nothing and is included for
000A01r 3                       ; compatibility with other Forth versions
000A01r 3                       ; """
000A01r 3               
000A01r 3               xt_chars:
000A01r 3                               ; Checking for underflow seems a bit stupid because this
000A01r 3                               ; routine does nothing on this machine. However, the user
000A01r 3                               ; should be warned that there is something wrong with the
000A01r 3                               ; code if this occurs.
000A01r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
000A04r 3               
000A04r 3  60           z_chars:        rts
000A05r 3               
000A05r 3               
000A05r 3               ; ## CLEAVE ( addr u -- addr2 u2 addr1 u1 ) "Split off word from string"
000A05r 3               ; ## "cleave"  auto  Tali Forth
000A05r 3               
000A05r 3                       ; """Given a range of memory with words delimited by whitespace,return
000A05r 3                       ; the first word at the top of the stack and the rest of the word
000A05r 3                       ; following it.
000A05r 3                       ;
000A05r 3                       ; Example:
000A05r 3                       ; s" w1 w2 w3" cleave  -> "w2 w3" "w1"
000A05r 3                       ; s" w1" cleave        -> "" "w1"
000A05r 3                       ;
000A05r 3                       ; Since it will be used in loops a lot, we want it to work in pure
000A05r 3                       ; assembler and be as fast as we can make it. Calls PARSE-NAME so we
000A05r 3                       ; strip leading delimiters.
000A05r 3                       ; """
000A05r 3               
000A05r 3               xt_cleave:
000A05r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
000A08r 3               
000A08r 3                               ; We arrive here with ( addr u ). We need to strip any leading
000A08r 3                               ; spaces by hand: PARSE-NAME does do that, but it doesn't
000A08r 3                               ; remember how many spaces were stripped. This means we can't
000A08r 3                               ; calculate the length of the remainder. Fortunately, Tali
000A08r 3                               ; Forth has just the word we need for this:
000A08r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_minus_leading    ; -LEADING ( addr u )
000A0Br 3               
000A0Br 3                               ; The main part we can turn over to PARSE-NAME, except that we
000A0Br 3                               ; have a string ( addr u ) and not stuff in the input buffer.
000A0Br 3                               ; We get around this by cheating: We place ( addr u ) in the
000A0Br 3                               ; input buffer and then call PARSE-NAME.
000A0Br 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_input_to_r       ; save old imput state
000A0Er 3               
000A0Er 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x         ; u is new ciblen
000A10r 3  85 rr                        sta ciblen
000A12r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
000A14r 3  85 rr                        sta ciblen+1
000A16r 3               
000A16r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x         ; addr is new cib
000A18r 3  85 rr                        sta cib
000A1Ar 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
000A1Cr 3  85 rr                        sta cib+1
000A1Er 3               
000A1Er 3  64 rr                        stz toin        ; >IN pointer is zero
000A20r 3  64 rr                        stz toin+1
000A22r 3               
000A22r 3                               ; PARSE-NAME gives us back the substring of the first word
000A22r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_parse_name       ; ( addr u addr-s u-s )
000A25r 3               
000A25r 3                               ; If we were given an empty string, then we're done. It's the
000A25r 3                               ; resposibility of the user to catch this as a sign to end the
000A25r 3                               ; any loop
000A25r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
000A27r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
000A29r 3  F0 23                        beq @done
000A2Br 3               
000A2Br 3                               ; Now we have to adjust the original string
000A2Br 3  B5 04                        lda 4,x         ; LSB of original u
000A2Dr 3  38                           sec
000A2Er 3  F5 00                        sbc 0,x
000A30r 3  95 04                        sta 4,x
000A32r 3               
000A32r 3  B5 05                        lda 5,x         ; MSB of original u
000A34r 3  F5 01                        sbc 1,x
000A36r 3  95 05                        sta 5,x
000A38r 3               
000A38r 3  B5 06                        lda 6,x         ; LSB of original addr
000A3Ar 3  18                           clc
000A3Br 3  75 00                        adc 0,x
000A3Dr 3  95 06                        sta 6,x
000A3Fr 3               
000A3Fr 3  B5 07                        lda 7,x         ; MSB of original addr
000A41r 3  75 01                        adc 1,x
000A43r 3  95 07                        sta 7,x
000A45r 3               
000A45r 3                               ; There is one small problem: PARSE-NAME will probably have
000A45r 3                               ; left the string with the rest of the words with leading
000A45r 3                               ; delimiters. We use our magic -LEADING again
000A45r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_swap         ; ( addr-s u-s addr u )
000A48r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_minus_leading
000A4Br 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_swap         ; ( addr u addr-s u-s )
000A4Er 3               @done:
000A4Er 3                               ; Restore input
000A4Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_r_to_input
000A51r 3               
000A51r 3  60           z_cleave:       rts
000A52r 3               
000A52r 3               
000A52r 3               
000A52r 3               ; ## CMOVE ( addr1 addr2 u -- ) "Copy bytes going from low to high"
000A52r 3               ; ## "cmove"  auto  ANS string
000A52r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/string/CMOVE
000A52r 3                       ; Copy u bytes from addr1 to addr2, going low to high (addr2 is
000A52r 3                       ; larger than addr1). Based on code in Leventhal, Lance A.
000A52r 3                       ; "6502 Assembly Language Routines", p. 201, where it is called
000A52r 3                       ; "move left".
000A52r 3                       ;
000A52r 3                       ; There are no official tests for this word.
000A52r 3                       ; """
000A52r 3               
000A52r 3               xt_cmove:
000A52r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_3
000A55r 3               
000A55r 3                               ; move destination address to where we can work with it
000A55r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
000A57r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2        ; use tmp2 because easier to remember
000A59r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
000A5Br 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2+1
000A5Dr 3               
000A5Dr 3                               ; move source address to where we can work with it
000A5Dr 3  B5 04                        lda 4,x
000A5Fr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1        ; use tmp1 because easier to remember
000A61r 3  B5 05                        lda 5,x
000A63r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
000A65r 3               
000A65r 3  A0 00                        ldy #0
000A67r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x         ; number of whole pages to move
000A69r 3  F0 0F                        beq @dopartial
000A6Br 3               
000A6Br 3               @page:
000A6Br 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp1),y
000A6Dr 3  91 rr                        sta (tmp2),y
000A6Fr 3  C8                           iny
000A70r 3  D0 F9                        bne @page
000A72r 3               
000A72r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp1+1
000A74r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp2+1
000A76r 3  D6 01                        dec 1,x
000A78r 3  D0 F1                        bne @page
000A7Ar 3               
000A7Ar 3               @dopartial:
000A7Ar 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x         ; length of last page
000A7Cr 3  F0 09                        beq @done
000A7Er 3               
000A7Er 3               @partial:
000A7Er 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp1),y
000A80r 3  91 rr                        sta (tmp2),y
000A82r 3  C8                           iny
000A83r 3               
000A83r 3  D6 00                        dec 0,x
000A85r 3  D0 F7                        bne @partial
000A87r 3               
000A87r 3               @done:          ; clear the stack
000A87r 3  8A                           txa
000A88r 3  18                           clc
000A89r 3  69 06                        adc #6
000A8Br 3  AA                           tax
000A8Cr 3               
000A8Cr 3  60           z_cmove:        rts
000A8Dr 3               
000A8Dr 3               
000A8Dr 3               
000A8Dr 3               ; ## CMOVE_UP ( add1 add2 u -- ) "Copy bytes from high to low"
000A8Dr 3               ; ## "cmove>"  auto  ANS string
000A8Dr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/string/CMOVEtop
000A8Dr 3                       ; Based on code in Leventhal, Lance A. "6502 Assembly Language
000A8Dr 3                       ; Routines", p. 201, where it is called "move right".
000A8Dr 3                       ;
000A8Dr 3                       ; There are no official tests for this word.
000A8Dr 3                       ; """
000A8Dr 3               
000A8Dr 3               xt_cmove_up:
000A8Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_3
000A90r 3               
000A90r 3                               ; Move destination address to where we can work with it
000A90r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
000A92r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2        ; use tmp2 because easier to remember
000A94r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
000A96r 3  18                           clc
000A97r 3  75 01                        adc 1,x
000A99r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2+1      ; point to last page of destination
000A9Br 3               
000A9Br 3                               ; Move source address to where we can work with it
000A9Br 3  B5 04                        lda 4,x
000A9Dr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1        ; use tmp1 because easier to remember
000A9Fr 3  B5 05                        lda 5,x
000AA1r 3  18                           clc
000AA2r 3  75 01                        adc 1,x
000AA4r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1      ; point to last page of source
000AA6r 3  F6 01                        inc 1,x         ; allows us to use bne with dec 1,x below
000AA8r 3               
000AA8r 3                               ; Move the last partial page first
000AA8r 3  B4 00                        ldy 0,x         ; length of last page
000AAAr 3  F0 0E                        beq @nopartial
000AACr 3               
000AACr 3               @outerloop:
000AACr 3  88                           dey
000AADr 3  F0 07                        beq @finishpage
000AAFr 3               
000AAFr 3               @innerloop:
000AAFr 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp1),y
000AB1r 3  91 rr                        sta (tmp2),y
000AB3r 3  88                           dey
000AB4r 3  D0 F9                        bne @innerloop
000AB6r 3               
000AB6r 3               @finishpage:
000AB6r 3  B2 rr                        lda (tmp1)      ; handle y = 0 separately
000AB8r 3  92 rr                        sta (tmp2)
000ABAr 3               
000ABAr 3               @nopartial:
000ABAr 3  C6 rr                        dec tmp1+1      ; back up to previous pages
000ABCr 3  C6 rr                        dec tmp2+1
000ABEr 3  D6 01                        dec 1,x
000AC0r 3  D0 EA                        bne @outerloop
000AC2r 3               @done:
000AC2r 3                               ; clear up the stack and leave
000AC2r 3  8A                           txa
000AC3r 3  18                           clc
000AC4r 3  69 06                        adc #6
000AC6r 3  AA                           tax
000AC7r 3               
000AC7r 3  60           z_cmove_up:     rts
000AC8r 3               
000AC8r 3               
000AC8r 3               
000AC8r 3               ; ## COLON ( "name" -- ) "Start compilation of a new word"
000AC8r 3               ; ## ":"  auto  ANS core
000AC8r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/Colon
000AC8r 3                       ;
000AC8r 3                       ; Use the CREATE routine and fill in the rest by hand.
000AC8r 3                       ; """
000AC8r 3               
000AC8r 3               xt_colon:
000AC8r 3                               ; If we're already in the compile state, complain
000AC8r 3                               ; and quit
000AC8r 3  A5 rr                        lda state
000ACAr 3  05 rr                        ora state+1
000ACCr 3  F0 05                        beq @1
000ACEr 3               
000ACEr 3  A9 07                        lda #err_state
000AD0r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp error
000AD3r 3               @1:
000AD3r 3                               ; switch to compile state
000AD3r 3  C6 rr                        dec state
000AD5r 3  C6 rr                        dec state+1
000AD7r 3               
000AD7r 3                               ; Set bit 6 in status to tell ";" and RECURSE this is a normal
000AD7r 3                               ; word
000AD7r 3  A9 40                        lda #%01000000
000AD9r 3  04 rr                        tsb status
000ADBr 3               
000ADBr 3                               ; CREATE is going to change the DP to point to the new word's
000ADBr 3                               ; header. While this is fine for (say) variables, it would mean
000ADBr 3                               ; that FIND-NAME etc would find a half-finished word when
000ADBr 3                               ; looking in the Dictionary. To prevent this, we save the old
000ADBr 3                               ; version of DP and restore it later. The new DP is placed in
000ADBr 3                               ; the variable WORKWORD until we're finished with a SEMICOLON.
000ADBr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr current_to_dp
000ADEr 3  A5 rr                        lda dp+1            ; CREATE uses a lot of variables
000AE0r 3  48                           pha
000AE1r 3  A5 rr                        lda dp
000AE3r 3  48                           pha
000AE4r 3               
000AE4r 3                               ; Tell create not to print warning for duplicate name.
000AE4r 3  A9 80                        lda #%10000000
000AE6r 3  04 rr                        tsb status
000AE8r 3               
000AE8r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_create
000AEBr 3               
000AEBr 3                               ; Get the nt (not the xt!) of the new word as described above.
000AEBr 3                               ; Only COLON, SEMICOLON and RECURSE get to access WORKWORD
000AEBr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr current_to_dp   ; This might be able to be omitted
000AEEr 3  A5 rr                        lda dp
000AF0r 3  85 rr                        sta workword
000AF2r 3  A5 rr                        lda dp+1
000AF4r 3  85 rr                        sta workword+1
000AF6r 3               
000AF6r 3                               ; Restore original DP
000AF6r 3  68                           pla
000AF7r 3  85 rr                        sta dp
000AF9r 3  68                           pla
000AFAr 3  85 rr                        sta dp+1
000AFCr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr dp_to_current
000AFFr 3               
000AFFr 3                               ; CREATE includes a subroutine jump to DOVAR by default. We
000AFFr 3                               ; back up three bytes and overwrite that.
000AFFr 3  A5 rr                        lda cp
000B01r 3  38                           sec
000B02r 3  E9 03                        sbc #3
000B04r 3  85 rr                        sta cp
000B06r 3  B0 02                        bcs @done
000B08r 3  C6 rr                        dec cp+1
000B0Ar 3               @done:
000B0Ar 3  60           z_colon:        rts
000B0Br 3               
000B0Br 3               
000B0Br 3               ; ## COLON_NONAME ( -- ) "Start compilation of a new word""
000B0Br 3               ; ## ":NONAME"  auto  ANS core
000B0Br 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ColonNONAME
000B0Br 3                       ; Compile a word with no nt.  ";" will put its xt on the stack.
000B0Br 3                       ; """
000B0Br 3               
000B0Br 3               xt_colon_noname:
000B0Br 3                               ; If we're already in the compile state, complain
000B0Br 3                               ; and quit
000B0Br 3  A5 rr                        lda state
000B0Dr 3  05 rr                        ora state+1
000B0Fr 3  F0 05                        beq @1
000B11r 3               
000B11r 3  A9 07                        lda #err_state
000B13r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp error
000B16r 3               @1:
000B16r 3                               ; switch to compile state
000B16r 3  C6 rr                        dec state
000B18r 3  C6 rr                        dec state+1
000B1Ar 3               
000B1Ar 3                               ; Clear bit 6 in status to tell ";" and RECURSE this is
000B1Ar 3                               ; a :NONAME word.
000B1Ar 3  A9 40                        lda #%01000000
000B1Cr 3  14 rr                        trb status
000B1Er 3               
000B1Er 3                               ; Put cp (the xt for this word) in WORKWORD. The flag above
000B1Er 3                               ; lets both ";" and RECURSE know that is is an xt instead of an
000B1Er 3                               ; nt and they will modify their behavior.
000B1Er 3  A5 rr                        lda cp
000B20r 3  85 rr                        sta workword
000B22r 3  A5 rr                        lda cp+1
000B24r 3  85 rr                        sta workword+1
000B26r 3               @done:
000B26r 3  60           z_colon_noname:        rts
000B27r 3               
000B27r 3               
000B27r 3               
000B27r 3               ; ## COMMA ( n -- ) "Allot and store one cell in memory"
000B27r 3               ; ## ","  auto  ANS core
000B27r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/Comma
000B27r 3                       ; Store TOS at current place in memory.
000B27r 3                       ;
000B27r 3                       ; Since this an eight-bit machine, we can ignore all alignment issues.
000B27r 3                       ; """
000B27r 3               
000B27r 3               xt_comma:
000B27r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
000B2Ar 3               
000B2Ar 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
000B2Cr 3  92 rr                        sta (cp)
000B2Er 3               
000B2Er 3  E6 rr                        inc cp
000B30r 3  D0 02                        bne @1
000B32r 3  E6 rr                        inc cp+1
000B34r 3               @1:
000B34r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
000B36r 3  92 rr                        sta (cp)
000B38r 3               
000B38r 3  E6 rr                        inc cp
000B3Ar 3  D0 02                        bne @done
000B3Cr 3  E6 rr                        inc cp+1
000B3Er 3               @done:
000B3Er 3  E8                           inx
000B3Fr 3  E8                           inx
000B40r 3               
000B40r 3  60           z_comma:        rts
000B41r 3               
000B41r 3               
000B41r 3               
000B41r 3               ; ## COMPARE ( addr1 u1 addr2 u2 -- -1 | 0 | 1) "Compare two strings"
000B41r 3               ; ## "compare"   auto  ANS string
000B41r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/string/COMPARE
000B41r 3                       ; Compare string1 (denoted by addr1 u1) to string2 (denoted by
000B41r 3                       ; addr2 u2).  Return -1 if string1 < string2, 0 if string1 = string2
000B41r 3                       ; and 1 if string1 > string2 (ASCIIbetical comparison).  A string
000B41r 3                       ; that entirely matches the beginning of the other string, but is
000B41r 3                       ; shorter, is considered less than the longer string.
000B41r 3                       ; """
000B41r 3               
000B41r 3               xt_compare:
000B41r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_4
000B44r 3               
000B44r 3                               ; Load the two string addresses into tmp1 and tmp2.
000B44r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
000B46r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2
000B48r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
000B4Ar 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2+1
000B4Cr 3  B5 06                        lda 6,x
000B4Er 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
000B50r 3  B5 07                        lda 7,x
000B52r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
000B54r 3                               ; The counts will be used in-place on the stack.
000B54r 3               
000B54r 3               @compare_loop:
000B54r 3                               ; Check to see if we are out of letters.
000B54r 3               
000B54r 3                               ; Check string1
000B54r 3  B5 04                        lda 4,x
000B56r 3  15 05                        ora 5,x
000B58r 3  F0 2C                        beq @str1_done
000B5Ar 3               
000B5Ar 3                               ; Check string2
000B5Ar 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
000B5Cr 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
000B5Er 3  F0 3A                        beq @greater    ; Str2 empty first
000B60r 3               
000B60r 3               @check_letter:
000B60r 3                               ; Both strings have at least one letter left.
000B60r 3                               ; Check the letters against each other.
000B60r 3  B2 rr                        lda (tmp1)
000B62r 3  D2 rr                        cmp (tmp2)
000B64r 3  90 26                        bcc @less
000B66r 3  D0 32                        bne @greater
000B68r 3               @next_letter:
000B68r 3                               ; Move both tmp pointers and decrement the counts
000B68r 3                               ; on the stack.
000B68r 3                               ; Increment tmp1
000B68r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp1
000B6Ar 3  D0 02                        bne @1
000B6Cr 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp1+1
000B6Er 3               @1:
000B6Er 3                               ; Increment tmp2
000B6Er 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp2
000B70r 3  D0 02                        bne @2
000B72r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp2+1
000B74r 3               @2:
000B74r 3                               ; Decrement count1 on the stack.
000B74r 3  B5 04                        lda 4,x
000B76r 3  D0 02                        bne @3
000B78r 3  D6 05                        dec 5,x
000B7Ar 3               @3:
000B7Ar 3  D6 04                        dec 4,x
000B7Cr 3               
000B7Cr 3                               ; Decrement count2 on the stack.
000B7Cr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
000B7Er 3  D0 02                        bne @4
000B80r 3  D6 01                        dec 1,x
000B82r 3               @4:
000B82r 3  D6 00                        dec 0,x
000B84r 3               
000B84r 3                               ; Loop around and check again.
000B84r 3  80 CE                        bra @compare_loop
000B86r 3               
000B86r 3               @str1_done:
000B86r 3                               ; String 1 is out of letters. Check string 2.
000B86r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
000B88r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
000B8Ar 3  F0 08                        beq @equal      ; Both out of letters
000B8Cr 3               
000B8Cr 3                               ; Falls into less (str1 is out but str2 has more)
000B8Cr 3               @less:
000B8Cr 3                               ; Return -1
000B8Cr 3  A9 FF                        lda #$FF
000B8Er 3  95 06                        sta 6,x
000B90r 3  95 07                        sta 7,x
000B92r 3  80 0C                        bra @done
000B94r 3               @equal:
000B94r 3                               ; Return 0
000B94r 3  74 06                        stz 6,x
000B96r 3  74 07                        stz 7,x
000B98r 3  80 06                        bra @done
000B9Ar 3               @greater:
000B9Ar 3                               ; Return 1
000B9Ar 3  A9 01                        lda #1
000B9Cr 3  95 06                        sta 6,x
000B9Er 3  74 07                        stz 7,x
000BA0r 3                               ; Falls into @done
000BA0r 3               @done:
000BA0r 3                               ; Remove all but the result from the stack.
000BA0r 3  8A                           txa
000BA1r 3  18                           clc
000BA2r 3  69 06                        adc #6
000BA4r 3  AA                           tax
000BA5r 3               
000BA5r 3  60           z_compare:      rts
000BA6r 3               
000BA6r 3               
000BA6r 3               
000BA6r 3               ; ## COMPILE_COMMA ( xt -- ) "Compile xt"
000BA6r 3               ; ## "compile,"  auto  ANS core ext
000BA6r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/COMPILEComma
000BA6r 3                       ; Compile the given xt in the current word definition. It is an
000BA6r 3                       ; error if we are not in the compile state. Because we are using
000BA6r 3                       ; subroutine threading, we can't use , (COMMA) to compile new words
000BA6r 3                       ; the traditional way. By default, native compiled is allowed, unless
000BA6r 3                       ; there is a NN (Never Native) flag associated. If not, we use the
000BA6r 3                       ; value NC_LIMIT (from definitions.tasm) to decide if the code
000BA6r 3                       ; is too large to be natively coded: If the size is larger than
000BA6r 3                       ; NC_LIMIT, we silently use subroutine coding. If the AN (Always
000BA6r 3                       ; Native) flag is set, the word is always natively compiled.
000BA6r 3                       ; """
000BA6r 3               
000BA6r 3               xt_compile_comma:
000BA6r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
000BA9r 3               
000BA9r 3                               ; See if this is an Always Native (AN) word by checking the
000BA9r 3                               ; AN flag. We need nt for this. First, save a copy of xt to
000BA9r 3                               ; the Return Stack
000BA9r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x                 ; MSB
000BABr 3  48                           pha
000BACr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
000BAEr 3  48                           pha                     ; LSB
000BAFr 3               
000BAFr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_int_to_name      ; ( xt -- nt )
000BB2r 3               
000BB2r 3                               ; See if this xt even has an nt.
000BB2r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
000BB4r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
000BB6r 3  D0 03                        bne @check_nt
000BB8r 3               
000BB8r 3                               ; No nt in dictionary. Just compile as a JSR.
000BB8r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @compile_as_jump
000BBBr 3               
000BBBr 3               @check_nt:
000BBBr 3                               ; put nt away for safe keeping
000BBBr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
000BBDr 3  85 rr                        sta tmptos
000BBFr 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
000BC1r 3  85 rr                        sta tmptos+1
000BC3r 3               
000BC3r 3                               ; status byte is one further down
000BC3r 3  F6 00                        inc 0,x
000BC5r 3  D0 02                        bne @1
000BC7r 3  F6 01                        inc 1,x                 ; ( nt -- nt+1 )
000BC9r 3               @1:
000BC9r 3  A1 00                        lda (0,x)
000BCBr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp3                ; keep copy of status byte for NN
