00109Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_tuck
0010A0r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_dabs
0010A3r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_less_number_sign
0010A6r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_number_sign_s
0010A9r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_rot
0010ACr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_sign
0010AFr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_number_sign_greater
0010B2r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_type
0010B5r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
0010B8r 3               
0010B8r 3  60           z_d_dot:        rts
0010B9r 3               
0010B9r 3               
0010B9r 3               
0010B9r 3               ; ## D_DOT_R ( d u -- ) "Print double right-justified u wide"
0010B9r 3               ; ## "d.r"  tested  ANS double
0010B9r 3                       ; """http://forth-standard.org/standard/double/DDotR"""
0010B9r 3                       ; Based on the Forth code
0010B9r 3                       ;  : D.R >R TUCK DABS <# #S ROT SIGN #> R> OVER - SPACES TYPE ;
0010B9r 3                       ; """
0010B9r 3               
0010B9r 3               xt_d_dot_r:
0010B9r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_3
0010BCr 3                               ; From the forth code:
0010BCr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_to_r
0010BFr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_tuck
0010C2r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_dabs
0010C5r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_less_number_sign
0010C8r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_number_sign_s
0010CBr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_rot
0010CEr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_sign
0010D1r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_number_sign_greater
0010D4r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_r_from
0010D7r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_over
0010DAr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_minus
0010DDr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_spaces
0010E0r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_type
0010E3r 3               
0010E3r 3  60           z_d_dot_r:      rts
0010E4r 3               
0010E4r 3               
0010E4r 3               
0010E4r 3               ; ## DROP ( u -- ) "Pop top entry on Data Stack"
0010E4r 3               ; ## "drop"  auto  ANS core
0010E4r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/DROP"""
0010E4r 3               xt_drop:
0010E4r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
0010E7r 3               
0010E7r 3  E8                           inx
0010E8r 3  E8                           inx
0010E9r 3               
0010E9r 3  60           z_drop:         rts
0010EAr 3               
0010EAr 3               
0010EAr 3               ; ## DUMP ( addr u -- ) "Display a memory region"
0010EAr 3               ; ## "dump"  tested  ANS tools
0010EAr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/tools/DUMP
0010EAr 3                       ;
0010EAr 3                       ; DUMP's exact output is defined as "implementation dependent".
0010EAr 3                       ; This is in assembler because it is
0010EAr 3                       ; useful for testing and development, so we want to have it work
0010EAr 3                       ; as soon as possible. Uses TMP2
0010EAr 3                       ; """
0010EAr 3               
0010EAr 3               xt_dump:
0010EAr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
0010EDr 3               @row:
0010EDr 3                               ; start counter for 16 numbers per row
0010EDr 3  A0 10                        ldy #16
0010EFr 3               
0010EFr 3                               ; We use TMP2 as the index for the ASCII characters
0010EFr 3                               ; that we print at the and of the hex block. We
0010EFr 3                               ; start saving them at HERE (CP)
0010EFr 3  64 rr                        stz tmp2
0010F1r 3               
0010F1r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_cr
0010F4r 3               
0010F4r 3                               ; print address number
0010F4r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
0010F6r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr byte_to_ascii
0010F9r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
0010FBr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr byte_to_ascii
0010FEr 3               
0010FEr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
001101r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
001104r 3               @loop:
001104r 3                               ; if there are zero bytes left to display, we're done
001104r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
001106r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
001108r 3  F0 39                        beq @all_printed
00110Ar 3               
00110Ar 3                               ; dump the contents
00110Ar 3  A1 02                        lda (2,x)
00110Cr 3  48                           pha                     ; byte_to_ascii destroys A
00110Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr byte_to_ascii
001110r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
001113r 3  68                           pla
001114r 3               
001114r 3                               ; Handle ASCII printing
001114r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr is_printable
001117r 3  B0 02                        bcs @printable
001119r 3  A9 2E                        lda #'.'                 ; Print dot if not printable
00111Br 3               @printable:
00111Br 3  5A                           phy                     ; save counter
00111Cr 3  A4 rr                        ldy tmp2
00111Er 3  91 rr                        sta (cp),y
001120r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp2
001122r 3  7A                           ply
001123r 3               
001123r 3                               ; extra space after eight bytes
001123r 3  C0 09                        cpy #9
001125r 3  D0 03                        bne @next_char
001127r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
00112Ar 3               
00112Ar 3               @next_char:
00112Ar 3  F6 02                        inc 2,x
00112Cr 3  D0 02                        bne @counter
00112Er 3  F6 03                        inc 3,x
001130r 3               
001130r 3               @counter:
001130r 3                               ; loop counter
001130r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
001132r 3  D0 02                        bne @1
001134r 3  D6 01                        dec 1,x
001136r 3               @1:
001136r 3  D6 00                        dec 0,x
001138r 3  88                           dey
001139r 3  D0 C9                        bne @loop               ; next byte
00113Br 3               
00113Br 3                               ; Done with one line, print the ASCII version of these
00113Br 3                               ; characters
00113Br 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
00113Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr print_ascii
001141r 3               
001141r 3  80 AA                        bra @row                ; new row
001143r 3               
001143r 3               @all_printed:
001143r 3                               ; See if there are any ASCII characters in the buffer
001143r 3                               ; left to print
001143r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp2
001145r 3  F0 06                        beq @done
001147r 3               
001147r 3                               ; In theory, we could try to make the ASCII part line
001147r 3                               ; up with the line before it. But that is a hassle (we
001147r 3                               ; use three bytes for each missed hex entry, and
001147r 3                               ; then there is the gap after eight entries) and it
001147r 3                               ; makes it harder to read. We settle for one extra
001147r 3                               ; space instead for the moment
001147r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
00114Ar 3  20 rr rr                     jsr print_ascii
00114Dr 3               @done:
00114Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_drop         ; one byte less than 4x INX
001150r 3  60           z_dump:         rts
001151r 3               
001151r 3               
001151r 3               print_ascii:
001151r 3                               ; Print the ASCII characters that we have saved from
001151r 3                               ; HERE (CP) to HERE plus whatever is in TMP2. This routine
001151r 3                               ; is not compiled (DUMP is probably never compiled anyway)
001151r 3                               ; but we keep it inside the scope of DUMP.
001151r 3  A0 00                        ldy #0
001153r 3               @ascii_loop:
001153r 3  B1 rr                        lda (cp),y
001155r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr emit_a
001158r 3  C8                           iny
001159r 3               
001159r 3                               ; extra space after eight chars
001159r 3  C0 08                        cpy #8
00115Br 3  D0 03                        bne @1
00115Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
001160r 3               @1:
001160r 3  C6 rr                        dec tmp2
001162r 3  D0 EF                        bne @ascii_loop
001164r 3               
001164r 3  60                           rts
001165r 3               
001165r 3               
001165r 3               
001165r 3               ; ## DUP ( u -- u u ) "Duplicate TOS"
001165r 3               ; ## "dup"  auto  ANS core
001165r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/DUP"""
001165r 3               xt_dup:
001165r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
001168r 3               
001168r 3  CA                           dex
001169r 3  CA                           dex
00116Ar 3               
00116Ar 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x         ; LSB
00116Cr 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
00116Er 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x         ; MSB
001170r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
001172r 3               
001172r 3  60           z_dup:          rts
001173r 3               
001173r 3               
001173r 3               ; ## ED ( -- u ) "Line-based editor"
001173r 3               ; ## "ed"  fragment  Tali Forth
001173r 3                       ; """Start the line-based editor ed6502. See separate file
001173r 3                       ; ed.asm or the manual for details.
001173r 3                       ; """
001173r 3               xt_ed:
001173r 3                           .ifdef ed6502
001173r 3                               jsr ed6502      ; kept in separate file
001173r 3                           .endif
001173r 3               
001173r 3  60           z_ed:           rts
001174r 3               
001174r 3               
001174r 3               ; ## EDITOR_WORDLIST ( -- u ) "WID for the Editor wordlist"
001174r 3               ; ## "editor-wordlist"  tested  Tali Editor
001174r 3                       ; """ Commonly used like `editor-wordlist >order` to add the editor
001174r 3                       ; words to the search order so they can be used.  This will need
001174r 3                       ; to be done before any of the words marked "Tali Editor" can be
001174r 3                       ; used.  See the tutorial on Wordlists and the Search Order for
001174r 3                       ; more information.
001174r 3               
001174r 3                       ;
001174r 3                       ; This is a dummy entry, the code is shared with ONE
001174r 3                       ; """
001174r 3               
001174r 3               
001174r 3               ; ## ELSE (C: orig -- orig) ( -- ) "Conditional flow control"
001174r 3               ; ## "else"  auto  ANS core
001174r 3                       ; """http://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ELSE
001174r 3                       ;
001174r 3                       ; The code is shared with ENDOF
001174r 3                       ; """
001174r 3               
001174r 3               xt_else:
001174r 3               xt_endof:
001174r 3                               ; Put an unconditional branch.
001174r 3  A0 rr                        ldy #>branch_runtime
001176r 3  A9 rr                        lda #<branch_runtime
001178r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr cmpl_subroutine
00117Br 3               
00117Br 3                               ; Put the address of the branch address on the stack.
00117Br 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_here
00117Er 3               
00117Er 3                               ; Use zero for the branch address for now.
00117Er 3                               ; THEN will fill it in later.
00117Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_zero
001181r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_comma
001184r 3               
001184r 3                               ; Get the address to jump to (just after the
001184r 3                               ; unconditional branch) for the IF to jump to
001184r 3                               ; when false.
001184r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_here
001187r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_rot
00118Ar 3               
00118Ar 3                               ; Update the original if 0branch address.
00118Ar 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_store
00118Dr 3               z_else:
00118Dr 3               z_endof:
00118Dr 3  60                           rts
00118Er 3               
00118Er 3               
00118Er 3               
00118Er 3               branch_runtime:
00118Er 3                       ; """Runtime component for a branch. Used by ELSE and ENDOF. This was
00118Er 3                       ; formally part of a separate word BRANCH which was later removed.
00118Er 3                       ; """
00118Er 3               
00118Er 3                               ; The address on the Return Stack points to the last byte
00118Er 3                               ; of the JSR address, one byte below the branch literal
00118Er 3  68                           pla
00118Fr 3  85 rr                        sta tmpbranch
001191r 3  68                           pla
001192r 3  85 rr                        sta tmpbranch+1
001194r 3               
001194r 3                               ; Keep in mind: the address we just popped points one byte
001194r 3                               ; lower than the branch literal we want to grab
001194r 3  A0 01                        ldy #1
001196r 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmpbranch),y  ; LSB
001198r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
00119Ar 3  C8                           iny
00119Br 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmpbranch),y  ; MSB
00119Dr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
00119Fr 3               
00119Fr 3  6C rr rr                     jmp (tmp1)
0011A2r 3               
0011A2r 3               
0011A2r 3               
0011A2r 3               ; ## EMIT ( char -- ) "Print character to current output"
0011A2r 3               ; ## "emit"  auto  ANS core
0011A2r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/EMIT
0011A2r 3                       ; Run-time default for EMIT. The user can revector this by changing
0011A2r 3                       ; the value of the OUTPUT variable. We ignore the MSB completely, and
0011A2r 3                       ; do not check to see if we have been given a valid ASCII character.
0011A2r 3                       ; Don't make this native compile.
0011A2r 3                       ; """
0011A2r 3               
0011A2r 3               xt_emit:
0011A2r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
0011A5r 3               
0011A5r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0011A7r 3  E8                           inx
0011A8r 3  E8                           inx
0011A9r 3               
0011A9r 3               emit_a:
0011A9r 3                       ; We frequently want to print the character in A without fooling
0011A9r 3                       ; around with the Data Stack. This is emit_a's job, which still
0011A9r 3                       ; allows the output to be vectored. Call it with JSR as you
0011A9r 3                       ; would XT_EMIT
0011A9r 3  6C rr rr                     jmp (output)            ; JSR/RTS
0011ACr 3               
0011ACr 3               z_emit:         ; never reached
0011ACr 3               
0011ACr 3               
0011ACr 3               
0011ACr 3               ; ## EMPTY_BUFFERS ( -- ) "Empty all buffers without saving"
0011ACr 3               ; ## "empty-buffers"  tested  ANS block ext
0011ACr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/block/EMPTY-BUFFERS"""
0011ACr 3               xt_empty_buffers:
0011ACr 3                               ; Set the buffer status to empty.
0011ACr 3  A0 2C                        ldy #buffstatus_offset
0011AEr 3  A9 00                        lda #0
0011B0r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y      ; Only LSB is used.
0011B2r 3               z_empty_buffers:
0011B2r 3  60                           rts
0011B3r 3               
0011B3r 3               
0011B3r 3               ; ## ENDCASE (C: case-sys -- ) ( x -- ) "Conditional flow control"
0011B3r 3               ; ## "endcase"  auto  ANS core ext
0011B3r 3                       ; """http://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ENDCASE"""
0011B3r 3               
0011B3r 3               xt_endcase:
0011B3r 3                               ; Postpone DROP to remove the item
0011B3r 3                               ; being checked.
0011B3r 3  A0 rr                        ldy #>xt_drop
0011B5r 3  A9 rr                        lda #<xt_drop
0011B7r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr cmpl_subroutine
0011BAr 3               
0011BAr 3                               ; There are a number of address (of branches that need their
0011BAr 3                               ; jump addressed filled in with the address of right here).
0011BAr 3                               ; Keep calling THEN to deal with them until we reach the
0011BAr 3                               ; 0 that CASE put on the stack at the beginning.
0011BAr 3               @endcase_loop:
0011BAr 3                               ; Check for 0 on the stack.
0011BAr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0011BCr 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
0011BEr 3  F0 05                        beq @done
0011C0r 3               
0011C0r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_then
0011C3r 3  80 F5                        bra @endcase_loop
0011C5r 3               @done:
0011C5r 3                               ; Remove the 0 from the stack.
0011C5r 3  E8                           inx
0011C6r 3  E8                           inx
0011C7r 3  60           z_endcase:      rts
0011C8r 3               
0011C8r 3               
0011C8r 3               
0011C8r 3               ; ## ENDOF (C: case-sys1 of-sys1-- case-sys2) ( -- ) "Conditional flow control"
0011C8r 3               ; ## "endof"  auto  ANS core ext
0011C8r 3                       ; """http://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ENDOF
0011C8r 3                       ; This is a dummy entry, the code is shared with ELSE
0011C8r 3                       ; """
0011C8r 3               
0011C8r 3               
0011C8r 3               ; ## ENVIRONMENT_Q  ( addr u -- 0 | i*x true )  "Return system information"
0011C8r 3               ; ## "environment?"  auto  ANS core
0011C8r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ENVIRONMENTq
0011C8r 3                       ;
0011C8r 3                       ; By ANS definition, we use upper-case strings here, see the
0011C8r 3                       ; string file for details. This can be realized as a high-level
0011C8r 3                       ; Forth word as
0011C8r 3                       ;
0011C8r 3                       ; : STRING_OF POSTPONE 2OVER POSTPONE COMPARE POSTPONE 0=
0011C8r 3                       ;    POSTPONE IF POSTPONE 2DROP ; IMMEDIATE COMPILE-ONLY
0011C8r 3                       ; HEX
0011C8r 3                       ; : ENVIRONMENT? ( C-ADDR U -- FALSE | I*X TRUE )
0011C8r 3                       ; CASE
0011C8r 3                       ; S" /COUNTED-STRING"    STRING_OF  7FFF TRUE ENDOF
0011C8r 3                       ; S" /HOLD"              STRING_OF    FF TRUE ENDOF
0011C8r 3                       ; S" /PAD"               STRING_OF    54 TRUE ENDOF ( 84 DECIMAL )
0011C8r 3                       ; S" ADDRESS-UNIT-BITS"  STRING_OF     8 TRUE ENDOF
0011C8r 3                       ; S" FLOORED"            STRING_OF FALSE TRUE ENDOF ( WE HAVE SYMMETRIC )
0011C8r 3                       ; S" MAX-CHAR"           STRING_OF   255 TRUE ENDOF
0011C8r 3                       ; S" MAX-D"              STRING_OF
0011C8r 3                                                    ; 7FFFFFFF. TRUE ENDOF
0011C8r 3                       ; S" MAX-N"              STRING_OF  7FFF TRUE ENDOF
0011C8r 3                       ; S" MAX-U"              STRING_OF  FFFF TRUE ENDOF
0011C8r 3                       ; S" MAX-UD"             STRING_OF
0011C8r 3                                                    ; FFFFFFFF. TRUE ENDOF
0011C8r 3                       ; S" RETURN-STACK-CELLS" STRING_OF    80 TRUE ENDOF
0011C8r 3                       ; S" STACK-CELLS"        STRING_OF    20 TRUE ENDOF ( FROM DEFINITIONS.ASM )
0011C8r 3                       ; ( DEFAULT ) 2DROP FALSE FALSE ( ONE FALSE WILL DROPPED BY ENDCASE )
0011C8r 3                       ; ENDCASE ;
0011C8r 3                       ;
0011C8r 3                       ; but that uses lots of memory and increases the start up time. This
0011C8r 3                       ; word is rarely used so we can try to keep it short at the expense
0011C8r 3                       ; of speed.
0011C8r 3                       ; """
0011C8r 3               
0011C8r 3               xt_environment_q:
0011C8r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
0011CBr 3               
0011CBr 3                               ; This code is table-driven: We walk through the list of
0011CBr 3                               ; strings until we find one that matches, and then we take
0011CBr 3                               ; the equivalent data from the results table. This is made
0011CBr 3                               ; a bit harder by the fact that some of these return a
0011CBr 3                               ; double-cell number and some a single-cell one.
0011CBr 3               
0011CBr 3                               ; We will walk through the table with variables that return
0011CBr 3                               ; a single-cell result
0011CBr 3  A0 00                        ldy #00                 ; counter for table
0011CDr 3               
0011CDr 3                               ; We use a flag on the the stack to signal if we have a single-cell
0011CDr 3                               ; or double-cell number. We use 0 to signal single-cell and 1 for
0011CDr 3                               ; double-cell.
0011CDr 3  5A                           phy
0011CEr 3               @table_loop:
0011CEr 3                               ; We arrived here with the address of the string to be checked
0011CEr 3                               ; on the stack. We make a copy. Index is in Y
0011CEr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_dup          ; ( addr u addr u ) 2DUP does not use Y
0011D1r 3               
0011D1r 3                               ; We do our work on the TOS to speed things up
0011D1r 3  CA                           dex
0011D2r 3  CA                           dex                     ; ( addr u addr u ? )
0011D3r 3               
0011D3r 3                               ; Get address of string to check from table
0011D3r 3  B9 rr rr                     lda env_table_single,y
0011D6r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0011D8r 3  C8                           iny
0011D9r 3  B9 rr rr                     lda env_table_single,y
0011DCr 3  95 01                        sta 1,x                 ; ( addr u addr u addr-t )
0011DEr 3  C8                           iny
0011DFr 3               
0011DFr 3                               ; See if this is the last entry. The LSB is still in A
0011DFr 3  15 00                        ora 0,x
0011E1r 3  F0 4D                        beq @table_done
0011E3r 3               
0011E3r 3                               ; We have a string entry. The address there is stored in
0011E3r 3                               ; old-style address format, that is, the first byte is the
0011E3r 3                               ; length of the string
0011E3r 3  5A                           phy                     ; save Y, which is used by COUNT
0011E4r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_count            ; ( addr u addr u addr-s u-s )
0011E7r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_compare          ; ( addr u f )
0011EAr 3  7A                           ply
0011EBr 3               
0011EBr 3                               ; If we found a match (flag is zero -- COMPARE is weird
0011EBr 3                               ; that way), return the result
0011EBr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0011EDr 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
0011EFr 3  F0 04                        beq @got_result
0011F1r 3               
0011F1r 3                               ; Flag is not zero, so not a perfect match, so try next
0011F1r 3                               ; word
0011F1r 3  E8                           inx                     ; DROP, now ( addr u )
0011F2r 3  E8                           inx
0011F3r 3               
0011F3r 3  80 D9                        bra @table_loop
0011F5r 3               
0011F5r 3               @got_result:
0011F5r 3                               ; We arrive here with ( addr u -1 ) and know that we've found
0011F5r 3                               ; a match. The index of the match+2 is in Y.
0011F5r 3  E8                           inx                     ; drop flag, now ( addr u )
0011F6r 3  E8                           inx
0011F7r 3  88                           dey                     ; go back to index we had
0011F8r 3  88                           dey
0011F9r 3               
0011F9r 3                               ; See if this is a single-cell word.
0011F9r 3  68                           pla
0011FAr 3  D0 0D                        bne @double_result
0011FCr 3               
0011FCr 3                               ; Single-cell result
0011FCr 3  B9 rr rr                     lda env_results_single,y
0011FFr 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
001201r 3  C8                           iny
001202r 3  B9 rr rr                     lda env_results_single,y
001205r 3  95 03                        sta 3,x                 ; ( res u )
001207r 3               
001207r 3  80 1F                        bra @set_flag
001209r 3               
001209r 3               @double_result:
001209r 3                               ; This is a double-celled result, which means we have to
001209r 3                               ; fool around with the index some more. We also need a
001209r 3                               ; further cell on the stack
001209r 3  CA                           dex                     ; ( addr u ? )
00120Ar 3  CA                           dex
00120Br 3               
00120Br 3                               ; We have 11 single-cell words we check, plus the 0000 as
00120Br 3                               ; a marker for the end of the table, so we arrive here
00120Br 3                               ; with Y as 22 or more. To get the index for the double-
00120Br 3                               ; cell words, we move the result
00120Br 3  98                           tya
00120Cr 3  38                           sec
00120Dr 3  E9 18                        sbc #24
00120Fr 3               
00120Fr 3                               ; We have four bytes per entry in the table, but the index
00120Fr 3                               ; keeps increasing by two, so we only have to multiply by
00120Fr 3                               ; two (shift left once) to get the right result
00120Fr 3  0A                           asl
001210r 3  A8                           tay
001211r 3               
001211r 3  B9 rr rr                     lda env_results_double,y
001214r 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
001216r 3  C8                           iny
001217r 3  B9 rr rr                     lda env_results_double,y
00121Ar 3  95 03                        sta 3,x                 ; ( res u ? )
00121Cr 3  C8                           iny
00121Dr 3               
00121Dr 3  B9 rr rr                     lda env_results_double,y
001220r 3  95 04                        sta 4,x
001222r 3  C8                           iny
001223r 3  B9 rr rr                     lda env_results_double,y
001226r 3  95 05                        sta 5,x                 ; ( res res ? )
001228r 3               
001228r 3                               ; fall through to @set_flag
001228r 3               @set_flag:
001228r 3  A9 FF                        lda #$ff
00122Ar 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
00122Cr 3  95 01                        sta 1,x                 ; ( res f )
00122Er 3               
00122Er 3  80 14                        bra @done
001230r 3               @table_done:
001230r 3                               ; We're done with a table, because the entry was a zero.
001230r 3                               ; We arrive here with ( addr u addr u 0 )
001230r 3               
001230r 3                               ; We take the flag from stack and increase it by one. If the
001230r 3                               ; flag is zero, we have just completed the single-cell number
001230r 3                               ; strings, so we in increase the flag and try again. Otherwise,
001230r 3                               ; we're done with the double-cell table without having found
001230r 3                               ; a match, and we're done
001230r 3  68                           pla
001231r 3  D0 09                        bne @no_match
001233r 3               
001233r 3                               ; Flag is zero, increase it to one and start over to check
001233r 3                               ; double-cell values
001233r 3  1A                           inc
001234r 3  48                           pha
001235r 3               
001235r 3  8A                           txa
001236r 3  18                           clc
001237r 3  69 06                        adc #6                  ; skip six bytes
001239r 3  AA                           tax                     ; ( addr u )
00123Ar 3               
00123Ar 3  80 92                        bra @table_loop
00123Cr 3               @no_match:
00123Cr 3                               ; Bummer, not found. We arrive here with
00123Cr 3                               ; ( addr u addr u 0 ) and need to return just a zero
00123Cr 3  8A                           txa
00123Dr 3  18                           clc
00123Er 3  69 0A                        adc #10
001240r 3  AA                           tax                     ; ( addr ) - not ( 0 ) !
001241r 3               
001241r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_false
001244r 3               @done:
001244r 3               z_environment_q:
001244r 3  60                           rts
001245r 3               
001245r 3               
001245r 3               ; Tables for ENVIRONMENT?. We use two separate ones, one for the single-cell
001245r 3               ; results and one for the double-celled results. The zero cell at the
001245r 3               ; end of each table marks its, uh, end. The strings themselves are defined
001245r 3               ; in strings.asm. Note if we add more entries to the single-cell table, we
001245r 3               ; have to adapt the result code for double printout, where we subtract 22
001245r 3               ; (two bytes each single-cell string and two bytes for the end-of-table
001245r 3               ; marker 0000
001245r 3               env_table_single:
001245r 3  rr rr rr rr          .word envs_cs, envs_hold, envs_pad, envs_aub, envs_floored
001249r 3  rr rr rr rr  
00124Dr 3  rr rr        
00124Fr 3  rr rr rr rr          .word envs_max_char, envs_max_n, envs_max_u, envs_rsc
001253r 3  rr rr rr rr  
001257r 3  rr rr rr rr          .word envs_sc, envs_wl, 0000
00125Br 3  00 00        
00125Dr 3               
00125Dr 3               env_table_double:
00125Dr 3  rr rr rr rr          .word envs_max_d, envs_max_ud, 0000
001261r 3  00 00        
001263r 3               
001263r 3               env_results_single:
001263r 3  FF 7F                .word $7FFF     ; /COUNTED-STRING
001265r 3  FF 00                .word $00FF     ; /HOLD
001267r 3  54 00                .word $0054     ; /PAD (this is 84 decimal)
001269r 3  08 00                .word $0008     ; ADDRESS-UNIT-BITS (keep "$" to avoid octal!)
00126Br 3  00 00                .word 0000      ; FLOORED ("FALSE", we have symmetric)
00126Dr 3  FF 00                .word $00FF     ; MAX-CHAR
00126Fr 3  FF 7F                .word $7FFF     ; MAX-N
001271r 3  FF FF                .word $FFFF     ; MAX-U
001273r 3  80 00                .word $0080     ; RETURN-STACK-CELLS
001275r 3  20 00                .word $0020     ; STACK-CELLS (from definitions.asm)
001277r 3  09 00                .word $0009     ; WORDLISTS
001279r 3               
001279r 3               env_results_double:
001279r 3  FF 7F FF FF          .word $7FFF, $FFFF      ; MAX-D
00127Dr 3  FF FF FF FF          .word $FFFF, $FFFF      ; MAX-UD
001281r 3               
001281r 3               
001281r 3               ; ## EQUAL ( n n -- f ) "See if TOS and NOS are equal"
001281r 3               ; ## "="  auto  ANS core
001281r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/Equal"""
001281r 3               
001281r 3               xt_equal:
001281r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
001284r 3               
001284r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x                 ; LSB
001286r 3  D5 02                        cmp 2,x
001288r 3  D0 0A                        bne @false
00128Ar 3               
00128Ar 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x                 ; MSB
00128Cr 3  D5 03                        cmp 3,x
00128Er 3  D0 04                        bne @false
001290r 3               
001290r 3  A9 FF                        lda #$ff
001292r 3  80 02                        bra @done
001294r 3               
001294r 3  A9 00        @false:         lda #0                  ; drop thru to done
001296r 3               
001296r 3  95 02        @done:          sta 2,x
001298r 3  95 03                        sta 3,x
00129Ar 3               
00129Ar 3  E8                           inx
00129Br 3  E8                           inx
00129Cr 3               
00129Cr 3  60           z_equal:        rts
00129Dr 3               
00129Dr 3               
00129Dr 3               
00129Dr 3               ; ## BLANK ( addr u -- ) "Fill memory region with spaces"
00129Dr 3               ; ## "blank"  auto  ANS string
00129Dr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/string/BLANK"""
00129Dr 3               xt_blank:
00129Dr 3                               ; We don't check for underflow here because
00129Dr 3                               ; we deal with that in FILL
00129Dr 3  CA                           dex
00129Er 3  CA                           dex
00129Fr 3  A9 20                        lda #AscSP
0012A1r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0012A3r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x
0012A5r 3               
0012A5r 3  80 06                        bra xt_fill     ; skip over code for ERASE
0012A7r 3               
0012A7r 3               
0012A7r 3               ; ## ERASE ( addr u -- ) "Fill memory region with zeros"
0012A7r 3               ; ## "erase"  auto  ANS core ext
0012A7r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ERASE
0012A7r 3                       ; Note that ERASE works with "address" units
0012A7r 3                       ; (bytes), not cells.
0012A7r 3                       ; """
0012A7r 3               
0012A7r 3               xt_erase:
0012A7r 3                               ; We don't check for underflow here because
0012A7r 3                               ; we deal with that in FILL
0012A7r 3  CA                           dex
0012A8r 3  CA                           dex
0012A9r 3  74 00                        stz 0,x
0012ABr 3  74 01                        stz 1,x
0012ADr 3               
0012ADr 3                               ; fall through to FILL
0012ADr 3               
0012ADr 3               ; ## FILL ( addr u char -- ) "Fill a memory region with a character"
0012ADr 3               ; ## "fill"  auto  ANS core
0012ADr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/FILL
0012ADr 3                       ; Fill u bytes of memory with char starting at addr. Note that
0012ADr 3                       ; this works on bytes, not on cells. On an 8-bit machine such as the
0012ADr 3                       ; 65c02, this is a serious pain in the rear. It is not defined what
0012ADr 3                       ; happens when we reach the end of the address space
0012ADr 3                       ; """
0012ADr 3               xt_fill:
0012ADr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_3
0012B0r 3               
0012B0r 3                               ; We use tmp1 to hold the address
0012B0r 3  B5 04                        lda 4,x         ; LSB
0012B2r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
0012B4r 3  B5 05                        lda 5,x
0012B6r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
0012B8r 3               
0012B8r 3                               ; We use tmp2 to hold the counter
0012B8r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
0012BAr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2
0012BCr 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
0012BEr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2+1
0012C0r 3               
0012C0r 3                               ; We use Y to hold the character
0012C0r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0012C2r 3  A8                           tay
0012C3r 3               @loop:
0012C3r 3                               ; Unfortunately, we also need to make sure that we don't
0012C3r 3                               ; write further than the end of the RAM. So RAM_END must
0012C3r 3                               ; be larger or equal to the current address
0012C3r 3  A9 80                        lda #>ram_end           ; MSB
0012C5r 3  C5 rr                        cmp tmp1+1
0012C7r 3  90 21                        bcc @done               ; RAM_END < TMP1, so leave
0012C9r 3  D0 06                        bne @check_counter      ; RAM_END is not smaller and not equal
0012CBr 3               
0012CBr 3  A9 00                        lda #<ram_end           ; LSB, because MSBs were equal
0012CDr 3  C5 rr                        cmp tmp1
0012CFr 3  90 19                        bcc @done               ; RAM_END < TMP1, so leave
0012D1r 3               
0012D1r 3               @check_counter:
0012D1r 3                               ; See if our counter has reached zero
0012D1r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp2
0012D3r 3  05 rr                        ora tmp2+1
0012D5r 3  F0 13                        beq @done
0012D7r 3               
0012D7r 3                               ; We're not in ROM and we still have stuff on the counter, so
0012D7r 3                               ; let's actually do what we came here to do
0012D7r 3  98                           tya
0012D8r 3  92 rr                        sta (tmp1)
0012DAr 3               
0012DAr 3                               ; Adjust the counter
0012DAr 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp2
0012DCr 3  D0 02                        bne @1
0012DEr 3  C6 rr                        dec tmp2+1
0012E0r 3  C6 rr        @1:               dec tmp2
0012E2r 3               
0012E2r 3                               ; Next address
0012E2r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp1
0012E4r 3  D0 DD                        bne @loop
0012E6r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp1+1
0012E8r 3               
0012E8r 3  80 D9                        bra @loop
0012EAr 3               
0012EAr 3               @done:
0012EAr 3                               ; Drop three cells off the Data Stack. This uses one byte
0012EAr 3                               ; less than six times INX
0012EAr 3  8A                           txa
0012EBr 3  18                           clc
0012ECr 3  69 06                        adc #6
0012EEr 3  AA                           tax
0012EFr 3               z_blank:
0012EFr 3               z_erase:
0012EFr 3  60           z_fill:         rts
0012F0r 3               
0012F0r 3               
0012F0r 3               
0012F0r 3               ; ## EXECUTE ( xt -- ) "Jump to word based on execution token"
0012F0r 3               ; ## "execute"  auto  ANS core
0012F0r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/EXECUTE"""
0012F0r 3               xt_execute:
0012F0r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
0012F3r 3               
0012F3r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr doexecute   ; do not combine to JMP (native coding)
0012F6r 3               
0012F6r 3  60           z_execute:      rts
0012F7r 3               
0012F7r 3               doexecute:
0012F7r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0012F9r 3  85 rr                        sta ip
0012FBr 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
0012FDr 3  85 rr                        sta ip+1
0012FFr 3               
0012FFr 3  E8                           inx
001300r 3  E8                           inx
001301r 3               
001301r 3                               ; we don't need a RTS here because we highjack the RTS of
001301r 3                               ; the word we're calling to get back to xt_execute
001301r 3  6C rr rr                     jmp (ip)
001304r 3               
001304r 3               ; end of doexecute
001304r 3               
001304r 3               
001304r 3               ; ## EXECUTE_PARSING ( addr u xt -- ) "Pass a string to a parsing word"
001304r 3               ; ## "execute-parsing"  auto  Gforth
001304r 3                       ; """https://www.complang.tuwien.ac.at/forth/gforth/Docs-html/The-Input-Stream.html
001304r 3                       ; Execute the parsing word defined by the execution token (xt) on the
001304r 3                       ; string as if it were passed on the command line. See the file
001304r 3                       ; tests/tali.fs for examples.
001304r 3                       ;
001304r 3                       ; Note that this word is coded completely
001304r 3                       ; different in its Gforth version, see the file execute-parsing.fs
001304r 3                       ; (in /usr/share/gforth/0.7.3/compat/ on Ubuntu 18.04 LTS) for details.
001304r 3                       ; """
001304r 3               xt_execute_parsing:
001304r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_3
001307r 3               
001307r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_input_to_r       ; save normal input for later
00130Ar 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_not_rote         ; -ROT ( xt addr u )
00130Dr 3               
00130Dr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x                 ; TOS is new ciblen
00130Fr 3  85 rr                        sta ciblen
001311r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
001313r 3  85 rr                        sta ciblen+1
001315r 3               
001315r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x                 ; NOS is new cib
001317r 3  85 rr                        sta cib
001319r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
00131Br 3  85 rr                        sta cib+1
00131Dr 3               
00131Dr 3  64 rr                        stz toin                ; Set >IN to zero
00131Fr 3  64 rr                        stz toin+1
001321r 3               
001321r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_drop         ; 2DROP ( xt )
001324r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_execute
001327r 3               
001327r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_r_to_input
00132Ar 3               
00132Ar 3               z_execute_parsing:
00132Ar 3  60                           rts
00132Br 3               
00132Br 3               
00132Br 3               ; ## EXIT ( -- ) "Return control to the calling word immediately"
00132Br 3               ; ## "exit"  auto  ANS core
00132Br 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/EXIT
00132Br 3                       ; If we're in a loop, we need to UNLOOP first and get everything
00132Br 3                       ; we we might have put on the Return Stack off as well. This should
00132Br 3                       ; be natively compiled.
00132Br 3                       ; """
00132Br 3               
00132Br 3               xt_exit:
00132Br 3  60                           rts             ; keep before z_exit
00132Cr 3               z_exit:                         ; never reached
00132Cr 3               
00132Cr 3               
00132Cr 3               
00132Cr 3               ; ## FALSE ( -- f ) "Push flag FALSE to Data Stack"
00132Cr 3               ; ## "false"  auto  ANS core ext
00132Cr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/FALSE"""
00132Cr 3               xt_false:
00132Cr 3  CA                           dex
00132Dr 3  CA                           dex
00132Er 3  74 00                        stz 0,x
001330r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x
001332r 3               
001332r 3  60           z_false:        rts
001333r 3               
001333r 3               
001333r 3               ; ## FETCH ( addr -- n ) "Push cell content from memory to stack"
001333r 3               ; ## "@"  auto  ANS core
001333r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/Fetch"""
001333r 3               xt_fetch:
001333r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
001336r 3               
001336r 3  A1 00                        lda (0,x)               ; LSB
001338r 3  A8                           tay
001339r 3  F6 00                        inc 0,x
00133Br 3  D0 02                        bne @1
00133Dr 3  F6 01                        inc 1,x
00133Fr 3               @1:
00133Fr 3  A1 00                        lda (0,x)               ; MSB
001341r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
001343r 3  94 00                        sty 0,x
001345r 3               
001345r 3  60           z_fetch:        rts
001346r 3               
001346r 3               
001346r 3               ; ## FIND ( caddr -- addr 0 | xt 1 | xt -1 ) "Find word in Dictionary"
001346r 3               ; ## "find"  auto  ANS core
001346r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/FIND
001346r 3                       ; Included for backwards compatibility only, because it still
001346r 3                       ; can be found in so may examples. It should, however, be replaced
001346r 3                       ; by FIND-NAME. Counted string either returns address with a FALSE
001346r 3                       ; flag if not found in the Dictionary, or the xt with a flag to
001346r 3                       ; indicate if this is immediate or not. FIND is a wrapper around
001346r 3                       ; FIND-NAME, we get this all over with as quickly as possible. See
001346r 3                       ; https://www.complang.tuwien.ac.at/forth/gforth/Docs-html/Word-Lists.html
001346r 3                       ; https://www.complang.tuwien.ac.at/forth/gforth/Docs-html/Name-token.html
001346r 3                       ; """
001346r 3               
001346r 3               xt_find:
001346r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
001349r 3               
001349r 3                               ; Save address in case conversion fails. We use the
001349r 3                               ; Return Stack instead of temporary variables like TMP1
001349r 3                               ; because this is shorter and anybody still using FIND
001349r 3                               ; can't be worried about speed anyway
001349r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x                 ; MSB
00134Br 3  48                           pha
00134Cr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x                 ; LSB
00134Er 3  48                           pha
00134Fr 3               
00134Fr 3                               ; Convert ancient-type counted string address to
00134Fr 3                               ; modern format
00134Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_count            ; ( caddr -- addr u )
001352r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_find_name        ; ( addr u -- nt | 0 )
001355r 3               
001355r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
001357r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
001359r 3  D0 0B                        bne @found_word
00135Br 3               
00135Br 3                               ; No word found. Return address of the string and a false
00135Br 3                               ; flag
00135Br 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_false            ; ( 0 0 )
00135Er 3               
00135Er 3                               ; The address needs to be restored.
00135Er 3  68                           pla                     ; LSB of address
00135Fr 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
001361r 3  68                           pla
001362r 3  95 03                        sta 3,x                 ; MSB of address
001364r 3               
001364r 3  80 27                        bra @done               ; ( addr 0 )
001366r 3               
001366r 3               @found_word:
001366r 3                               ; We don't need the address after all, dump it
001366r 3  68                           pla
001367r 3  68                           pla
001368r 3               
001368r 3                               ; We arrive here with ( nt ) on the TOS. Now we have to
001368r 3                               ; convert the return values to FIND's format
001368r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_dup              ; ( nt nt )
00136Br 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_name_to_int      ; ( nt xt )
00136Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_swap             ; ( xt nt )
001371r 3               
001371r 3  A0 00                        ldy #0                  ; Prepare flag
001373r 3               
001373r 3                               ; The flags are in the second byte of the header
001373r 3  F6 00                        inc 0,x
001375r 3  D0 02                        bne @1
001377r 3  F6 01                        inc 1,x                 ; ( xt nt+1 )
001379r 3               @1:
001379r 3  A1 00                        lda (0,x)               ; ( xt char )
00137Br 3  29 04                        and #IM
00137Dr 3  D0 08                        bne @immediate          ; bit set, we're immediate
00137Fr 3               
00137Fr 3  A9 FF                        lda #$FF                ; We're not immediate, return -1
001381r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
001383r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
001385r 3  80 06                        bra @done
001387r 3               
001387r 3               @immediate:
001387r 3  A9 01                        lda #1                  ; We're immediate, return 1
001389r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
00138Br 3  74 01                        stz 1,x
00138Dr 3               @done:
00138Dr 3  60           z_find:         rts
00138Er 3               
00138Er 3               
00138Er 3               
00138Er 3               ; ## FIND_NAME ( addr u -- nt|0 ) "Get the name token of input word"
00138Er 3               ; ## "find-name"  auto  Gforth
00138Er 3               
00138Er 3               xt_find_name:
00138Er 3                       ; """www.complang.tuwien.ac.at/forth/gforth/Docs-html/Name-token.html
00138Er 3                       ; Given a string, find the Name Token (nt) of a word or return
00138Er 3                       ; zero if the word is not in the dictionary. We use this instead of
00138Er 3                       ; ancient FIND to look up words in the Dictionary passed by
00138Er 3                       ; PARSE-NAME. Note this returns the nt, not the xt of a word like
00138Er 3                       ; FIND. To convert, use NAME>INT. This is a Gforth word. See
00138Er 3                       ; https://www.complang.tuwien.ac.at/forth/gforth/Docs-html/Name-token.html
00138Er 3                       ; FIND calls this word
00138Er 3                       ; """
00138Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
001391r 3               
001391r 3                               ; check for special case of an empty string (length zero)
001391r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
001393r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
001395r 3  D0 03                        bne @nonempty
001397r 3               
001397r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @fail_done
00139Ar 3               
00139Ar 3               @nonempty:
00139Ar 3                               ; Set up for traversing the wordlist search order.
00139Ar 3  64 rr                        stz tmp3                ; Start at the beginning
00139Cr 3               
00139Cr 3               @wordlist_loop:
00139Cr 3  A0 1E                        ldy #num_order_offset   ; Compare to byte variable #ORDER
00139Er 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp3
0013A0r 3  D1 rr                        cmp (up),y              ; Check to see if we are done
0013A2r 3  D0 03                        bne @have_string
0013A4r 3               
0013A4r 3                               ; We ran out of wordlists to search.
0013A4r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @fail_done
0013A7r 3               
0013A7r 3               @have_string:
0013A7r 3                               ; set up first loop iteration
0013A7r 3               
0013A7r 3                               ; Get the current wordlist id
0013A7r 3  18                           clc             ; SEARCH-ORDER is array of bytes.
0013A8r 3  69 1F                        adc #search_order_offset
0013AAr 3  A8                           tay
0013ABr 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y      ; Get the id byte, which is the offset
0013ADr 3                                               ; into the cell array WORDLISTS
0013ADr 3               
0013ADr 3                               ; Get the DP for that wordlist.
0013ADr 3  0A                           asl                     ; Turn offset into cells offset.
0013AEr 3  18                           clc
0013AFr 3  69 06                        adc #wordlists_offset
0013B1r 3  A8                           tay
0013B2r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0013B4r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
0013B6r 3  C8                           iny
0013B7r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0013B9r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
0013BBr 3               
0013BBr 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x                 ; Address of mystery string
0013BDr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2
0013BFr 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
0013C1r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2+1
0013C3r 3               
0013C3r 3               @loop:
0013C3r 3                               ; first quick test: Are strings the same length?
0013C3r 3  B2 rr                        lda (tmp1)
0013C5r 3  D5 00                        cmp 0,x
0013C7r 3  D0 54                        bne @next_entry
0013C9r 3               
0013C9r 3               @compare_string:
0013C9r 3                               ; are the same length, so we now have to compare each
0013C9r 3                               ; character
0013C9r 3               
0013C9r 3                               ; second quick test: Is the first character the same?
0013C9r 3  B2 rr                        lda (tmp2)      ; first character of mystery string
0013CBr 3               
0013CBr 3                               ; Lowercase the incoming charcter.
0013CBr 3  C9 5B                        cmp #$5B        ; ASCII '[' (one past Z)
0013CDr 3  B0 07                        bcs @compare_first
0013CFr 3  C9 41                        cmp #$41        ; ASCII 'A'
0013D1r 3  90 03                        bcc @compare_first
0013D3r 3               
0013D3r 3                               ; An uppercase letter has been located.  Make it
0013D3r 3                               ; lowercase.
0013D3r 3  18                           clc
0013D4r 3  69 20                        adc #$20
0013D6r 3               
0013D6r 3               @compare_first:
0013D6r 3  A0 08                        ldy #8          ; Offset in nt to name
0013D8r 3  D1 rr                        cmp (tmp1),y    ; first character of current word
0013DAr 3  D0 41                        bne @next_entry
0013DCr 3               
0013DCr 3                               ; String length is the same and the first character is the
0013DCr 3                               ; same. If the length of the string is 1, we're already done
0013DCr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0013DEr 3  3A                           dec
0013DFr 3  F0 2C                        beq @success
0013E1r 3               
0013E1r 3                               ; No such luck: The strings are the same length and the first
0013E1r 3                               ; char is the same, but the word is more than one char long.
0013E1r 3                               ; So we suck it up and compare every single character. We go
0013E1r 3                               ; from back to front, because words like CELLS and CELL+ would
0013E1r 3                               ; take longer otherwise. We can also shorten the loop by one
0013E1r 3                               ; because we've already compared the first char.
0013E1r 3               
0013E1r 3                               ; The string of the word we're testing against is 8 bytes down
0013E1r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp1
0013E3r 3  48                           pha             ; Preserve tmp1 on the return stack.
0013E4r 3  18                           clc
0013E5r 3  69 08                        adc #8
0013E7r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1        ; Reusing tmp1 temporarily for string check.
0013E9r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp1+1
0013EBr 3  48                           pha             ; Preserve tmp1+1 on the return stack.
0013ECr 3  69 00                        adc #0          ; we only need the carry
0013EEr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
0013F0r 3               
0013F0r 3  B4 00                        ldy 0,x         ; index is length of string minus 1
0013F2r 3  88                           dey
0013F3r 3               
0013F3r 3               @string_loop:
0013F3r 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp2),y    ; last char of mystery string
0013F5r 3               
0013F5r 3                               ; Lowercase the incoming charcter.
0013F5r 3  C9 5B                        cmp #$5B         ; ASCII '[' (one past Z)
0013F7r 3  B0 07                        bcs @check_char
0013F9r 3  C9 41                        cmp #$41        ; ASCII 'A'
0013FBr 3  90 03                        bcc @check_char
0013FDr 3               
0013FDr 3                               ; An uppercase letter has been located.  Make it
0013FDr 3                               ; lowercase.
0013FDr 3  18                           clc
0013FEr 3  69 20                        adc #$20
001400r 3               
001400r 3               @check_char:
001400r 3  D1 rr                        cmp (tmp1),y    ; last char of word we're testing against
001402r 3  D0 13                        bne @next_entry_tmp1
001404r 3               
001404r 3  88                           dey
001405r 3  D0 EC                        bne @string_loop
001407r 3               
001407r 3               @success_tmp1:
001407r 3  68                           pla             ; Restore tmp1 from the return stack.
001408r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
00140Ar 3  68                           pla
00140Br 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
00140Dr 3               
00140Dr 3               @success:
00140Dr 3                               ; The strings match. Put correct nt NOS, because we'll drop
00140Dr 3                               ; TOS before we leave
00140Dr 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp1
00140Fr 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
001411r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp1+1
001413r 3  95 03                        sta 3,x
001415r 3               
001415r 3  80 20                        bra @done
001417r 3               
001417r 3               @next_entry_tmp1:
001417r 3  68                           pla             ; Restore tmp1 from the return stack.
001418r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
00141Ar 3  68                           pla
00141Br 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
00141Dr 3               
00141Dr 3               @next_entry:
00141Dr 3                               ; Not the same, so we get the next word. Next header
00141Dr 3                               ; address is two bytes down
00141Dr 3  A0 02                        ldy #2
00141Fr 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp1),y
001421r 3  48                           pha
001422r 3  C8                           iny
001423r 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp1),y
001425r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
001427r 3  68                           pla
001428r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
00142Ar 3               
00142Ar 3                               ; If we got a zero, we've walked the whole Dictionary and
00142Ar 3                               ; return as a failure, otherwise try again
00142Ar 3  05 rr                        ora tmp1+1
00142Cr 3  D0 95                        bne @loop
00142Er 3               
00142Er 3                               ; Move on to the next wordlist in the search order.
00142Er 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp3
001430r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @wordlist_loop
001433r 3               
001433r 3               @fail_done:
001433r 3  74 02                        stz 2,x         ; failure flag
001435r 3  74 03                        stz 3,x
001437r 3               @done:
001437r 3  E8                           inx
001438r 3  E8                           inx
001439r 3               
001439r 3  60           z_find_name:    rts
00143Ar 3               
00143Ar 3               
00143Ar 3               
00143Ar 3               ; ## FLUSH ( -- ) "Save dirty buffers and empty buffers"
00143Ar 3               ; ## "flush"  auto  ANS block
00143Ar 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/block/FLUSH"""
00143Ar 3               xt_flush:
00143Ar 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_save_buffers
00143Dr 3               
00143Dr 3                               ; Set the buffer status to empty.
00143Dr 3  A0 2C                        ldy #buffstatus_offset
00143Fr 3  A9 00                        lda #0
001441r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y      ; Only LSB is used.
001443r 3               z_flush:
001443r 3  60                           rts
001444r 3               
001444r 3               
001444r 3               ; ## FM_SLASH_MOD ( d n1  -- rem n2 ) "Floored signed division"
001444r 3               ; ## "fm/mod"  auto  ANS core
001444r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/FMDivMOD
001444r 3                       ; Note that by default, Tali Forth uses SM/REM for most things.
001444r 3                       ;
001444r 3                       ; There are various ways to realize this. We follow EForth with
001444r 3                       ;    DUP 0< DUP >R  IF NEGATE >R DNEGATE R> THEN >R DUP
001444r 3                       ;    0<  IF R@ + THEN  R> UM/MOD R> IF SWAP NEGATE SWAP THEN
001444r 3                       ; See (http://www.forth.org/eforth.html). However you can also
001444r 3                       ; go FM/MOD via SM/REM (http://www.figuk.plus.com/build/arith.htm):
001444r 3                       ;     DUP >R  SM/REM DUP 0< IF SWAP R> + SWAP 1+ ELSE  R> DROP THEN
001444r 3                       ; """
001444r 3               
001444r 3               xt_fm_slash_mod:
001444r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_3
001447r 3               
001447r 3                               ; if sign of n1 is negative, negate both n1 and d
001447r 3  64 rr                        stz tmp2        ; default: n is positive
001449r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x         ; MSB of n1
00144Br 3  10 0E                        bpl @check_d
00144Dr 3               
00144Dr 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp2        ; set flag to negative for n1
00144Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_negate   ; NEGATE
001452r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_to_r     ; >R
001455r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_dnegate  ; DNEGATE
001458r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_r_from   ; R>
00145Br 3               
00145Br 3               @check_d:
00145Br 3                               ; If d is negative, add n1 to high cell of d
00145Br 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x         ; MSB of high word of d
00145Dr 3  10 0D                        bpl @multiply
00145Fr 3               
00145Fr 3  18                           clc
001460r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x         ; LSB of n1
001462r 3  75 02                        adc 2,x         ; LSB of dh
001464r 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
001466r 3               
001466r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x         ; MSB of n1
001468r 3  75 03                        adc 3,x         ; MSB of dh
00146Ar 3  95 03                        sta 3,x
00146Cr 3               
00146Cr 3               @multiply:
00146Cr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_um_slash_mod     ; ( d n1 -- rem n2 )
00146Fr 3               
00146Fr 3                               ; if n was negative, negate the result
00146Fr 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp2
001471r 3  F0 07                        beq @done
001473r 3               
001473r 3  E8                           inx             ; pretend that we SWAP
001474r 3  E8                           inx
001475r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_negate
001478r 3  CA                           dex
001479r 3  CA                           dex
00147Ar 3               @done:
00147Ar 3  60           z_fm_slash_mod: rts
00147Br 3               
00147Br 3               
00147Br 3               
00147Br 3               ; ## FORTH ( -- ) "Replace first WID in search order with Forth-Wordlist"
00147Br 3               ; ## "forth"  auto  ANS search ext
00147Br 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/search/FORTH"""
00147Br 3               xt_forth:
00147Br 3  A0 1F                        ldy #search_order_offset
00147Dr 3  A9 00                        lda #0          ; The WID for Forth is 0.
00147Fr 3               
00147Fr 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
001481r 3               z_forth:
001481r 3  60                           rts
001482r 3               
001482r 3               
001482r 3               ; This is a special jsr target to skip the zeroing of BLK at the beginning
001482r 3               ; of evaluate.  It's used by LOAD to allow setting BLK while the block is
001482r 3               ; being evaluated.  Evaluate's normal behavior is to zero BLK.
001482r 3               load_evaluate:
001482r 3                               ; Set a flag (using tmp1) to not zero BLK
001482r 3  A9 FF                        lda #$FF
001484r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
001486r 3  80 11                        bra load_evaluate_start
001488r 3               
001488r 3               ; ## EVALUATE ( addr u -- ) "Execute a string"
001488r 3               ; ## "evaluate"  auto  ANS core
001488r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/EVALUATE
001488r 3                       ; Set SOURCE-ID to -1, make addr u the input source, set >IN to zero.
001488r 3                       ; After processing the line, revert to old input source. We use this
001488r 3                       ; to compile high-level Forth words and user-defined words during
001488r 3                       ; start up and cold boot. In contrast to ACCEPT, we need to, uh,
001488r 3                       ; accept more than 255 characters here, even though it's a pain in
001488r 3                       ; the 8-bit.
001488r 3                       ; """
001488r 3               
001488r 3               xt_evaluate:
001488r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
00148Br 3               
00148Br 3                               ; Clear the flag to zero BLK.  Only LOAD will set the flag,
00148Br 3                               ; and will set the block number.
00148Br 3  64 rr                        stz tmp1
00148Dr 3               
00148Dr 3                               ; If u is zero (which can happen a lot for the user-defined
00148Dr 3                               ; words), just leave again
00148Dr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
00148Fr 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
001491r 3  D0 06                        bne _eval_got_work
001493r 3               
001493r 3  E8                           inx
001494r 3  E8                           inx
001495r 3  E8                           inx
001496r 3  E8                           inx
001497r 3               
001497r 3  80 42                        bra _eval_done
001499r 3               
001499r 3               ; Special entry point for LOAD to bypass the zeroing of BLK.
001499r 3               load_evaluate_start:
001499r 3               _eval_got_work:
001499r 3                               ; Save the current value of BLK on the return stack.
001499r 3  A0 01                        ldy #blk_offset+1
00149Br 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
00149Dr 3  48                           pha
00149Er 3  88                           dey
00149Fr 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0014A1r 3  48                           pha
0014A2r 3               
0014A2r 3                               ; See if we should zero BLK.
0014A2r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp1
0014A4r 3  D0 05                        bne @nozero
0014A6r 3               
0014A6r 3                               ; Set BLK to zero.
0014A6r 3                               ; lda #0        ; A is already zero from loading tmp1
0014A6r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
0014A8r 3  C8                           iny
0014A9r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
0014ABr 3               
0014ABr 3               @nozero:
0014ABr 3                               ; Save the input state to the Return Stack
0014ABr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_input_to_r
0014AEr 3               
0014AEr 3                               ; set SOURCE-ID to -1
0014AEr 3  A9 FF                        lda #$ff
0014B0r 3  85 rr                        sta insrc
0014B2r 3  85 rr                        sta insrc+1
0014B4r 3               
0014B4r 3                               ; set >IN to zero
0014B4r 3  64 rr                        stz toin
0014B6r 3  64 rr                        stz toin+1
0014B8r 3               
0014B8r 3                               ; move TOS and NOS to input buffers
0014B8r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0014BAr 3  85 rr                        sta ciblen
0014BCr 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
0014BEr 3  85 rr                        sta ciblen+1
0014C0r 3               
0014C0r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
0014C2r 3  85 rr                        sta cib
0014C4r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
0014C6r 3  85 rr                        sta cib+1
0014C8r 3               
0014C8r 3  E8                           inx             ; A clean stack is a clean mind
0014C9r 3  E8                           inx
0014CAr 3  E8                           inx
0014CBr 3  E8                           inx
0014CCr 3               
0014CCr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr interpret   ; ( -- )
0014CFr 3               
0014CFr 3                               ; restore variables
0014CFr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_r_to_input
0014D2r 3               
0014D2r 3                               ; Restore BLK from the return stack.
0014D2r 3  A0 00                        ldy #blk_offset
0014D4r 3  68                           pla
0014D5r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
0014D7r 3  C8                           iny
0014D8r 3  68                           pla
0014D9r 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
0014DBr 3               
0014DBr 3               _eval_done:
0014DBr 3  60           z_evaluate:     rts
0014DCr 3               
0014DCr 3

0014DCr 3               ; ## FORTH_WORDLIST ( -- u ) "WID for the Forth Wordlist"
0014DCr 3               ; ## "forth-wordlist"  auto  ANS search
0014DCr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/search/FORTH-WORDLIST"""
0014DCr 3                       ; This is a dummy entry, the actual code is shared with ZERO.
0014DCr 3               
0014DCr 3               
0014DCr 3               ; ## GET_CURRENT ( -- wid ) "Get the id of the compilation wordlist"
0014DCr 3               ; ## "get-current" auto ANS search
0014DCr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/search/GET-CURRENT"""
0014DCr 3               
0014DCr 3               xt_get_current:
0014DCr 3                               ; This is a little different than some of the variables
0014DCr 3                               ; in the user area as we want the value rather than
0014DCr 3                               ; the address.
0014DCr 3  CA                           dex
0014DDr 3  CA                           dex
0014DEr 3  A0 04                        ldy #current_offset
0014E0r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0014E2r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x         ; CURRENT is a byte variable
0014E4r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x         ; so the MSB is zero.
0014E6r 3               
0014E6r 3  60           z_get_current:  rts
0014E7r 3               
0014E7r 3               
0014E7r 3               
0014E7r 3               ; ## GET_ORDER ( -- wid_n .. wid_1 n) "Get the current search order"
0014E7r 3               ; ## "get-order" auto ANS search
0014E7r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/search/GET-ORDER"""
0014E7r 3               
0014E7r 3               xt_get_order:
0014E7r 3                               ; Get #ORDER - the number of wordlists in the search order.
0014E7r 3  A0 1E                        ldy #num_order_offset
0014E9r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0014EBr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
0014EDr 3  F0 16                        beq @done       ; If zero, there are no wordlists.
0014EFr 3               
0014EFr 3               @loop:
0014EFr 3                               ; Count down towards the front of the list.
0014EFr 3                               ; By decrementing first, we also turn the length into an offset.
0014EFr 3  C6 rr                        dec tmp1        ; Count down by bytes.
0014F1r 3               
0014F1r 3                               ; Get a pointer to the current wordlist, working back to front.
0014F1r 3  A9 1F                        lda #search_order_offset
0014F3r 3  18                           clc
0014F4r 3  65 rr                        adc tmp1
0014F6r 3  A8                           tay
0014F7r 3               
0014F7r 3                               ; Put that wordlist id on the stack.
0014F7r 3  CA                           dex
0014F8r 3  CA                           dex
0014F9r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
0014FBr 3  95 00                        sta 0,x         ; Search order array is bytes, so
0014FDr 3  74 01                        stz 1,x         ; put a zero in the high byte.
0014FFr 3               
0014FFr 3                               ; See if that was the last one to process (first in the list).
0014FFr 3  A9 00                        lda #0
001501r 3  C5 rr                        cmp tmp1
001503r 3  D0 EA                        bne @loop
001505r 3               
001505r 3               @done:
001505r 3                               ; Put the number of items on the stack.
001505r 3  CA                           dex
001506r 3  CA                           dex
001507r 3  A0 1E                        ldy #num_order_offset
001509r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y
00150Br 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
00150Dr 3  74 01                        stz 1,x         ; We only support 8 wordlists.
00150Fr 3               
00150Fr 3  60           z_get_order:    rts
001510r 3               
001510r 3               
001510r 3               
001510r 3               ; ## GREATER_THAN ( n n -- f ) "See if NOS is greater than TOS"
001510r 3               ; ## ">"  auto  ANS core
001510r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/more"""
001510r 3               
001510r 3               xt_greater_than:
001510r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
001513r 3               
001513r 3  A0 00                        ldy #0          ; default false
001515r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr compare_16bit
001518r 3               
001518r 3                               ; for signed numbers, NOS>TOS gives us Z=0 and N=1
001518r 3  F0 03                        beq @false
00151Ar 3  10 01                        bpl @false
00151Cr 3               
00151Cr 3                               ; true
00151Cr 3  88                           dey
00151Dr 3               @false:
00151Dr 3  98                           tya
00151Er 3               
00151Er 3  E8                           inx
00151Fr 3  E8                           inx
001520r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
001522r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
001524r 3               
001524r 3  60           z_greater_than: rts
001525r 3

001525r 3               ; ## HERE ( -- addr ) "Put Compiler Pointer on Data Stack"
001525r 3               ; ## "here"  auto  ANS core
001525r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/HERE
001525r 3                       ; This code is also used by the assembler directive ARROW
001525r 3                       ; ("->") though as immediate"""
001525r 3               xt_here:
001525r 3               xt_asm_arrow:

00152Dr 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
00152Fr 3

001537r 3               
001537r 3               ; ## HEXSTORE ( addr1 u1 addr2 -- u2 ) "Store a list of numbers"
001537r 3               ; ## "hexstore"  auto  Tali
001537r 3                       ; """Given a string addr1 u1 with numbers in the current base seperated
001537r 3                       ; by spaces, store the numbers at the address addr2, returning the
001537r 3                       ; number of elements. Non-number elements are skipped, an zero-length
001537r 3                       ; string produces a zero output.
001537r 3                       ; """
001537r 3               
001537r 3               xt_hexstore:
001537r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_3
00153Ar 3               
00153Ar 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_dup              ; Save copy of original address
00153Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_to_r         ; ( addr1 u1 ) ( R: addr2 addr2 )
001540r 3               
001540r 3               @loop:
001540r 3                               ; Loop until string is totally consumed
001540r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
001542r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
001544r 3  F0 36                        beq @done
001546r 3               
001546r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_cleave           ; ( addr1 u1 addr3 u3 ) ( R: addr2 addr2 )
001549r 3               
001549r 3                               ; Prepare the conversion of the number.
001549r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_to_r
