001E3Dr 3  A5 rr                        lda insrc               ; cheat: We only check LSB
001E3Fr 3  D0 2D                        bne @src_not_kbd
001E41r 3               
001E41r 3                               ; SOURCE-ID of zero means we're getting stuff from the keyboard
001E41r 3                               ; with ACCEPT, which wants the address of the current input
001E41r 3                               ; buffer NOS and the max number of characters to accept TOS
001E41r 3  CA                           dex
001E42r 3  CA                           dex
001E43r 3  CA                           dex
001E44r 3  CA                           dex
001E45r 3               
001E45r 3  A5 rr                        lda cib                 ; address of CIB is NOS
001E47r 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
001E49r 3  A5 rr                        lda cib+1
001E4Br 3  95 03                        sta 3,x
001E4Dr 3               
001E4Dr 3  64 rr                        stz ciblen              ; go in with empty buffer
001E4Fr 3  64 rr                        stz ciblen+1
001E51r 3               
001E51r 3  A9 FF                        lda #bsize              ; max number of chars is TOS
001E53r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
001E55r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x                 ; cheat: We only accept max 255
001E57r 3               
001E57r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_accept           ; ( addr n1 -- n2)
001E5Ar 3               
001E5Ar 3                               ; ACCEPT returns the number of characters accepted, which
001E5Ar 3                               ; belong in CIBLEN
001E5Ar 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
001E5Cr 3  85 rr                        sta ciblen
001E5Er 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
001E60r 3  85 rr                        sta ciblen+1            ; though we only accept 255 chars
001E62r 3               
001E62r 3                               ; make >IN point to beginning of buffer
001E62r 3  64 rr                        stz toin
001E64r 3  64 rr                        stz toin+1
001E66r 3               
001E66r 3  A9 FF                        lda #$FF                ; overwrite with TRUE flag
001E68r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
001E6Ar 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
001E6Cr 3               
001E6Cr 3  80 10                        bra @done
001E6Er 3               
001E6Er 3               @src_not_kbd:
001E6Er 3                               ; If SOURCE-ID doesn't return a zero, it must be a string in
001E6Er 3                               ; memory or a file (remember, no blocks in this version).
001E6Er 3                               ; If source is a string, we were given the flag -1 ($FFFF)
001E6Er 3  1A                           inc
001E6Fr 3  D0 08                        bne @src_not_string
001E71r 3               
001E71r 3                               ; Simply return FALSE flag as per specification
001E71r 3  CA                           dex
001E72r 3  CA                           dex
001E73r 3  74 00                        stz 0,x
001E75r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x
001E77r 3               
001E77r 3  80 05                        bra z_refill
001E79r 3               
001E79r 3               @src_not_string:
001E79r 3                               ; Since we don't have blocks, this must mean that we are trying
001E79r 3                               ; to read from a file. However, we don't have files yet, so we
001E79r 3                               ; report an error and jump to ABORT.
001E79r 3  A9 01                        lda #err_badsource
001E7Br 3  4C rr rr                     jmp error
001E7Er 3               @done:
001E7Er 3  60           z_refill:       rts
001E7Fr 3               
001E7Fr 3               
001E7Fr 3               
001E7Fr 3               ; ## REPEAT (C: orig dest -- ) ( -- ) "Loop flow control"
001E7Fr 3               ; ## "repeat"  auto  ANS core
001E7Fr 3                       ; """http://forth-standard.org/standard/core/REPEAT"""
001E7Fr 3               
001E7Fr 3               xt_repeat:
001E7Fr 3                               ; Run again first
001E7Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_again
001E82r 3               
001E82r 3                               ; Stuff HERE in for the branch address
001E82r 3                               ; to get out of the loop
001E82r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_here
001E85r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_swap
001E88r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_store
001E8Br 3               
001E8Br 3  60           z_repeat:       rts
001E8Cr 3               
001E8Cr 3               
001E8Cr 3               
001E8Cr 3               ; ## RIGHT_BRACKET ( -- ) "Enter the compile state"
001E8Cr 3               ; ## "]"  auto  ANS core
001E8Cr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/right-bracket
001E8Cr 3                       ; This is an immediate word.
001E8Cr 3                       ; """
001E8Cr 3               xt_right_bracket:
001E8Cr 3  A9 FF                        lda #$FF
001E8Er 3  85 rr                        sta state
001E90r 3  85 rr                        sta state+1
001E92r 3               z_right_bracket:
001E92r 3  60                           rts
001E93r 3               
001E93r 3               
001E93r 3               ; ## ROOT_WORDLIST ( -- u ) "WID for the Root (minimal) wordlist"
001E93r 3               ; ## "root-wordlist"  tested  Tali Editor
001E93r 3               xt_root_wordlist:
001E93r 3  CA                           dex             ; The WID for the Root wordlist is 3.
001E94r 3  CA                           dex
001E95r 3  A9 03                        lda #3
001E97r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
001E99r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x
001E9Br 3               
001E9Br 3               z_root_wordlist:
001E9Br 3  60                           rts
001E9Cr 3               
001E9Cr 3               
001E9Cr 3               ; ## ROT ( a b c -- b c a ) "Rotate first three stack entries downwards"
001E9Cr 3               ; ## "rot"  auto  ANS core
001E9Cr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/ROT
001E9Cr 3                       ; Remember "R for 'Revolution'" - the bottom entry comes out
001E9Cr 3                       ; on top!
001E9Cr 3                       ; """
001E9Cr 3               
001E9Cr 3               xt_rot:
001E9Cr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_3
001E9Fr 3               
001E9Fr 3  B4 05                        ldy 5,x         ; MSB first
001EA1r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
001EA3r 3  95 05                        sta 5,x
001EA5r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
001EA7r 3  95 03                        sta 3,x
001EA9r 3  94 01                        sty 1,x
001EABr 3               
001EABr 3  B4 04                        ldy 4,x         ; LSB next
001EADr 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
001EAFr 3  95 04                        sta 4,x
001EB1r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
001EB3r 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
001EB5r 3  94 00                        sty 0,x
001EB7r 3               
001EB7r 3  60           z_rot:          rts
001EB8r 3               
001EB8r 3               
001EB8r 3               
001EB8r 3               ; ## RSHIFT ( x u -- x ) "Shift TOS to the right"
001EB8r 3               ; ## "rshift"  auto  ANS core
001EB8r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/RSHIFT"""
001EB8r 3               xt_rshift:
001EB8r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_2
001EBBr 3               
001EBBr 3                               ; We shift maximal by 16 bits, mask everything else
001EBBr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
001EBDr 3  29 0F                        and #%00001111
001EBFr 3  F0 08                        beq @done               ; if 0 shifts, quit
001EC1r 3               
001EC1r 3  A8                           tay
001EC2r 3               @loop:
001EC2r 3  56 03                        lsr 3,x
001EC4r 3  76 02                        ror 2,x
001EC6r 3  88                           dey
001EC7r 3  D0 F9                        bne @loop
001EC9r 3               @done:
001EC9r 3  E8                           inx
001ECAr 3  E8                           inx
001ECBr 3               
001ECBr 3  60           z_rshift:       rts
001ECCr 3               
001ECCr 3               
001ECCr 3               ; ## S_BACKSLASH_QUOTE ( "string" -- )( -- addr u ) "Store string in memory"
001ECCr 3               ; ## "s\""  auto  ANS core
001ECCr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/Seq
001ECCr 3                       ; Store address and length of string given, returning ( addr u ).
001ECCr 3                       ; ANS core claims this is compile-only, but the file set expands it
001ECCr 3                       ; to be interpreted, so it is a state-sensitive word, which in theory
001ECCr 3                       ; are evil. We follow general usage. This is just like S" except
001ECCr 3                       ; that it allows for some special escaped characters.
001ECCr 3                       ; """
001ECCr 3               
001ECCr 3               xt_s_backslash_quote:
001ECCr 3                               ; tmp2 will be used to determine if we are handling
001ECCr 3                               ; escaped characters or not. In this case, we are,
001ECCr 3                               ; so set it to $FF (the upper byte will be used to
001ECCr 3                               ; determine if we just had a \ and the next character
001ECCr 3                               ; needs to be modifed as an escaped character).
001ECCr 3  A9 FF                        lda #$FF
001ECEr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2
001ED0r 3  64 rr                        stz tmp2+1
001ED2r 3               
001ED2r 3                               ; Now that the flag is set, jump into s_quote to process
001ED2r 3                               ; the string.
001ED2r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr s_quote_start
001ED5r 3               @done:
001ED5r 3               z_s_backslash_quote:
001ED5r 3  60                           rts
001ED6r 3               
001ED6r 3               
001ED6r 3               ; This is a helper function for s_backslash_quote to convert a character
001ED6r 3               ; from ASCII to the corresponding hex value, eg 'F'->15
001ED6r 3               convert_hex_value:
001ED6r 3               
001ED6r 3  C9 41                cmp #'A'
001ED8r 3  90 07                bcc @digit
001EDAr 3               
001EDAr 3                       ; It's A-F
001EDAr 3  29 DF                and #$DF                ; Make it uppercase.
001EDCr 3  38                   sec
001EDDr 3  E9 37                sbc #'7'                 ; gives value 10 for 'A'
001EDFr 3  80 03                bra @done
001EE1r 3               
001EE1r 3               @digit:
001EE1r 3                       ; It's 0-9
001EE1r 3  38                   sec
001EE2r 3  E9 30                sbc #'0'
001EE4r 3               
001EE4r 3               @done:
001EE4r 3  60                   rts
001EE5r 3               
001EE5r 3               
001EE5r 3               
001EE5r 3               ; ## SEARCH_WORDLIST ( caddr u wid -- 0 | xt 1 | xt -1) "Search for a word in a wordlist"
001EE5r 3               ; ## "search-wordlist" auto ANS search
001EE5r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/search/SEARCH_WORDLIST"""
001EE5r 3               
001EE5r 3               xt_search_wordlist:
001EE5r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_3
001EE8r 3               
001EE8r 3                               ; Set up tmp1 with the wordlist indicated by wid
001EE8r 3                               ; on the stack. Start by putting the base address
001EE8r 3                               ; of the wordlists in tmp2.
001EE8r 3  A5 rr                        lda up
001EEAr 3  18                           clc
001EEBr 3  69 06                        adc #wordlists_offset
001EEDr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2
001EEFr 3  A5 rr                        lda up+1
001EF1r 3  69 00                        adc #0          ; Adding carry
001EF3r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2+1
001EF5r 3               
001EF5r 3                               ; Add the wid (in cells) to the base address.
001EF5r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
001EF7r 3  0A                           asl             ; Convert wid to offset in cells (x2)
001EF8r 3  65 rr                        adc tmp2
001EFAr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2
001EFCr 3  90 02                        bcc @1
001EFEr 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp2+1      ; Propagate carry if needed.
001F00r 3               
001F00r 3                               ; tmp2 now holds the address of the dictionary pointer
001F00r 3                               ; for the given wordlist.
001F00r 3               @1:
001F00r 3                               ; Remove the wid from the stack.
001F00r 3  E8                           inx
001F01r 3  E8                           inx
001F02r 3               
001F02r 3                               ; check for special case of an empty string (length zero)
001F02r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
001F04r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
001F06r 3  D0 03                        bne @check_wordlist
001F08r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @done
001F0Br 3               
001F0Br 3               @check_wordlist:
001F0Br 3                               ; Check for special case of empty wordlist
001F0Br 3                               ; (dictionary pointer, in tmp2, is 0)
001F0Br 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp2
001F0Dr 3  05 rr                        ora tmp2+1
001F0Fr 3  D0 03                        bne @have_string
001F11r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @done
001F14r 3               
001F14r 3               @have_string:
001F14r 3                               ; set up first loop iteration
001F14r 3  B2 rr                        lda (tmp2)              ; nt of first word in Dictionary
001F16r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
001F18r 3               
001F18r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp2                ; Move to the upper byte
001F1Ar 3  D0 02                        bne @2
001F1Cr 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp2+1
001F1Er 3               @2:
001F1Er 3  B2 rr                        lda (tmp2)
001F20r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
001F22r 3               
001F22r 3                               ; Reuse tmp2 to hold the address of the mystery string.
001F22r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x                 ; Address of mystery string
001F24r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2
001F26r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
001F28r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2+1
001F2Ar 3               
001F2Ar 3               @loop:
001F2Ar 3                               ; first quick test: Are strings the same length?
001F2Ar 3  B2 rr                        lda (tmp1)
001F2Cr 3  D5 00                        cmp 0,x
001F2Er 3  D0 7B                        bne @next_entry
001F30r 3               
001F30r 3               @compare_string:
001F30r 3                               ; are the same length, so we now have to compare each
001F30r 3                               ; character
001F30r 3               
001F30r 3                               ; second quick test: Is the first character the same?
001F30r 3  B2 rr                        lda (tmp2)      ; first character of mystery string
001F32r 3               
001F32r 3                               ; Lowercase the incoming charcter.
001F32r 3  C9 5B                        cmp #$5B        ; ASCII '[' (one past Z)
001F34r 3  B0 07                        bcs @compare_first
001F36r 3  C9 41                        cmp #$41        ; ASCII 'A'
001F38r 3  90 03                        bcc @compare_first
001F3Ar 3               
001F3Ar 3                               ; An uppercase letter has been located.  Make it
001F3Ar 3                               ; lowercase.
001F3Ar 3  18                           clc
001F3Br 3  69 20                        adc #$20
001F3Dr 3               
001F3Dr 3               @compare_first:
001F3Dr 3  A0 08                        ldy #8          ; Offset in nt to name
001F3Fr 3  D1 rr                        cmp (tmp1),y    ; first character of current word
001F41r 3  D0 68                        bne @next_entry
001F43r 3               
001F43r 3                               ; string length are the same and the first character is the
001F43r 3                               ; same. If the length of the string is 1, we're already done
001F43r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
001F45r 3  3A                           dec
001F46r 3  F0 2C                        beq @success
001F48r 3               
001F48r 3                               ; No such luck: The strings are the same length and the first
001F48r 3                               ; char is the same, but the word is more than one char long.
001F48r 3                               ; So we suck it up and compare every single character. We go
001F48r 3                               ; from back to front, because words like CELLS and CELL+ would
001F48r 3                               ; take longer otherwise. We can also shorten the loop by one
001F48r 3                               ; because we've already compared the first char.
001F48r 3               
001F48r 3                               ; The string of the word we're testing against is 8 bytes down
001F48r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp1
001F4Ar 3  48                           pha             ; Preserve tmp1 on the return stack.
001F4Br 3  18                           clc
001F4Cr 3  69 08                        adc #8
001F4Er 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1        ; Reusing tmp1 temporarily for string check.
001F50r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp1+1
001F52r 3  48                           pha             ; Preserve tmp1+1 on the return stack.
001F53r 3  69 00                        adc #0          ; we only need the carry
001F55r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
001F57r 3               
001F57r 3  B4 00                        ldy 0,x         ; index is length of string minus 1
001F59r 3  88                           dey
001F5Ar 3               
001F5Ar 3               @string_loop:
001F5Ar 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp2),y    ; last char of mystery string
001F5Cr 3               
001F5Cr 3                               ; Lowercase the incoming charcter.
001F5Cr 3  C9 5B                        cmp #$5B         ; ASCII '[' (one past Z)
001F5Er 3  B0 07                        bcs @check_char
001F60r 3  C9 41                        cmp #$41        ; ASCII 'A'
001F62r 3  90 03                        bcc @check_char
001F64r 3               
001F64r 3                               ; An uppercase letter has been located.  Make it
001F64r 3                               ; lowercase.
001F64r 3  18                           clc
001F65r 3  69 20                        adc #$20
001F67r 3               @check_char:
001F67r 3  D1 rr                        cmp (tmp1),y    ; last char of word we're testing against
001F69r 3  D0 3A                        bne @next_entry_tmp1
001F6Br 3               
001F6Br 3  88                           dey
001F6Cr 3  D0 EC                        bne @string_loop
001F6Er 3               
001F6Er 3               @success_tmp1:
001F6Er 3  68                           pla             ; Restore tmp1 from the return stack.
001F6Fr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
001F71r 3  68                           pla
001F72r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
001F74r 3               
001F74r 3               @success:
001F74r 3                               ; The strings match. Drop the count and put correct nt TOS
001F74r 3  E8                           inx
001F75r 3  E8                           inx
001F76r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp1
001F78r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
001F7Ar 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp1+1
001F7Cr 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
001F7Er 3               
001F7Er 3                               ; Change the nt into an xt, but save a copy of the nt
001F7Er 3                               ; to look up whether the word is immediate or not.
001F7Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_dup              ; ( nt nt )
001F81r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_name_to_int      ; ( nt xt )
001F84r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_swap             ; ( xt nt )
001F87r 3               
001F87r 3  A0 00                        ldy #0                  ; Prepare flag
001F89r 3               
001F89r 3                               ; The flags are in the second byte of the header
001F89r 3  F6 00                        inc 0,x
001F8Br 3  D0 02                        bne @3
001F8Dr 3  F6 01                        inc 1,x                 ; ( xt nt+1 )
001F8Fr 3               @3:
001F8Fr 3  A1 00                        lda (0,x)               ; ( xt char )
001F91r 3  29 04                        and #IM
001F93r 3  D0 08                        bne @immediate          ; bit set, we're immediate
001F95r 3               
001F95r 3  A9 FF                        lda #$FF                ; We're not immediate, return -1
001F97r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
001F99r 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
001F9Br 3  80 28                        bra @done_nodrop
001F9Dr 3               
001F9Dr 3               @immediate:
001F9Dr 3  A9 01                        lda #1                  ; We're immediate, return 1
001F9Fr 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
001FA1r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x
001FA3r 3               
001FA3r 3  80 20                        bra @done_nodrop
001FA5r 3               
001FA5r 3               @next_entry_tmp1:
001FA5r 3  68                           pla             ; Restore tmp1 from the return stack.
001FA6r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
001FA8r 3  68                           pla
001FA9r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
001FABr 3               @next_entry:
001FABr 3                               ; Not the same, so we get the next word. Next header
001FABr 3                               ; address is two bytes down
001FABr 3  A0 02                        ldy #2
001FADr 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp1),y
001FAFr 3  48                           pha
001FB0r 3  C8                           iny
001FB1r 3  B1 rr                        lda (tmp1),y
001FB3r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
001FB5r 3  68                           pla
001FB6r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
001FB8r 3               
001FB8r 3                               ; If we got a zero, we've walked the whole Dictionary and
001FB8r 3                               ; return as a failure, otherwise try again
001FB8r 3  05 rr                        ora tmp1+1
001FBAr 3  F0 03                        beq @fail_done
001FBCr 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @loop
001FBFr 3               
001FBFr 3               @fail_done:
001FBFr 3  74 02                        stz 2,x         ; failure flag
001FC1r 3  74 03                        stz 3,x
001FC3r 3               @done:
001FC3r 3  E8                           inx
001FC4r 3  E8                           inx
001FC5r 3               @done_nodrop:
001FC5r 3               z_search_wordlist:
001FC5r 3  60                           rts
001FC6r 3               
001FC6r 3               
001FC6r 3               
001FC6r 3               ; ## SEE ( "name" -- ) "Print information about a Forth word"
001FC6r 3               ; ## "see" tested  ANS tools
001FC6r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/tools/SEE
001FC6r 3                       ; SEE takes the name of a word and prints its name token (nt),
001FC6r 3                       ; execution token (xt), size in bytes, flags used, and then dumps the
001FC6r 3                       ; code and disassembles it.
001FC6r 3                       ; """
001FC6r 3               
001FC6r 3               xt_see:
001FC6r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_parse_name       ; ( addr u )
001FC9r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_find_name        ; ( nt | 0 )
001FCCr 3               
001FCCr 3                               ; If we got back a zero we don't know that word and so we quit
001FCCr 3                               ; with an error
001FCCr 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
001FCEr 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
001FD0r 3  D0 05                        bne @1
001FD2r 3               
001FD2r 3  A9 05                        lda #err_noname
001FD4r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp error
001FD7r 3               @1:
001FD7r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_cr
001FDAr 3               
001FDAr 3                               ; We have a legal word, so let's get serious. Save the current
001FDAr 3                               ; number base and use hexadecimal instead.
001FDAr 3  A5 rr                        lda base
001FDCr 3  48                           pha
001FDDr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_hex
001FE0r 3               
001FE0r 3  A9 0A                        lda #str_see_nt
001FE2r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr print_string_no_lf
001FE5r 3               
001FE5r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_dup              ; ( nt nt )
001FE8r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_u_dot
001FEBr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space            ; ( nt )
001FEEr 3               
001FEEr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_dup              ; ( nt nt )
001FF1r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_name_to_int      ; ( nt xt )
001FF4r 3               
001FF4r 3  A9 0B                        lda #str_see_xt
001FF6r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr print_string_no_lf
001FF9r 3               
001FF9r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_dup              ; ( nt xt xt )
001FFCr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_u_dot
001FFFr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_cr               ; ( nt xt )
002002r 3               
002002r 3                               ; We print letters for flags and then later follow it with 1 or
002002r 3                               ; 0 to mark if which flag is set
002002r 3  A9 09                        lda #str_see_flags
002004r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr print_string_no_lf
002007r 3               
002007r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_over             ; ( nt xt nt )
00200Ar 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_one_plus         ; ( nt xt nt+1 )
00200Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_fetch            ; ( nt xt flags )
002010r 3               
002010r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
002012r 3               
002012r 3                               ; This is crude, but for the moment it is good enough
002012r 3  A0 06                        ldy #6                  ; Not all bits are used
002014r 3               @flag_loop:
002014r 3  48                           pha
002015r 3  29 01                        and #%00000001
002017r 3  18                           clc
002018r 3  69 30                        adc #$30                ; ASCII "0"
00201Ar 3  20 rr rr                     jsr emit_a
00201Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
002020r 3               
002020r 3  68                           pla
002021r 3  6A                           ror                     ; Next flag
002022r 3               
002022r 3  88                           dey
002023r 3  D0 EF                        bne @flag_loop
002025r 3               
002025r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_cr
002028r 3               
002028r 3  E8                           inx
002029r 3  E8                           inx                     ; ( nt xt )
00202Ar 3               
00202Ar 3                               ; Figure out the size
00202Ar 3  A9 0C                        lda #str_see_size
00202Cr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr print_string_no_lf
00202Fr 3               
00202Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_swap             ; ( xt nt )
002032r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_wordsize         ; ( xt u )
002035r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_dup              ; ( xt u u ) for DUMP and DISASM
002038r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_decimal
00203Br 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_u_dot            ; ( xt u )
00203Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_hex
002041r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_cr
002044r 3               
002044r 3                               ; Dump hex and disassemble
002044r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_two_dup          ; ( xt u xt u )
002047r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_dump
00204Ar 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_cr
00204Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_disasm
002050r 3               
002050r 3  68                           pla
002051r 3  85 rr                        sta base
002053r 3               
002053r 3  60           z_see:          rts
002054r 3               
002054r 3               
002054r 3               
002054r 3               ; ## SET_CURRENT ( wid -- ) "Set the compilation wordlist"
002054r 3               ; ## "set-current" auto ANS search
002054r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/search/SET-CURRENT"""
002054r 3               
002054r 3               xt_set_current:
002054r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
002057r 3               
002057r 3                               ; Save the value from the data stack.
002057r 3  A0 04                        ldy #current_offset
002059r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x         ; CURRENT is byte variable
00205Br 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y      ; so only the LSB is used.
00205Dr 3               
00205Dr 3  E8                           inx
00205Er 3  E8                           inx
00205Fr 3               
00205Fr 3  60           z_set_current:  rts
002060r 3               
002060r 3               
002060r 3               
002060r 3               ; ## SET_ORDER ( wid_n .. wid_1 n -- ) "Set the current search order"
002060r 3               ; ## "set-order" auto ANS search
002060r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/search/SET-ORDER"""
002060r 3               
002060r 3               xt_set_order:
002060r 3                               ; Test for -1 TOS
002060r 3  A9 FF                        lda #$FF
002062r 3  D5 01                        cmp 1,x
002064r 3  D0 12                        bne @start
002066r 3  D5 00                        cmp 0,x
002068r 3  D0 0E                        bne @start
00206Ar 3               
00206Ar 3                               ; There is a -1 TOS.  Replace it with the default
00206Ar 3                               ; search order, which is just the FORTH-WORDLIST.
00206Ar 3  CA                           dex             ; Make room for the count.
00206Br 3  CA                           dex
00206Cr 3  74 03                        stz 3,x         ; ROOT-WORDLIST is 3
00206Er 3  A9 03                        lda #3
002070r 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
002072r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x         ; Count is 1.
002074r 3  A9 01                        lda #1
002076r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
002078r 3               
002078r 3                               ; Continue processing with ( forth-wordlist 1 -- )
002078r 3               @start:
002078r 3                               ; Set #ORDER - the number of wordlists in the search order.
002078r 3  A0 1E                        ldy #num_order_offset
00207Ar 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
00207Cr 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y      ; #ORDER is a byte variable.
00207Er 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1        ; Save a copy for zero check and looping.
002080r 3                                               ; Only the low byte is saved in tmp1 as
002080r 3                                               ; only 8 wordlists are allowed.
002080r 3               
002080r 3  E8                           inx             ; Drop the count off the data stack.
002081r 3  E8                           inx
002082r 3               
002082r 3                               ; Check if there are zero wordlists.
002082r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp1
002084r 3  F0 0D                        beq @done       ; If zero, there are no wordlists.
002086r 3               
002086r 3                               ; Move the wordlist ids from the data stack to the search order.
002086r 3  A0 1F                        ldy #search_order_offset
002088r 3               @loop:
002088r 3                               ; Move one wordlist id over into the search order.
002088r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x         ; The search order is a byte array
00208Ar 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y      ; so only save the LSB
00208Cr 3  C8                           iny
00208Dr 3               
00208Dr 3                               ; Remove it from the data stack.
00208Dr 3  E8                           inx
00208Er 3  E8                           inx
00208Fr 3               
00208Fr 3                               ; See if that was the last one to process (first in the list).
00208Fr 3  C6 rr                        dec tmp1
002091r 3  D0 F5                        bne @loop
002093r 3               
002093r 3               @done:
002093r 3  60           z_set_order:    rts
002094r 3               
002094r 3               
002094r 3               
002094r 3               
002094r 3               ; ## S_QUOTE ( "string" -- )( -- addr u ) "Store string in memory"
002094r 3               ; ## "s""  auto  ANS core
002094r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/Sq
002094r 3                       ; Store address and length of string given, returning ( addr u ).
002094r 3                       ; ANS core claims this is compile-only, but the file set expands it
002094r 3                       ; to be interpreted, so it is a state-sensitive word, which in theory
002094r 3                       ; are evil. We follow general usage.
002094r 3                       ;
002094r 3                       ; Can also be realized as
002094r 3                       ;     : S" [CHAR] " PARSE POSTPONE SLITERAL ; IMMEDIATE
002094r 3                       ; but it is used so much we want it in code.
002094r 3                       ; """
002094r 3               
002094r 3               xt_s_quote:
002094r 3                               ; tmp2 will be used to determine if we are handling
002094r 3                               ; escaped characters or not.  In this case, we are
002094r 3                               ; not, so set it to zero.
002094r 3  64 rr                        stz tmp2
002096r 3  64 rr                        stz tmp2+1
002098r 3               
002098r 3               s_quote_start:
002098r 3                               ; Make room on the data stack for the address.
002098r 3  CA                           dex
002099r 3  CA                           dex
00209Ar 3                               ; Make room on the data stack for the count.
00209Ar 3  CA                           dex
00209Br 3  CA                           dex
00209Cr 3               
00209Cr 3                               ; Put a jmp over the string data with address to be filled
00209Cr 3                               ; in later.
00209Cr 3  A9 4C                        lda #$4C
00209Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr cmpl_a
0020A1r 3               
0020A1r 3                               ; Address to be filled in later, just use $4C for the moment
0020A1r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr cmpl_a
0020A4r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr cmpl_a
0020A7r 3               
0020A7r 3                               ; Save the current value of HERE on the data stack for the
0020A7r 3                               ; address of the string.
0020A7r 3  A5 rr                        lda cp
0020A9r 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
0020ABr 3  A5 rr                        lda cp+1
0020ADr 3  95 03                        sta 3,x
0020AFr 3               
0020AFr 3               @savechars_loop:
0020AFr 3                               ; Start saving the string into the dictionary up to the
0020AFr 3                               ; ending double quote. First, check to see if the input
0020AFr 3                               ; buffer is empty.
0020AFr 3  A5 rr                        lda toin+1              ; MSB
0020B1r 3  C5 rr                        cmp ciblen+1
0020B3r 3  90 2A                        bcc @input_fine         ; unsigned comparison
0020B5r 3               
0020B5r 3  A5 rr                        lda toin                ; LSB
0020B7r 3  C5 rr                        cmp ciblen
0020B9r 3  90 24                        bcc @input_fine
0020BBr 3               
0020BBr 3                               ; Input buffer is empty. Refill it. Refill calls accept,
0020BBr 3                               ; which uses tmp2 and tmp3. Save and restore them.
0020BBr 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp2
0020BDr 3  48                           pha
0020BEr 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp2+1
0020C0r 3  48                           pha
0020C1r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp3    ; Only tmp3 used, so don't bother with tmp3+1
0020C3r 3  48                           pha
0020C4r 3               
0020C4r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_refill           ; ( -- f )
0020C7r 3               
0020C7r 3  68                           pla
0020C8r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp3
0020CAr 3  68                           pla
0020CBr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2+1
0020CDr 3  68                           pla
0020CEr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2
0020D0r 3               
0020D0r 3                               ; Check result of refill.
0020D0r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0020D2r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
0020D4r 3  D0 05                        bne @refill_ok
0020D6r 3               
0020D6r 3                               ; Something when wrong with refill.
0020D6r 3  A9 06                        lda #err_refill
0020D8r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp error
0020DBr 3               
0020DBr 3               @refill_ok:
0020DBr 3                               ; Remove the refill flag from the data stack.
0020DBr 3  E8                           inx
0020DCr 3  E8                           inx
0020DDr 3               
0020DDr 3                               ; For refill success, jump back up to the empty check, just in
0020DDr 3                               ; case refill gave us an empty buffer (eg. empty/blank line of
0020DDr 3                               ; input)
0020DDr 3  80 D0                        bra @savechars_loop
0020DFr 3               
0020DFr 3               @input_fine:
0020DFr 3                               ; There should be at least one valid char to use.
0020DFr 3                               ; Calculate it's address at CIB+TOIN into tmp1
0020DFr 3  A5 rr                        lda cib
0020E1r 3  18                           clc
0020E2r 3  65 rr                        adc toin        ; LSB
0020E4r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
0020E6r 3  A5 rr                        lda cib+1
0020E8r 3  65 rr                        adc toin+1      ; MSB
0020EAr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
0020ECr 3               
0020ECr 3                               ; Get the character
0020ECr 3  B2 rr                        lda (tmp1)
0020EEr 3               
0020EEr 3                               ; Check to see if we are handling escaped characters.
0020EEr 3  24 rr                        bit tmp2
0020F0r 3  30 03                        bmi @handle_escapes    ; Only checking bit 7
0020F2r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @regular_char
0020F5r 3               
0020F5r 3               @handle_escapes:
0020F5r 3                               ; We are handling escaped characters.  See if we have
0020F5r 3                               ; already seen the backslash.
0020F5r 3  24 rr                        bit tmp2+1
0020F7r 3  30 03                        bmi @escaped
0020F9r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @not_escaped
0020FCr 3               
0020FCr 3               @escaped:
0020FCr 3               
0020FCr 3                               ; We have seen a backslash (previous character). Check to see if
0020FCr 3                               ; we are in the middle of a \x sequence (bit 6 of tmp2+1 will
0020FCr 3                               ; be clear in that case )
0020FCr 3  70 22                        bvs @check_esc_chars
0020FEr 3               
0020FEr 3                               ; We are in the middle of a \x sequence. Check to see if we
0020FEr 3                               ; are on the first or second digit.
0020FEr 3  A9 01                        lda #1
002100r 3  24 rr                        bit tmp2+1
002102r 3  D0 10                        bne @esc_x_second_digit
002104r 3               
002104r 3                               ; First digit.
002104r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp2+1  ; Adjust flag for second digit next time.
002106r 3  B2 rr                        lda (tmp1)  ; Get the char again.
002108r 3               
002108r 3                               ; Convert to hex
002108r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr convert_hex_value
00210Br 3               
00210Br 3                               ; This is the upper nybble, so move it up.
00210Br 3  0A                           asl
00210Cr 3  0A                           asl
00210Dr 3  0A                           asl
00210Er 3  0A                           asl
00210Fr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp3    ; Save it for later.
002111r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @next_character
002114r 3               
002114r 3               @esc_x_second_digit:
002114r 3               
002114r 3                               ; We are on the second hex digit of a \x sequence. Clear the
002114r 3                               ; escaped character flag (because we are handling it right
002114r 3                               ; here)
002114r 3  64 rr                        stz tmp2+1
002116r 3  B2 rr                        lda (tmp1)
002118r 3               
002118r 3                               ; Convert to hex, combine with value in tmp3
002118r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr convert_hex_value
00211Br 3  05 rr                        ora tmp3
00211Dr 3               
00211Dr 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @save_character
002120r 3               
002120r 3               @check_esc_chars:
002120r 3                               ; Clear the escaped character flag (because we are
002120r 3                               ; handling it right here)
002120r 3  64 rr                        stz tmp2+1
002122r 3               
002122r 3                               ; Process the escaped character
002122r 3               @check_esc_a:
002122r 3  C9 61                        cmp #'a'
002124r 3  D0 05                        bne @check_esc_b
002126r 3               
002126r 3                               ; BEL (ASCII value 7)
002126r 3  A9 07                        lda #7
002128r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @save_character
00212Br 3               
00212Br 3               @check_esc_b:
00212Br 3  C9 62                        cmp #'b'
00212Dr 3  D0 05                        bne @check_esc_e
00212Fr 3               
00212Fr 3                               ; Backspace (ASCII value 8)
00212Fr 3  A9 08                        lda #8
002131r 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @save_character
002134r 3               
002134r 3               @check_esc_e:
002134r 3  C9 65                        cmp #'e'
002136r 3  D0 04                        bne @check_esc_f
002138r 3               
002138r 3                               ; ESC (ASCII value 27)
002138r 3  A9 1B                        lda #27
00213Ar 3  80 75                        bra @save_character
00213Cr 3               
00213Cr 3               @check_esc_f:
00213Cr 3  C9 66                        cmp #'f'
00213Er 3  D0 04                        bne @check_esc_l
002140r 3               
002140r 3                               ; FF (ASCII value 12)
002140r 3  A9 0C                        lda #12
002142r 3  80 6D                        bra @save_character
002144r 3               
002144r 3               @check_esc_l:
002144r 3  C9 6C                        cmp #'l'
002146r 3  D0 04                        bne @check_esc_m
002148r 3               
002148r 3                               ; LF (ASCII value 10)
002148r 3  A9 0A                        lda #10
00214Ar 3  80 65                        bra @save_character
00214Cr 3               
00214Cr 3               @check_esc_m:
00214Cr 3                               ; This one is not like the others because we save two
00214Cr 3                               ; characters
00214Cr 3  C9 6D                        cmp #'m'
00214Er 3  D0 09                        bne @check_esc_n
002150r 3               
002150r 3                               ; CR/LF pair (ASCII values 13, 10)
002150r 3  A9 0D                        lda #13
002152r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr cmpl_a
002155r 3  A9 0A                        lda #10
002157r 3  80 58                        bra @save_character
002159r 3               
002159r 3               @check_esc_n:
002159r 3  C9 6E                        cmp #'n'
00215Br 3  D0 04                        bne @check_esc_q
00215Dr 3               
00215Dr 3                               ; newline, impl. dependant, using LF (ASCII values 10)
00215Dr 3  A9 0A                        lda #10
00215Fr 3  80 50                        bra @save_character
002161r 3               
002161r 3               @check_esc_q:
002161r 3  C9 71                        cmp #'q'
002163r 3  D0 04                        bne @check_esc_r
002165r 3               
002165r 3                               ; Double quote (ASCII value 34)
002165r 3  A9 22                        lda #34
002167r 3  80 48                        bra @save_character
002169r 3               
002169r 3               @check_esc_r:
002169r 3  C9 72                        cmp #'r'
00216Br 3  D0 04                        bne @check_esc_t
00216Dr 3               
00216Dr 3                               ; CR (ASCII value 13)
00216Dr 3  A9 0D                        lda #13
00216Fr 3  80 40                        bra @save_character
002171r 3               
002171r 3               @check_esc_t:
002171r 3  C9 74                        cmp #'t'
002173r 3  D0 04                        bne @check_esc_v
002175r 3               
002175r 3                               ; Horizontal TAB (ASCII value 9)
002175r 3  A9 09                        lda #9
002177r 3  80 38                        bra @save_character
002179r 3               
002179r 3               @check_esc_v:
002179r 3  C9 76                        cmp #'v'
00217Br 3  D0 04                        bne @check_esc_z
00217Dr 3               
00217Dr 3                               ; Vertical TAB (ASCII value 11)
00217Dr 3  A9 0B                        lda #11
00217Fr 3  80 30                        bra @save_character
002181r 3               
002181r 3               @check_esc_z:
002181r 3  C9 7A                        cmp #'z'
002183r 3  D0 04                        bne @check_esc_quote
002185r 3               
002185r 3                               ; NULL (ASCII value 0)
002185r 3  A9 00                        lda #0
002187r 3  80 28                        bra @save_character
002189r 3               
002189r 3               @check_esc_quote:
002189r 3  C9 22                        cmp #$22
00218Br 3  D0 04                        bne @check_esc_x
00218Dr 3               
00218Dr 3                               ; Double quote (ASCII value 34)
00218Dr 3  A9 22                        lda #34
00218Fr 3  80 20                        bra @save_character
002191r 3               
002191r 3               @check_esc_x:
002191r 3  C9 78                        cmp #'x'
002193r 3  D0 06                        bne @check_esc_backslash
002195r 3               
002195r 3                               ; This one is difficult. We need to get the next TWO
002195r 3                               ; characters (which might require a refill in the middle)
002195r 3                               ; and combine them as two hex digits. We do this by
002195r 3                               ; clearing bit 6 of tmp2+1 to indicate we are in a digit
002195r 3                               ; and using bit 0 to keep track of which digit we are on.
002195r 3  A9 BE                        lda #$BE        ; Clear bits 6 and 0
002197r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2+1
002199r 3  80 19                        bra @next_character
00219Br 3               
00219Br 3               @check_esc_backslash:
00219Br 3  C9 5C                        cmp #$5C
00219Dr 3  D0 04                        bne @not_escaped
00219Fr 3               
00219Fr 3                               ; Backslash (ASCII value 92)
00219Fr 3  A9 5C                        lda #92
0021A1r 3  80 0E                        bra @save_character
0021A3r 3               
0021A3r 3               @not_escaped:
0021A3r 3                               ; Check for the backslash to see if we should escape
0021A3r 3                               ; the next char.
0021A3r 3  C9 5C                        cmp #$5C        ; The backslash char
0021A5r 3  D0 06                        bne @regular_char
0021A7r 3               
0021A7r 3                               ; We found a backslash.  Don't save anyhing, but set
0021A7r 3                               ; a flag (in tmp2+1) to handle the next char. We don't
0021A7r 3                               ; try to get the next char here as it may require a
0021A7r 3                               ; refill of the input buffer.
0021A7r 3  A9 FF                        lda #$FF
0021A9r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2+1
0021ABr 3  80 07                        bra @next_character
0021ADr 3               
0021ADr 3               @regular_char:
0021ADr 3                               ; Check if the current character is the end of the string.
0021ADr 3  C9 22                        cmp #$22        ; ASCII for "
0021AFr 3  F0 0C                        beq @found_string_end
0021B1r 3               
0021B1r 3               @save_character:
0021B1r 3                               ; If we didn't reach the end of the string, compile this
0021B1r 3                               ; character into the dictionary
0021B1r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr cmpl_a
0021B4r 3               
0021B4r 3               @next_character:
0021B4r 3                               ; Move on to the next character.
0021B4r 3  E6 rr                        inc toin
0021B6r 3  D0 02                        bne @savechars_loop_longjump
0021B8r 3  E6 rr                        inc toin+1
0021BAr 3               
0021BAr 3               @savechars_loop_longjump:
0021BAr 3  4C rr rr                     jmp @savechars_loop
0021BDr 3               
0021BDr 3               @found_string_end:
0021BDr 3                               ; Use up the delimiter.
0021BDr 3  E6 rr                        inc toin
0021BFr 3  D0 02                        bne @1
0021C1r 3  E6 rr                        inc toin+1
0021C3r 3               @1:
0021C3r 3                               ; Calculate the length of the string, which is the
0021C3r 3                               ; difference between cp and the address of the start
0021C3r 3                               ; of the string (currently saved on the stack).
0021C3r 3  A5 rr                        lda cp
0021C5r 3  38                           sec
0021C6r 3  F5 02                        sbc 2,x
0021C8r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x         ; LSB
0021CAr 3  A5 rr                        lda cp+1
0021CCr 3  F5 03                        sbc 3,x
0021CEr 3  95 01                        sta 1,x         ; MSB
0021D0r 3               
0021D0r 3                               ; Update the address of the jump-over jmp instruction.
0021D0r 3                               ; First determine location of jmp instructions address.
0021D0r 3                               ; It should be 2 bytes before the start of the string.
0021D0r 3                               ; Compute it into tmp1, which is no longer being used.
0021D0r 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
0021D2r 3  38                           sec
0021D3r 3  E9 02                        sbc #2
0021D5r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
0021D7r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
0021D9r 3  E9 00                        sbc #0          ; Propagate borrow
0021DBr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
0021DDr 3               
0021DDr 3                               ; Update the address of the jump to HERE.
0021DDr 3  A5 rr                        lda cp
0021DFr 3  92 rr                        sta (tmp1)
0021E1r 3  A0 01                        ldy #1
0021E3r 3  A5 rr                        lda cp+1
0021E5r 3  91 rr                        sta (tmp1),y
0021E7r 3               
0021E7r 3                               ; What happens next depends on the state (which is bad, but
0021E7r 3                               ; that's the way it works at the moment). If we are
0021E7r 3                               ; interpretating, we save the string to a transient buffer
0021E7r 3                               ; and return that address (used for file calls, see
0021E7r 3                               ; https://forth-standard.org/standard/file/Sq . If we're
0021E7r 3                               ; compiling, we just need SLITERAL
0021E7r 3  A5 rr                        lda state
0021E9r 3  05 rr                        ora state+1             ; paranoid
0021EBr 3  F0 03                        beq @done
0021EDr 3               
0021EDr 3                               ; Jump into the middle of the sliteral word, after the
0021EDr 3                               ; string data has been compiled into the dictionary,
0021EDr 3                               ; because we've already done that step.
0021EDr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr sliteral_const_str         ; ( addr u -- )
0021F0r 3               
0021F0r 3               @done:
0021F0r 3  60           z_s_quote:      rts
0021F1r 3               
0021F1r 3               
0021F1r 3               
0021F1r 3               ; ## S_TO_D ( u -- d ) "Convert single cell number to double cell"
0021F1r 3               ; ## "s>d"  auto  ANS core
0021F1r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/StoD"""
0021F1r 3               
0021F1r 3               xt_s_to_d:
0021F1r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
0021F4r 3               
0021F4r 3  CA                           dex
0021F5r 3  CA                           dex
0021F6r 3  74 00                        stz 0,x
0021F8r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x
0021FAr 3               
0021FAr 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
0021FCr 3  10 04                        bpl @done
0021FEr 3               
0021FEr 3                               ; negative, extend sign
0021FEr 3  D6 00                        dec 0,x
002200r 3  D6 01                        dec 1,x
002202r 3               @done:
002202r 3  60           z_s_to_d:       rts
002203r 3               
002203r 3               
002203r 3               
002203r 3               ; ## SAVE_BUFFERS ( -- ) "Save all dirty buffers to storage"
002203r 3               ; ## "save-buffers"  tested  ANS block
002203r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/block/SAVE-BUFFERS"""
002203r 3               
002203r 3               xt_save_buffers:
002203r 3                               ; Check the buffer status
002203r 3  A0 2C                        ldy #buffstatus_offset
002205r 3  B1 rr                        lda (up),y      ; Only bits 0 and 1 are used, so only
002207r 3  C9 03                        cmp #3          ; LSB is needed.
002209r 3  D0 12                        bne @done       ; Either not used or not dirty = done!
00220Br 3               
00220Br 3                               ; We need to save the block.
00220Br 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_blkbuffer
00220Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_buffblocknum
002211r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_fetch
002214r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_block_write
002217r 3               
002217r 3                               ; Mark the buffer as clean now.
002217r 3  A9 01                        lda #1
002219r 3  A0 2C                        ldy #buffstatus_offset
00221Br 3  91 rr                        sta (up),y
00221Dr 3               
00221Dr 3               @done:
00221Dr 3  60           z_save_buffers: rts
00221Er 3               
00221Er 3               
00221Er 3               
00221Er 3               ; ## SCR ( -- addr ) "Push address of variable holding last screen listed"
00221Er 3               ; ## "scr"  auto  ANS block ext
00221Er 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/block/SCR"""
00221Er 3               xt_scr:
00221Er 3                               ; SCR is at UP + scr_offset
00221Er 3  CA                           dex
00221Fr 3  CA                           dex
002220r 3  18                           clc
002221r 3  A5 rr                        lda up
002223r 3  69 02                        adc #scr_offset ; Add offset
002225r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
002227r 3  A5 rr                        lda up+1
002229r 3  69 00                        adc #0          ; Adding carry
00222Br 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
00222Dr 3               
00222Dr 3  60           z_scr:          rts
00222Er 3               
00222Er 3               
00222Er 3               ; ## SEARCH ( addr1 u1 addr2 u2 -- addr3 u3 flag) "Search for a substring"
00222Er 3               ; ## "search"   auto  ANS string
00222Er 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/string/SEARCH
00222Er 3                       ; Search for string2 (denoted by addr2 u2) in string1 (denoted by
00222Er 3                       ; addr1 u1). If a match is found the flag will be true and
00222Er 3                       ; addr3 will have the address of the start of the match and u3 will have
00222Er 3                       ; the number of characters remaining from the match point to the end
00222Er 3                       ; of the original string1. If a match is not found, the flag will be
00222Er 3                       ; false and addr3 and u3 will be the original string1's addr1 and u1.
00222Er 3                       ; """
00222Er 3               
00222Er 3               xt_search:
00222Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_4
002231r 3               
002231r 3                               ; ANS says if the second string is a zero-length string it
002231r 3                               ; automatically matches.
002231r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
002233r 3  15 01                        ora 1,x
002235r 3  D0 0B                        bne @start_search
002237r 3               
002237r 3                               ; The second string is a zero length string.  Just remove
002237r 3                               ; the second string and put a true flag.
002237r 3  E8                           inx             ; Remove u2
002238r 3  E8                           inx
002239r 3  A9 FF                        lda #$FF        ; Turn addr2 into a true flag
00223Br 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
00223Dr 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
00223Fr 3  4C rr rr                     jmp z_search
002242r 3               
002242r 3               @start_search:
002242r 3                               ; Put an offset (starting at zero) on the stack.
002242r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_zero
002245r 3               
002245r 3               @search_loop:
002245r 3                               ; We stop (not found) when u2 + offset > u1
002245r 3                               ; Calculate u2+offset into tmp1
002245r 3  18                           clc
002246r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
002248r 3  75 02                        adc 2,x
00224Ar 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
00224Cr 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
00224Er 3  75 03                        adc 3,x
002250r 3               
002250r 3               
002250r 3                               ; Compare to u1. Start with the high byte
002250r 3  D5 07                        cmp 7,x
002252r 3  90 12                        bcc @init_comparison ; Obviously less
002254r 3  D0 06                        bne @not_found
002256r 3               
002256r 3                               ; The upper address byte matched - check the lower byte
002256r 3                               ; Load u1 first so we can use just a carry to check.
002256r 3  B5 06                        lda 6,x
002258r 3  C5 rr                        cmp tmp1
00225Ar 3  B0 0A                        bcs @init_comparison
00225Cr 3               
00225Cr 3               @not_found:
00225Cr 3                               ; The substring isn't in the main string.
00225Cr 3                               ; Return just the main string and a false flag.
00225Cr 3  E8                           inx             ; Remove offset
00225Dr 3  E8                           inx
00225Er 3  E8                           inx             ; Remove u2
00225Fr 3  E8                           inx
002260r 3  74 00                        stz 0,x         ; Turn addr2 into a false flag
002262r 3  74 01                        stz 1,x
002264r 3  80 66                        bra z_search
002266r 3               
002266r 3               @init_comparison:
002266r 3                               ; Use tmp1 to hold address in string 1.
002266r 3                               ; Use tmp2 to hold address in string 2.
002266r 3                               ; Use tmp3 to hold the number of characters left to check.
002266r 3               
002266r 3                               ; Compute the starting address in string 1
002266r 3                               ; as addr1 + offset
002266r 3  18                           clc
002267r 3  B5 08                        lda 8,x
002269r 3  75 00                        adc 0,x
00226Br 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1
00226Dr 3  B5 09                        lda 9,x
00226Fr 3  75 01                        adc 1,x
002271r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp1+1
002273r 3               
002273r 3                               ; The starting address in string 2 is just addr2.
002273r 3  B5 04                        lda 4,x
002275r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2
002277r 3  B5 05                        lda 5,x
002279r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp2+1
00227Br 3               
00227Br 3                               ; The number of characters to check is u2.
00227Br 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
00227Dr 3  85 rr                        sta tmp3
00227Fr 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
002281r 3  85 rr                        sta tmp3+1
002283r 3               
002283r 3               @comparison_loop:
002283r 3                               ; Check to see if the current characters match.
002283r 3  B2 rr                        lda (tmp1)
002285r 3  D2 rr                        cmp (tmp2)
002287r 3  F0 05                        beq @letters_match
002289r 3               
002289r 3                               ; One of the letters didn't match.
002289r 3                               ; Increment the offset and try again.
002289r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_one_plus
00228Cr 3  80 B7                        bra @search_loop
00228Er 3               
00228Er 3               @letters_match:
00228Er 3                               ; The letters match.  Advance the pointers until the
00228Er 3                               ; count reaches zero.
00228Er 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp1
002290r 3  D0 02                        bne @1
002292r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp1+1
002294r 3               @1:
002294r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp2
002296r 3  D0 02                        bne @2
002298r 3  E6 rr                        inc tmp2+1
00229Ar 3               @2:
00229Ar 3                               ; Decrement the count of remaining letters to check.
00229Ar 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp3
00229Cr 3  D0 02                        bne @3
00229Er 3  C6 rr                        dec tmp3+1
0022A0r 3               @3:
0022A0r 3  C6 rr                        dec tmp3
0022A2r 3               
0022A2r 3                               ; Check if we've reached zero.
0022A2r 3  A5 rr                        lda tmp3
0022A4r 3  05 rr                        ora tmp3+1
0022A6r 3  D0 DB                        bne @comparison_loop ; Check the next letter
0022A8r 3               
0022A8r 3                               ; We've run out of letters and they all match!
0022A8r 3                               ; Return (addr1+offset) (u1-offset) true
0022A8r 3                               ; Add offset to addr1.
0022A8r 3  18                           clc
0022A9r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
0022ABr 3  75 08                        adc 8,x
0022ADr 3  95 08                        sta 8,x
0022AFr 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
0022B1r 3  75 09                        adc 9,x
0022B3r 3  95 09                        sta 9,x
0022B5r 3               
0022B5r 3                               ; Subtract offset from u1.
0022B5r 3  38                           sec
0022B6r 3  B5 06                        lda 6,x
0022B8r 3  F5 00                        sbc 0,x
0022BAr 3  95 06                        sta 6,x
0022BCr 3  B5 07                        lda 7,x
0022BEr 3  F5 01                        sbc 1,x
0022C0r 3  95 07                        sta 7,x
0022C2r 3               
0022C2r 3                               ; Replace addr2, u2, and offset with a true flag.
0022C2r 3  E8                           inx             ; drop offset
0022C3r 3  E8                           inx
0022C4r 3  E8                           inx             ; drop u2
0022C5r 3  E8                           inx
0022C6r 3  A9 FF                        lda #$FF
0022C8r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x         ; Turn addr2 into a true flag.
0022CAr 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
0022CCr 3               
0022CCr 3  60           z_search:       rts
0022CDr 3               
0022CDr 3               
0022CDr 3               
0022CDr 3               ; ## SEMICOLON ( -- ) "End compilation of new word"
0022CDr 3               ; ## ";"  auto  ANS core
0022CDr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/Semi
0022CDr 3                       ; End the compilation of a new word into the Dictionary.
0022CDr 3                       ;
0022CDr 3                       ; When we
0022CDr 3                       ; enter this, WORKWORD is pointing to the nt_ of this word in the
0022CDr 3                       ; Dictionary, DP to the previous word, and CP to the next free byte.
0022CDr 3                       ; A Forth definition would be (see "Starting Forth"):
0022CDr 3                       ; : POSTPONE EXIT  REVEAL POSTPONE ; [ ; IMMEDIATE  Following the
0022CDr 3                       ; practice of Gforth, we warn here if a word has been redefined.
0022CDr 3                       ; """
0022CDr 3               
0022CDr 3               xt_semicolon:
0022CDr 3                               ; Check if this is a : word or a :NONAME word.
0022CDr 3  24 rr                        bit status
0022CFr 3  70 11                        bvs @colonword
0022D1r 3               
0022D1r 3                               ; This is a :NONAME word - just put an RTS on the end and
0022D1r 3                               ; the address (held in workword) on the stack.
0022D1r 3  A9 60                        lda #$60                ; opcode for RTS
0022D3r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr cmpl_a
0022D6r 3               
0022D6r 3  CA                           dex
0022D7r 3  CA                           dex
0022D8r 3  A5 rr                        lda workword
0022DAr 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0022DCr 3  A5 rr                        lda workword+1
0022DEr 3  95 01                        sta 1,x
0022E0r 3  80 45                        bra @semicolon_done
0022E2r 3               
0022E2r 3               @colonword:
0022E2r 3                               ; CP is the byte that will be the address we use in the
0022E2r 3                               ; header as the end-of-compile address (z_word). This is
0022E2r 3                               ; six bytes down from the header
0022E2r 3  A0 06                        ldy #6
0022E4r 3  A5 rr                        lda cp
0022E6r 3  91 rr                        sta (workword),y
0022E8r 3  C8                           iny
0022E9r 3  A5 rr                        lda cp+1
0022EBr 3  91 rr                        sta (workword),y
0022EDr 3               
0022EDr 3                               ; Allocate one further byte and save the RTS instruction
0022EDr 3                               ; there
0022EDr 3  A9 60                        lda #$60                ; opcode for RTS
0022EFr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr cmpl_a
0022F2r 3               
0022F2r 3                               ; Before we formally add the word to the Dictionary, we
0022F2r 3                               ; check to see if it is already present, and if yes, we
0022F2r 3                               ; warn the user.
0022F2r 3               
0022F2r 3                               ; See if word already in Dictionary.
0022F2r 3                               ; (STATUS bit 7 will be high as CREATE already
0022F2r 3                               ;  checked for us.)
0022F2r 3  24 rr                        bit status
0022F4r 3  10 26                        bpl @new_word   ; Bit 7 is clear = new word
0022F6r 3               
0022F6r 3                               ; We start by putting the string of the
0022F6r 3                               ; word we're defining on the stack
0022F6r 3  CA                           dex
0022F7r 3  CA                           dex
0022F8r 3  CA                           dex
0022F9r 3  CA                           dex
0022FAr 3               
0022FAr 3                               ; WORKWORD points to the beginning of the head of our new
0022FAr 3                               ; word, where the first byte is the length of the string
0022FAr 3                               ; We can't use LATESTNT because we haven't added the new
0022FAr 3                               ; word to the Dictionary yet
0022FAr 3  B2 rr                        lda (workword)
0022FCr 3  95 00                        sta 0,x
0022FEr 3  74 01                        stz 1,x
002300r 3               
002300r 3                               ; Eight bytes below WORKWORD is the actual beginning of
002300r 3                               ; the string
002300r 3  A5 rr                        lda workword
002302r 3  18                           clc
002303r 3  69 08                        adc #8
002305r 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
002307r 3  A5 rr                        lda workword+1
002309r 3  69 00                        adc #0                  ; only want carry
00230Br 3  95 03                        sta 3,x
00230Dr 3               
00230Dr 3                               ; This word is already in the Dictionary, so we print a
00230Dr 3                               ; warning to the user.
00230Dr 3  A9 02                        lda #str_redefined       ; address of string "redefined"
00230Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr print_string_no_lf
002312r 3               
002312r 3                               ; Now we print the offending word.
002312r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_type
002315r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_space
002318r 3               
002318r 3                               ; Clear bit 7 of status (so future words will print message
002318r 3                               ; by defaut)
002318r 3  A9 80                        lda #%10000000
00231Ar 3  14 rr                        trb status
00231Cr 3               
00231Cr 3               @new_word:
00231Cr 3                               ; Let's get this over with. Save beginning of our word
00231Cr 3                               ; as new last word in the Dictionary
00231Cr 3  A5 rr                        lda workword
00231Er 3  85 rr                        sta dp
002320r 3  A5 rr                        lda workword+1
002322r 3  85 rr                        sta dp+1
002324r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr dp_to_current       ; Save the updated DP to the
002327r 3                                                       ; CURRENT wordlist.
002327r 3               @semicolon_done:
002327r 3                               ; Word definition complete. Return compile flag to zero
002327r 3                               ; to return to interpret mode
002327r 3  64 rr                        stz state
002329r 3  64 rr                        stz state+1
00232Br 3               
00232Br 3  60           z_semicolon:    rts
00232Cr 3               
00232Cr 3               
00232Cr 3               
00232Cr 3               ; ## SIGN ( n -- ) "Add minus to pictured output"
00232Cr 3               ; ## "sign"  auto  ANS core
00232Cr 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/SIGN
00232Cr 3                       ;
00232Cr 3                       ; Code based on
00232Cr 3                       ; http://pforth.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/fth/numberio.fth
00232Cr 3                       ; Original Forth code is   0< IF ASCII - HOLD THEN
00232Cr 3                       ; """
00232Cr 3               
00232Cr 3               xt_sign:
00232Cr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_1
00232Fr 3               
00232Fr 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x         ; check MSB of TOS
002331r 3  30 04                        bmi @minus
002333r 3               
002333r 3  E8                           inx
002334r 3  E8                           inx
002335r 3  80 09                        bra @done
002337r 3               @minus:
002337r 3  A9 2D                        lda #$2D        ; ASCII for "-"
002339r 3  95 00                        sta 0,x         ; overwrite TOS
00233Br 3  74 01                        stz 1,x         ; paranoid
00233Dr 3               
00233Dr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_hold
002340r 3               @done:
002340r 3  60           z_sign:         rts
002341r 3               
002341r 3               
002341r 3               
002341r 3               ; ## SLASH ( n1 n2 -- n ) "Divide NOS by TOS"
002341r 3               ; ## "/"  auto  ANS core
002341r 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/Div
002341r 3                       ;
002341r 3                       ; Forth code is either  >R S>D R> FM/MOD SWAP DROP
002341r 3                       ; or >R S>D R> SM/REM SWAP DROP -- we use SM/REM in Tali Forth.
002341r 3                       ; This code is currently unoptimized. This code without the SLASH
002341r 3                       ; DROP at the end is /MOD, so we share the code as far as possible.
002341r 3                       ; """
002341r 3               
002341r 3               xt_slash:
002341r 3                               ; With all the multiplication going on, it would be hard to
002341r 3                               ; make sure that one of our temporary variables is not
002341r 3                               ; overwritten. We make sure that doesn't happen by taking the
002341r 3                               ; hit of pushing the flag to the 65c02's stack
002341r 3  A9 00                        lda #0
002343r 3  48                           pha
002344r 3  80 03                        bra _common
002346r 3               
002346r 3               xt_slash_mod:
002346r 3                               ; Note that /MOD accesses this code
002346r 3  A9 FF                        lda #$FF
002348r 3  48                           pha             ; falls through to _common
002349r 3               
002349r 3               _common:
002349r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_to_r             ; >R
00234Cr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_s_to_d           ; S>D
00234Fr 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_r_from           ; R>
002352r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_sm_slash_rem     ; SM/REM
002355r 3               
002355r 3                               ; Get the flag back from the 65c02's stack. Zero is SLASH,
002355r 3                               ; $FF is SLASH MOD
002355r 3  68                           pla
002356r 3  D0 05                        bne @done
002358r 3               
002358r 3                               ; The following code is for SLASH only
002358r 3  20 rr rr                     jsr xt_swap
00235Br 3  E8                           inx             ; DROP
00235Cr 3  E8                           inx
00235Dr 3               @done:
00235Dr 3               z_slash_mod:
00235Dr 3  60           z_slash:        rts
00235Er 3               
00235Er 3               
00235Er 3               
00235Er 3               ; ## SLASH_MOD ( n1 n2 -- n3 n4 ) "Divide NOS by TOS with a remainder"
00235Er 3               ; ## "/mod"  auto  ANS core
00235Er 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/core/DivMOD
00235Er 3                       ;
00235Er 3                       ; This is a dummy entry, the actual code is shared with SLASH
00235Er 3                       ; """
00235Er 3               
00235Er 3               
00235Er 3               ; ## SLASH_STRING ( addr u n -- addr u ) "Shorten string by n"
00235Er 3               ; ## "/string"  auto  ANS string
00235Er 3                       ; """https://forth-standard.org/standard/string/DivSTRING
00235Er 3                       ;
00235Er 3                       ; Forth code is
00235Er 3                       ; : /STRING ( ADDR U N -- ADDR U ) ROT OVER + ROT ROT - ;
00235Er 3                       ; Put differently, we need to add TOS and 3OS, and subtract
00235Er 3                       ; TOS from NOS, and then drop TOS
00235Er 3                       ; """
00235Er 3               
00235Er 3               xt_slash_string:
00235Er 3  20 rr rr                     jsr underflow_3
002361r 3               
002361r 3  18                           clc             ; 3OS+TOS
002362r 3  B5 00                        lda 0,x
002364r 3  75 04                        adc 4,x
002366r 3  95 04                        sta 4,x
002368r 3               
002368r 3  B5 01                        lda 1,x
00236Ar 3  75 05                        adc 5,x
00236Cr 3  95 05                        sta 5,x
00236Er 3               
00236Er 3  38                           sec             ; NOS-TOS
00236Fr 3  B5 02                        lda 2,x
002371r 3  F5 00                        sbc 0,x
002373r 3  95 02                        sta 2,x
002375r 3               
002375r 3  B5 03                        lda 3,x
002377r 3  F5 01                        sbc 1,x
002379r 3  95 03                        sta 3,x
00237Br 3               
00237Br 3  E8                           inx
00237Cr 3  E8                           inx
00237Dr 3               
00237Dr 3  60           z_slash_string: rts
00237Er 3               
00237Er 3
