00421Fr 2               ; User-defined Forth words, see forth_code/README.md
00421Fr 2               user_words_start:
00421Fr 2  20 32 30 20  .incbin "forth_code/user_words.asc"
004223r 2  63 6F 6E 73  
004227r 2  74 61 6E 74  
0048E1r 2               user_words_end:
0048E1r 2               
0048E1r 2               
0048E1r 2               ; =====================================================================
0048E1r 2               ; COMPILE WORDS, JUMPS and SUBROUTINE JUMPS INTO CODE
0048E1r 2               
0048E1r 2               ; These three routines compile instructions such as "jsr xt_words" into a word
0048E1r 2               ; at compile time so they are available at run time. Words that use this
0048E1r 2               ; routine may not be natively compiled. We use "cmpl" as not to confuse these
0048E1r 2               ; routines with the COMPILE, word. Always call this with a subroutine jump.
0048E1r 2               ; This means combining JSR/RTS to JMP in those cases is not going to work. To
0048E1r 2               ; use, load the LSB of the address in A and the MSB in Y. You can remember
0048E1r 2               ; which comes first by thinking of the song "Young Americans" ("YA") by David
0048E1r 2               ; Bowie.
0048E1r 2               
0048E1r 2               ;               ldy #>addr      ; MSB   ; "Young"
0048E1r 2               ;               lda #<addr      ; LSB   ; "Americans"
0048E1r 2               ;               jsr cmpl_subroutine
0048E1r 2               
0048E1r 2               ; Also, we keep a routine here to compile a single byte passed through A.
0048E1r 2               
0048E1r 2               cmpl_subroutine:
0048E1r 2                   ; This is the entry point to compile JSR <ADDR>
0048E1r 2  48               pha             ; save LSB of address
0048E2r 2  A9 20            lda #$20        ; load opcode for JSR
0048E4r 2  80 03            bra cmpl_common
0048E6r 2               cmpl_jump:
0048E6r 2                   ; This is the entry point to compile JMP <ADDR>
0048E6r 2  48               pha             ; save LSB of address
0048E7r 2  A9 4C            lda #$4c        ; load opcode for JMP, fall thru to cmpl_common
0048E9r 2               cmpl_common:
0048E9r 2                   ; At this point, A contains the opcode to be compiled,
0048E9r 2                   ; the LSB of the address is on the 65c02 stack, and the MSB of
0048E9r 2                   ; the address is in Y
0048E9r 2  20 rr rr         jsr cmpl_a      ; compile opcode
0048ECr 2  68               pla             ; retrieve address LSB; fall thru to cmpl_word
0048EDr 2               cmpl_word:
0048EDr 2                   ; This is the entry point to compile a word (little-endian)
0048EDr 2  20 rr rr         jsr cmpl_a      ; compile LSB of address
0048F0r 2  98               tya             ; fall thru for MSB
0048F1r 2               cmpl_a:
0048F1r 2                   ; This is the entry point to compile a single byte which
0048F1r 2                   ; is passed in A. The built-in assembler assumes that this
0048F1r 2                   ; routine does not modify Y.
0048F1r 2  92 rr            sta (cp)
0048F3r 2  E6 rr            inc cp
0048F5r 2  D0 02            bne _done
0048F7r 2  E6 rr            inc cp+1
0048F9r 2               _done:
0048F9r 2  60               rts
0048FAr 2               
0048FAr 2               
0048FAr 2               
0048FAr 2               ; =====================================================================
0048FAr 2               ; CODE FIELD ROUTINES
0048FAr 2               
0048FAr 2               doconst:
0048FAr 2               ; """Execute a CONSTANT: Push the data in the first two bytes of
0048FAr 2               ; the Data Field onto the Data Stack
0048FAr 2               ; """
0048FAr 2  CA               dex             ; make room for constant
0048FBr 2  CA               dex
0048FCr 2               
0048FCr 2                   ; The value we need is stored in the two bytes after the
0048FCr 2                   ; JSR return address, which in turn is what is on top of
0048FCr 2                   ; the Return Stack
0048FCr 2  68               pla             ; LSB of return address
0048FDr 2  85 rr            sta tmp1
0048FFr 2  68               pla             ; MSB of return address
004900r 2  85 rr            sta tmp1+1
004902r 2               
004902r 2                   ; Start LDY with 1 instead of 0 because of how JSR stores
004902r 2                   ; the return address on the 65c02
004902r 2  A0 01            ldy #1
004904r 2  B1 rr            lda (tmp1),y
004906r 2  95 00            sta 0,x
004908r 2  C8               iny
004909r 2  B1 rr            lda (tmp1),y
00490Br 2  95 01            sta 1,x
00490Dr 2               
00490Dr 2                   ; This takes us back to the original caller, not the
00490Dr 2                   ; DOCONST caller
00490Dr 2  60               rts
00490Er 2               
00490Er 2               
00490Er 2               dodefer:
00490Er 2               ; """Execute a DEFER statement at runtime: Execute the address we
00490Er 2               ; find after the caller in the Data Field
00490Er 2               ; """
00490Er 2                   ; The xt we need is stored in the two bytes after the JSR
00490Er 2                   ; return address, which is what is on top of the Return
00490Er 2                   ; Stack. So all we have to do is replace our return jump
00490Er 2                   ; with what we find there
00490Er 2  68               pla             ; LSB
00490Fr 2  85 rr            sta tmp1
004911r 2  68               pla             ; MSB
004912r 2  85 rr            sta tmp1+1
004914r 2               
004914r 2  A0 01            ldy #1
004916r 2  B1 rr            lda (tmp1),y
004918r 2  85 rr            sta tmp2
00491Ar 2  C8               iny
00491Br 2  B1 rr            lda (tmp1),y
00491Dr 2  85 rr            sta tmp2+1
00491Fr 2               
00491Fr 2  6C rr rr         jmp (tmp2)      ; This is actually a jump to the new target
004922r 2               
004922r 2               defer_error:
004922r 2                   ; """Error routine for undefined DEFER: Complain and abort"""
004922r 2  A9 03            lda #err_defer
004924r 2  4C rr rr         jmp error
004927r 2               
004927r 2               dodoes:
004927r 2               ; """Execute the runtime portion of DOES>. See DOES> and
004927r 2               ; docs/create-does.txt for details and
004927r 2               ; http://www.bradrodriguez.com/papers/moving3.htm
004927r 2               ; """
004927r 2                   ; Assumes the address of the CFA of the original defining word
004927r 2                   ; (say, CONSTANT) is on the top of the Return Stack. Save it
004927r 2                   ; for a later jump, adding one byte because of the way the
004927r 2                   ; 6502 works
004927r 2  7A               ply             ; LSB
004928r 2  68               pla             ; MSB
004929r 2  C8               iny
00492Ar 2  D0 01            bne @1
00492Cr 2  1A               inc
00492Dr 2               @1:
00492Dr 2  84 rr            sty tmp2
00492Fr 2  85 rr            sta tmp2+1
004931r 2               
004931r 2                   ; Next on the Return Stack should be the address of the PFA of
004931r 2                   ; the calling defined word (say, the name of whatever constant we
004931r 2                   ; just defined). Move this to the Data Stack, again adding one.
004931r 2  CA               dex
004932r 2  CA               dex
004933r 2               
004933r 2  7A               ply
004934r 2  68               pla
004935r 2  C8               iny
004936r 2  D0 01            bne @2
004938r 2  1A               inc
004939r 2               @2:
004939r 2  94 00            sty 0,x         ; LSB
00493Br 2  95 01            sta 1,x         ; MSB
00493Dr 2               
00493Dr 2                   ; This leaves the return address from the original main routine
00493Dr 2                   ; on top of the Return Stack. We leave that untouched and jump
00493Dr 2                   ; to the special code of the defining word. It's RTS instruction
00493Dr 2                   ; will take us back to the main routine
00493Dr 2  6C rr rr         jmp (tmp2)
004940r 2               
004940r 2               
004940r 2               dovar:
004940r 2               ; """Execute a variable: Push the address of the first bytes of
004940r 2               ; the Data Field onto the stack. This is called with JSR so we
004940r 2               ; can pick up the address of the calling variable off the 65c02's
004940r 2               ; stack. The final RTS takes us to the original caller of the
004940r 2               ; routine that itself called DOVAR. This is the default
004940r 2               ; routine installed with CREATE.
004940r 2               ; """
004940r 2                   ; Pull the return address off the machine's stack, adding
004940r 2                   ; one because of the way the 65c02 handles subroutines
004940r 2  7A               ply             ; LSB
004941r 2  68               pla             ; MSB
004942r 2  C8               iny
004943r 2  D0 01            bne @1
004945r 2  1A               inc
004946r 2               @1:
004946r 2  CA               dex
004947r 2  CA               dex
004948r 2               
004948r 2  95 01            sta 1,x
00494Ar 2  98               tya
00494Br 2  95 00            sta 0,x
00494Dr 2               
00494Dr 2  60               rts
00494Er 2               
00494Er 2               ; =====================================================================
00494Er 2               ; LOW LEVEL HELPER FUNCTIONS
00494Er 2               
00494Er 2               byte_to_ascii:
00494Er 2               ; """Convert byte in A to two ASCII hex digits and EMIT them"""
00494Er 2               .scope
00494Er 2  48               pha
00494Fr 2  4A               lsr             ; convert high nibble first
004950r 2  4A               lsr
004951r 2  4A               lsr
004952r 2  4A               lsr
004953r 2  20 rr rr         jsr _nibble_to_ascii
004956r 2  68               pla
004957r 2               
004957r 2                   ; fall through to _nibble_to_ascii
004957r 2               
004957r 2               _nibble_to_ascii:
004957r 2               ; """Private helper function for byte_to_ascii: Print lower nibble
004957r 2               ; of A and and EMIT it. This does the actual work.
004957r 2               ; """
004957r 2  29 0F            and #$0F
004959r 2  09 30            ora #'0'
00495Br 2  C9 3A            cmp #$3A        ; '9+1
00495Dr 2  90 02            bcc @1
00495Fr 2  69 06            adc #$06
004961r 2               
004961r 2  4C rr rr     @1:               jmp emit_a
004964r 2               
004964r 2  60               rts
004965r 2               .endscope
004965r 2               
004965r 2               compare_16bit:
004965r 2               ; """Compare TOS/NOS and return results in form of the 65c02 flags
004965r 2               ; Adapted from Leventhal "6502 Assembly Language Subroutines", see
004965r 2               ; also http://www.6502.org/tutorials/compare_beyond.html
004965r 2               ; For signed numbers, Z signals equality and N which number is larger:
004965r 2               ;       if TOS = NOS: Z=1 and N=0
004965r 2               ;       if TOS > NOS: Z=0 and N=0
004965r 2               ;       if TOS < NOS: Z=0 and N=1
004965r 2               ; For unsigned numbers, Z signals equality and C which number is larger:
004965r 2               ;       if TOS = NOS: Z=1 and N=0
004965r 2               ;       if TOS > NOS: Z=0 and C=1
004965r 2               ;       if TOS < NOS: Z=0 and C=0
004965r 2               ; Compared to the book routine, WORD1 (MINUED) is TOS
004965r 2               ;                               WORD2 (SUBTRAHEND) is NOS
004965r 2               ; """
004965r 2               .scope
004965r 2                   ; Compare LSB first to set the carry flag
004965r 2  B5 00            lda 0,x                 ; LSB of TOS
004967r 2  D5 02            cmp 2,x                 ; LSB of NOS
004969r 2  F0 0A            beq _equal
00496Br 2               
00496Br 2                   ; LSBs are not equal, compare MSB
00496Br 2  B5 01            lda 1,x                 ; MSB of TOS
00496Dr 2  F5 03            sbc 3,x                 ; MSB of NOS
00496Fr 2  09 01            ora #1                  ; Make zero flag 0 because not equal
004971r 2  70 08            bvs _overflow
004973r 2  80 08            bra _not_equal
004975r 2               _equal:
004975r 2                   ; Low bytes are equal, so we compare high bytes
004975r 2  B5 01            lda 1,x                 ; MSB of TOS
004977r 2  F5 03            sbc 3,x                 ; MSB of NOS
004979r 2  50 04            bvc _done
00497Br 2               _overflow:
00497Br 2                   ; Handle overflow because we use signed numbers
00497Br 2  49 80            eor #$80                ; complement negative flag
00497Dr 2               _not_equal:
00497Dr 2  09 01            ora #1                  ; if overflow, we can't be eqal
00497Fr 2               _done:
00497Fr 2  60               rts
004980r 2               .endscope
004980r 2               
004980r 2               current_to_dp:
004980r 2               ; """Look up the current (compilation) dictionary pointer
004980r 2               ; in the wordlist set and put it into the dp zero-page
004980r 2               ; variable. Uses A and Y.
004980r 2               ; """
004980r 2                   ; Determine which wordlist is current
004980r 2  A0 04            ldy #current_offset
004982r 2  B1 rr            lda (up),y      ; current is a byte variable
004984r 2  0A               asl             ; turn it into an offset (in cells)
004985r 2               
004985r 2                   ; Get the dictionary pointer for that wordlist.
004985r 2  18               clc
004986r 2  69 06            adc #wordlists_offset   ; add offset to wordlists base.
004988r 2  A8               tay
004989r 2  B1 rr            lda (up),y              ; get the dp for that wordlist.
00498Br 2  85 rr            sta dp
00498Dr 2  C8               iny
00498Er 2  B1 rr            lda (up),y
004990r 2  85 rr            sta dp+1
004992r 2               
004992r 2  60               rts
004993r 2               
004993r 2               
004993r 2               dp_to_current:
004993r 2               ; """Look up which wordlist is current and update its pointer
004993r 2               ; with the value in dp. Uses A and Y.
004993r 2               ; """
004993r 2                   ; Determine which wordlist is current
004993r 2  A0 04            ldy #current_offset
004995r 2  B1 rr            lda (up),y      ; current is a byte variable
004997r 2  0A               asl             ; turn it into an offset (in cells)
004998r 2               
004998r 2                   ; Get the dictionary pointer for that wordlist.
004998r 2  18               clc
004999r 2  69 06            adc #wordlists_offset   ; add offset to wordlists base.
00499Br 2  A8               tay
00499Cr 2  A5 rr            lda dp
00499Er 2  91 rr            sta (up),y              ; get the dp for that wordlist.
0049A0r 2  C8               iny
0049A1r 2  A5 rr            lda dp+1
0049A3r 2  91 rr            sta (up),y
0049A5r 2               
0049A5r 2  60               rts
0049A6r 2               
0049A6r 2               interpret:
0049A6r 2               .scope
0049A6r 2               ; """Core routine for the interpreter called by EVALUATE and QUIT.
0049A6r 2               ; Process one line only. Assumes that the address of name is in
0049A6r 2               ; cib and the length of the whole input line string is in ciblen
0049A6r 2               ; """
0049A6r 2                   ; Normally we would use PARSE here with the SPACE character as
0049A6r 2                   ; a parameter (PARSE replaces WORD in modern Forths). However,
0049A6r 2                   ; Gforth's PARSE-NAME makes more sense as it uses spaces as
0049A6r 2                   ; delimiters per default and skips any leading spaces, which
0049A6r 2                   ; PARSE doesn't
0049A6r 2               _loop:
0049A6r 2  20 rr rr         jsr xt_parse_name       ; ( "string" -- addr u )
0049A9r 2               
0049A9r 2                   ; If PARSE-NAME returns 0 (empty line), no characters were left
0049A9r 2                   ; in the line and we need to go get a new line
0049A9r 2  B5 00            lda 0,x
0049ABr 2  15 01            ora 1,x
0049ADr 2  F0 70            beq _line_done
0049AFr 2               
0049AFr 2                   ; Go to FIND-NAME to see if this is a word we know. We have to
0049AFr 2                   ; make a copy of the address in case it isn't a word we know and
0049AFr 2                   ; we have to go see if it is a number
0049AFr 2  20 rr rr         jsr xt_two_dup          ; ( addr u -- addr u addr u )
0049B2r 2  20 rr rr         jsr xt_find_name        ; ( addr u addr u -- addr u nt|0 )
0049B5r 2               
0049B5r 2                   ; A zero signals that we didn't find a word in the Dictionary
0049B5r 2  B5 00            lda 0,x
0049B7r 2  15 01            ora 1,x
0049B9r 2  D0 28            bne _got_name_token
0049BBr 2               
0049BBr 2                   ; We didn't get any nt we know of, so let's see if this is
0049BBr 2                   ; a number.
0049BBr 2  E8               inx                     ; ( addr u 0 -- addr u )
0049BCr 2  E8               inx
0049BDr 2               
0049BDr 2                   ; If the number conversion doesn't work, NUMBER will do the
0049BDr 2                   ; complaining for us
0049BDr 2  20 rr rr         jsr xt_number           ; ( addr u -- u|d )
0049C0r 2               
0049C0r 2                   ; Otherweise, if we're interpreting, we're done
0049C0r 2  A5 rr            lda state
0049C2r 2  F0 E2            beq _loop
0049C4r 2               
0049C4r 2                   ; We're compiling, so there is a bit more work.  Check
0049C4r 2                   ; status bit 5 to see if it's a single or double-cell
0049C4r 2                   ; number.
0049C4r 2  A9 20            lda #$20
0049C6r 2  24 rr            bit status
0049C8r 2  F0 0D            beq _single_number
0049CAr 2               
0049CAr 2                   ; It's a double cell number.  If we swap the
0049CAr 2                   ; upper and lower half, we can use the literal_runtime twice
0049CAr 2                   ; to compile it into the dictionary.
0049CAr 2  20 rr rr         jsr xt_swap
0049CDr 2  A0 rr            ldy #>literal_runtime
0049CFr 2  A9 rr            lda #<literal_runtime
0049D1r 2  20 rr rr         jsr cmpl_subroutine
0049D4r 2               
0049D4r 2                   ; compile our number
0049D4r 2  20 rr rr         jsr xt_comma
0049D7r 2               
0049D7r 2                   ; Fall into _single_number to process the other half.
0049D7r 2               _single_number:
0049D7r 2  A0 rr            ldy #>literal_runtime
0049D9r 2  A9 rr            lda #<literal_runtime
0049DBr 2  20 rr rr         jsr cmpl_subroutine
0049DEr 2               
0049DEr 2                   ; compile our number
0049DEr 2  20 rr rr         jsr xt_comma
0049E1r 2               
0049E1r 2                   ; That was so much fun, let's do it again!
0049E1r 2  80 C3            bra _loop
0049E3r 2               
0049E3r 2               _got_name_token:
0049E3r 2                   ; We have a known word's nt TOS. We're going to need its xt
0049E3r 2                   ; though, which is four bytes father down.
0049E3r 2               
0049E3r 2                   ; We arrive here with ( addr u nt ), so we NIP twice
0049E3r 2  B5 00            lda 0,x
0049E5r 2  95 04            sta 4,x
0049E7r 2  B5 01            lda 1,x
0049E9r 2  95 05            sta 5,x
0049EBr 2               
0049EBr 2  E8               inx
0049ECr 2  E8               inx
0049EDr 2  E8               inx
0049EEr 2  E8               inx                     ; ( nt )
0049EFr 2               
0049EFr 2                   ; Save a version of nt for error handling and compilation stuff
0049EFr 2  B5 00            lda 0,x
0049F1r 2  85 rr            sta tmpbranch
0049F3r 2  B5 01            lda 1,x
0049F5r 2  85 rr            sta tmpbranch+1
0049F7r 2               
0049F7r 2  20 rr rr         jsr xt_name_to_int      ; ( nt - xt )
0049FAr 2               
0049FAr 2                   ; See if we are in interpret or compile mode, 0 is interpret
0049FAr 2  A5 rr            lda state
0049FCr 2  D0 13            bne _compile
0049FEr 2               
0049FEr 2                   ; We are interpreting, so EXECUTE the xt that is TOS. First,
0049FEr 2                   ; though, see if this isn't a compile-only word, which would be
0049FEr 2                   ; illegal. The status byte is the second one of the header.
0049FEr 2  A0 01            ldy #1
004A00r 2  B1 rr            lda (tmpbranch),y
004A02r 2  29 01            and #CO                 ; mask everything but Compile Only bit
004A04r 2  F0 05            beq _interpret
004A06r 2               
004A06r 2  A9 02            lda #err_compileonly
004A08r 2  4C rr rr         jmp error
004A0Br 2               
004A0Br 2               _interpret:
004A0Br 2                   ; We JSR to EXECUTE instead of calling the xt directly because
004A0Br 2                   ; the RTS of the word we're executing will bring us back here,
004A0Br 2                   ; skipping EXECUTE completely during RTS. If we were to execute
004A0Br 2                   ; xt directly, we have to fool around with the Return Stack
004A0Br 2                   ; instead, which is actually slightly slower
004A0Br 2  20 rr rr         jsr xt_execute
004A0Er 2               
004A0Er 2                   ; That's quite enough for this word, let's get the next one
004A0Er 2  4C rr rr         jmp _loop
004A11r 2               
004A11r 2               _compile:
004A11r 2                   ; We're compiling! However, we need to see if this is an
004A11r 2                   ; IMMEDIATE word, which would mean we execute it right now even
004A11r 2                   ; during compilation mode. Fortunately, we saved the nt so life
004A11r 2                   ; is easier. The flags are in the second byte of the header
004A11r 2  A0 01            ldy #1
004A13r 2  B1 rr            lda (tmpbranch),y
004A15r 2  29 04            and #IM                 ; Mask all but IM bit
004A17r 2  D0 F2            bne _interpret          ; IMMEDIATE word, execute right now
004A19r 2               
004A19r 2                   ; Compile the xt into the Dictionary with COMPILE,
004A19r 2  20 rr rr         jsr xt_compile_comma
004A1Cr 2  4C rr rr         jmp _loop
004A1Fr 2               
004A1Fr 2               _line_done:
004A1Fr 2                   ; drop stuff from PARSE_NAME
004A1Fr 2  E8               inx
004A20r 2  E8               inx
004A21r 2  E8               inx
004A22r 2  E8               inx
004A23r 2               
004A23r 2  60               rts
004A24r 2               .endscope
004A24r 2               
004A24r 2               
004A24r 2               is_printable:
004A24r 2               .scope
004A24r 2               ; """Given a character in A, check if it is a printable ASCII
004A24r 2               ; character in the range from $20 to $7E inclusive. Returns the
004A24r 2               ; result in the Carry Flag: 0 (clear) is not printable, 1 (set)
004A24r 2               ; is printable. Keeps A. See
004A24r 2               ; http://www.obelisk.me.uk/6502/algorithms.html for a
004A24r 2               ; discussion of various ways to do this
004A24r 2  C9 20            cmp #AscSP              ; $20
004A26r 2  90 08            bcc _done
004A28r 2  C9 7F            cmp #'~' + 1             ; $7E
004A2Ar 2  B0 03            bcs _failed
004A2Cr 2               
004A2Cr 2  38               sec
004A2Dr 2  80 01            bra _done
004A2Fr 2               _failed:
004A2Fr 2  18               clc
004A30r 2               _done:
004A30r 2  60               rts
004A31r 2               .endscope
004A31r 2               
004A31r 2               
004A31r 2               is_whitespace:
004A31r 2               .scope
004A31r 2               ; """Given a character in A, check if it is a whitespace
004A31r 2               ; character, that is, an ASCII value from 0 to 32 (where
004A31r 2               ; 32 is SPACE). Returns the result in the Carry Flag:
004A31r 2               ; 0 (clear) is no, it isn't whitespace, while 1 (set) means
004A31r 2               ; that it is whitespace. See PARSE and PARSE-NAME for
004A31r 2               ; a discussion of the uses. Does not change A or Y.
004A31r 2  C9 00            cmp #00         ; explicit comparison to leave Y untouched
004A33r 2  90 08            bcc _done
004A35r 2               
004A35r 2  C9 21            cmp #AscSP+1
004A37r 2  B0 03            bcs _failed
004A39r 2               
004A39r 2  38               sec
004A3Ar 2  80 01            bra _done
004A3Cr 2               _failed:
004A3Cr 2  18               clc
004A3Dr 2               _done:
004A3Dr 2  60               rts
004A3Er 2               .endscope
004A3Er 2               
004A3Er 2               
004A3Er 2               ; Underflow tests. We jump to the label with the number of cells (not: bytes)
004A3Er 2               ; required for the word. This routine flows into the generic error handling
004A3Er 2               ; code
004A3Er 2               underflow_1:
004A3Er 2               ; """Make sure we have at least one cell on the Data Stack"""
004A3Er 2  E0 rr            cpx #dsp0-1
004A40r 2  10 10            bpl underflow_error
004A42r 2  60               rts
004A43r 2               underflow_2:
004A43r 2               ; """Make sure we have at least two cells on the Data Stack"""
004A43r 2  E0 rr            cpx #dsp0-3
004A45r 2  10 0B            bpl underflow_error
004A47r 2  60               rts
004A48r 2               underflow_3:
004A48r 2               ; """Make sure we have at least three cells on the Data Stack"""
004A48r 2  E0 rr            cpx #dsp0-5
004A4Ar 2  10 06            bpl underflow_error
004A4Cr 2  60               rts
004A4Dr 2               underflow_4:
004A4Dr 2               ; """Make sure we have at least four cells on the Data Stack"""
004A4Dr 2  E0 rr            cpx #dsp0-7
004A4Fr 2  10 01            bpl underflow_error
004A51r 2  60               rts
004A52r 2               
004A52r 2               underflow_error:
004A52r 2                   ; Entry for COLD/ABORT/QUIT
004A52r 2  A9 09            lda #err_underflow      ; fall through to error
004A54r 2               
004A54r 2               error:
004A54r 2               ; """Given the error number in a, print the associated error string and
004A54r 2               ; call abort. Uses tmp3.
004A54r 2               ; """
004A54r 2  0A               asl
004A55r 2  A8               tay
004A56r 2  B9 rr rr         lda error_table,y
004A59r 2  85 rr            sta tmp3                ; LSB
004A5Br 2  C8               iny
004A5Cr 2  B9 rr rr         lda error_table,y
004A5Fr 2  85 rr            sta tmp3+1              ; MSB
004A61r 2               
004A61r 2  20 rr rr         jsr print_common
004A64r 2  20 rr rr         jsr xt_cr
004A67r 2  4C rr rr         jmp xt_abort            ; no jsr, as we clobber return stack
004A6Ar 2               
004A6Ar 2               
004A6Ar 2               ; =====================================================================
004A6Ar 2               ; PRINTING ROUTINES
004A6Ar 2               
004A6Ar 2               ; We distinguish two types of print calls, both of which take the string number
004A6Ar 2               ; (see strings.asm) in A:
004A6Ar 2               
004A6Ar 2               ;       print_string       - with a line feed
004A6Ar 2               ;       print_string_no_lf - without a line feed
004A6Ar 2               
004A6Ar 2               ; In addition, print_common provides a lower-level alternative for error
004A6Ar 2               ; handling and anything else that provides the address of the
004A6Ar 2               ; zero-terminated string directly in tmp3. All of those routines assume that
004A6Ar 2               ; printing should be more concerned with size than speed, because anything to
004A6Ar 2               ; do with humans reading text is going to be slow.
004A6Ar 2               
004A6Ar 2               print_string_no_lf:
004A6Ar 2               ; """Given the number of a zero-terminated string in A, print it to the
004A6Ar 2               ; current output without adding a LF. Uses Y and tmp3 by falling
004A6Ar 2               ; through to print_common
004A6Ar 2               ; """
004A6Ar 2                   ; Get the entry from the string table
004A6Ar 2  0A               asl
004A6Br 2  A8               tay
004A6Cr 2  B9 rr rr         lda string_table,y
004A6Fr 2  85 rr            sta tmp3                ; LSB
004A71r 2  C8               iny
004A72r 2  B9 rr rr         lda string_table,y
004A75r 2  85 rr            sta tmp3+1              ; MSB
004A77r 2               
004A77r 2                   ; fall through to print_common
004A77r 2               print_common:
004A77r 2               ; """Common print routine used by both the print functions and
004A77r 2               ; the error printing routine. Assumes string address is in tmp3. Uses
004A77r 2               ; Y.
004A77r 2               ; """
004A77r 2               .scope
004A77r 2  A0 00            ldy #0
004A79r 2               _loop:
004A79r 2  B1 rr            lda (tmp3),y
004A7Br 2  F0 06            beq _done               ; strings are zero-terminated
004A7Dr 2               
004A7Dr 2  20 rr rr         jsr emit_a              ; allows vectoring via output
004A80r 2  C8               iny
004A81r 2  80 F6            bra _loop
004A83r 2               _done:
004A83r 2  60               rts
004A84r 2               .endscope
004A84r 2               
004A84r 2               print_string:
004A84r 2               ; """Print a zero-terminated string to the console/screen, adding a LF.
004A84r 2               ; We do not check to see if the index is out of range. Uses tmp3.
004A84r 2               ; """
004A84r 2  20 rr rr         jsr print_string_no_lf
004A87r 2  4C rr rr         jmp xt_cr               ; JSR/RTS because never compiled
004A8Ar 2               
004A8Ar 2               
004A8Ar 2               print_u:
004A8Ar 2               ; """basic printing routine used by higher-level constructs,
004A8Ar 2               ; the equivalent of the forth word  0 <# #s #> type  which is
004A8Ar 2               ; basically u. without the space at the end. used for various
004A8Ar 2               ; outputs
004A8Ar 2               ; """
004A8Ar 2  20 rr rr         jsr xt_zero                     ; 0
004A8Dr 2  20 rr rr         jsr xt_less_number_sign         ; <#
004A90r 2  20 rr rr         jsr xt_number_sign_s            ; #S
004A93r 2  20 rr rr         jsr xt_number_sign_greater      ; #>
004A96r 2  4C rr rr         jmp xt_type                     ; JSR/RTS because never compiled
004A99r 2               
004A99r 2               ; END
004A99r 2               
004A99r 1               ; .include "../../ed.s"
004A99r 1               
004A99r 1               .segment "DATA"
004A99r 1               
004A99r 1               platform_bye:
004A99r 1               kernel_init:
004A99r 1               v_nmi:
004A99r 1  A9 FF            lda #$FF
004A9Br 1  8D 82 FF         sta DDRB
004A9Er 1  8D 83 FF         sta DDRA
004AA1r 1  9C 81 FF         stz PORTA
004AA4r 1  9C 80 FF         stz PORTB
004AA7r 1               .ifdef video_init
004AA7r 1                   jsr video_init
004AA7r 1               .endif
004AA7r 1               .ifdef ps2_init
004AA7r 1  20 rr rr         jsr ps2_init
004AAAr 1               .endif
004AAAr 1               
004AAAr 1               .ifdef timer_init
004AAAr 1  20 rr rr         jsr timer_init
004AADr 1               .endif
004AADr 1  20 rr rr         jsr acia_init
004AB0r 1               .ifdef lcd_init
004AB0r 1                   jsr lcd_init
004AB0r 1               .endif
004AB0r 1               .ifdef spi_init
004AB0r 1                   jsr spi_init
004AB0r 1               .endif
004AB0r 1               .ifdef kb_init
004AB0r 1                   jsr kb_init
004AB0r 1               .endif
004AB0r 1               
004AB0r 1               
004AB0r 1  DA A2 00 BD      printascii welcome_message
004AB4r 1  rr rr F0 06  
004AB8r 1  20 rr rr E8  
004ABFr 1               
004ABFr 1               
004ABFr 1  4C rr rr         jmp forth
004AC2r 1               
004AC2r 1               
004AC2r 1               kernel_putc:
004AC2r 1                   ; """Print a single character to the console. """
004AC2r 1                   ;; Send_Char - send character in A out serial port.
004AC2r 1                   ;; Uses: A (original value restored)
004AC2r 1               send_char:
004AC2r 1  48               pha
004AC3r 1                   .ifdef char_out
004AC3r 1                   jsr char_out
004AC3r 1                   .endif
004AC3r 1                   .ifdef acia_out
004AC3r 1  20 rr rr         jsr acia_out
004AC6r 1                   .endif
004AC6r 1               send_char_exit:
004AC6r 1               .ifdef lcd_print
004AC6r 1                   ; jsr lcd_print
004AC6r 1               .endif
004AC6r 1  68               pla
004AC7r 1  60               rts
004AC8r 1               
004AC8r 1               
004AC8r 1                       ;; Get_Char - get a character from the serial port into A.
004AC8r 1                       ;; Set the carry flag if char is valid.
004AC8r 1                       ;; Return immediately with carry flag clear if no char available.
004AC8r 1                       ;; Uses: A (return value)
004AC8r 1               
004AC8r 1               Get_Char:
004AC8r 1  20 rr rr         jsr acia_getc
004ACBr 1  90 05            bcc get_ps2_char                ; check keyboard buffer if nothing from ACIA
004ACDr 1  20 rr rr         jsr check_ctrl_c
004AD0r 1  38               sec                             ; Set Carry to show we got a character
004AD1r 1  60               rts                             ; Return
004AD2r 1               
004AD2r 1               get_ps2_char:                       ; no ACIA char available, try to get from KB buffer
004AD2r 1               .ifdef ps2_get_char
004AD2r 1  20 rr rr         jsr ps2_get_char
004AD5r 1               .endif
004AD5r 1  90 02            bcc get_kb_char
004AD7r 1  38               sec
004AD8r 1               
004AD8r 1  60               rts
004AD9r 1               get_kb_char:
004AD9r 1                   .ifdef kb_get_char
004AD9r 1               
004AD9r 1                   ; ldy #5
004AD9r 1                   ; jsr delay_short
004AD9r 1                   ; ply
004AD9r 1                       jsr kb_get_char
004AD9r 1               
004AD9r 1                   .endif
004AD9r 1               exit:                         ; Indicate no char available.
004AD9r 1  60               rts                             ; return
004ADAr 1               
004ADAr 1               kernel_getc:
004ADAr 1                   ; """Get a single character from the keyboard (waits for key).
004ADAr 1                   ; """
004ADAr 1                   ;; Get_Char_Wait - same as Get_Char only blocking.
004ADAr 1                   ;; Uses: A (return value)
004ADAr 1               Get_Char_Wait:
004ADAr 1  20 rr rr         jsr Get_Char
004ADDr 1  90 FB            bcc Get_Char_Wait
004ADFr 1  60               rts
004AE0r 1               
004AE0r 1               check_ctrl_c:
004AE0r 1                   ;; Check if we have ctrl-C character, if so jump to nmi
004AE0r 1  C9 03            cmp #$03
004AE2r 1  D0 12            bne exit_ctrl_c
004AE4r 1  DA A2 00 BD      printascii abort_message
004AE8r 1  rr rr F0 06  
004AECr 1  20 rr rr E8  
004AF3r 1  4C rr rr         jmp xt_abort
004AF6r 1               
004AF6r 1               exit_ctrl_c:
004AF6r 1  60               rts
004AF7r 1               
004AF7r 1               
004AF7r 1               v_irq:                          ; IRQ handler
004AF7r 1  48                   pha
004AF8r 1  5A                   phy
004AF9r 1                       ; check if bit 7 of IFR is set
004AF9r 1  AD 8D FF             lda IFR
004AFCr 1  10 0B                bpl v_kb_irq  ; Interrupt not from VIA, exit
004AFEr 1               
004AFEr 1  29 08                and #$08        ; ps2 has priority
004B00r 1  D0 12                bne v_irq_ps2
004B02r 1  AD 8D FF             lda IFR
004B05r 1  29 40                and #$40
004B07r 1  D0 20                bne v_irq_timer
004B09r 1               v_kb_irq:
004B09r 1  AD 9D FF             lda KB_IFR
004B0Cr 1  10 26                bpl v_irq_exit
004B0Er 1  29 40                and #$40
004B10r 1  D0 22                bne v_kb_irq_timer
004B12r 1  80 20                bra v_irq_exit
004B14r 1               
004B14r 1               
004B14r 1               v_irq_ps2:
004B14r 1                   .ifdef ps2_irq
004B14r 1  A5 rr                lda time
004B16r 1  85 rr                sta last_ps2_time
004B18r 1  A5 rr                lda time+1
004B1Ar 1  85 rr                sta last_ps2_time+1
004B1Cr 1  A5 rr                lda time+2
004B1Er 1  85 rr                sta last_ps2_time+2
004B20r 1  A5 rr                lda time+3
004B22r 1  85 rr                sta last_ps2_time+3
004B24r 1                       ; this delay is here to ensure we prevent desynchronization
004B24r 1                       ;ldy #$04         ; correct delay seems to be #$20 at 10Mhz
004B24r 1                       ; jsr delay_short
004B24r 1               
004B24r 1               
004B24r 1  20 rr rr             jsr ps2_irq
004B27r 1               
004B27r 1                       ; ldy #$04         ; correct delay seems to be #$20 at 10Mhz
004B27r 1                       ; jsr delay_short
004B27r 1                   .endif
004B27r 1  80 0B                bra v_irq_exit
004B29r 1               
004B29r 1               v_irq_timer:
004B29r 1  AD 84 FF             lda T1CL
004B2Cr 1                       ; clear timer interrupt
004B2Cr 1                   .ifdef timer_irq
004B2Cr 1  20 rr rr             jsr timer_irq
004B2Fr 1                   .endif
004B2Fr 1  20 rr rr             jsr Get_Char ; Check if a char is waiting to be able to break on CTRL-C
004B32r 1                       ; check if there is a char waiting to be printed to the lcd
004B32r 1                       ; lda lcd_char
004B32r 1                       ; beq v_exit
004B32r 1                       ; jsr lcd_print
004B32r 1                       ; stz lcd_char
004B32r 1               
004B32r 1               
004B32r 1  80 00                bra v_irq_exit
004B34r 1               v_kb_irq_timer:
004B34r 1               .ifdef kb_time
004B34r 1                   lda KB_T1CL ; clear timer interrupt
004B34r 1                   inc kb_time
004B34r 1                   bne v_irq_exit
004B34r 1               .endif
004B34r 1                   ;jsr kb_scan
004B34r 1               v_irq_exit:
004B34r 1  7A               ply
004B35r 1  68               pla
004B36r 1  40               rti
004B37r 1

004B3Br 1  xx xx xx xx  
004B3Fr 1  xx xx xx xx  
004C00r 1  xx xx xx xx  FAT_BUFFER: .res $200
004C04r 1  xx xx xx xx  
004C08r 1  xx xx xx xx
